كتاب الحج باب الجنايات
يدها أو كفها فعليها دم إن كان كثيراً فاحشاً، وإن كان قليلاً فعليها صدقة كما ذكره الأسبيجابي وغيره بخلاف خضاب الرأس بالحناء فإنه موجب للدم مطلقاً. وأما خضاب اللحية فوقع في الهداية أن كلاً من الرأس واللحية مضمون ولم يقل بالدم، وزاد الشارح أن كلا منهما مضمون بالدم وهو سهو منه لأن اللحية مضمونة بالصدقة كما في معراج الدراية معزياً للمبسوط، وقيد بالحناء لأنه لو خضب بالوسمة فليس عليه دم ولكن إن خاف أن يقتل الهوام أطعم شيئاً لأن فيه معنى الجناية من هذا الوجه ولكنه غير متكامل فيلزمه الصدقة كما في المبسوط والوسمة - بسكون السين وكسرها وهو الأفصح - شجر يخضب بورقه. وفي الهداية : وعن أبي يوسف إذا خضب رأسه بالوسمة لأجل المعالجة من الصداع فعليه الجزاء باعتبار أنه يغلف رأسه وهذا صحيح .اهـ. يعني ينبغي أن لا يكون فيه خلاف لأن التغطية موجبة بالاتفاق غير أنها للعلاج فلهذا ذكر الجزاء ولم يذكر الدم. والحناء منون في عبارة المصنف لأنه فعال لا فعلاء ليمنع فه ألف التأنيث . صر
وقوله : «أو ادهن بزيت معطوف على قوله «طيب» أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان مطبوخاً أو غير مطبوخ مطيباً أو غير مطيب، ولم يقيده بالكثير لما علم من تقييده في الطيب لأنه إذا فرق في الطيب بين العضو وما دونه فالزيت أولى لأنه لا خلاف في الطيب، وفي الزيت الذي ليس بمطيب ولا مطبوخ خلافهما فقالا : يجب فيه صدقة لأن الجناية فيه قاصرة لأنه من الأطعمة إلا أن فيه ارتفاقاً لمعنى قتل الهوام وإزالة الشعث وقال الإمام: يجب دم لأنه أصل هذا الرأس واليد فقال : وكذا لو خضبت يدها بها ولم يقيده بقلة ولا كثرة وما في الأسبيجابي مبني على اعتبار الكثرة في نفس الطيب ولا تنس ذلك التوفيق قوله : (وهو سهو منه) قال في النهر : هو الساهي وذلك أن صاحب المعراج إنما نقل هذا عن المبسوط فيما لو اختضب بالوسمة فقال ما لفظه : ذكر في المبسوط خضب رأسه بالوسمة فعليه . للخضاب بل لتغطية الرأس. هذا هو الصحيح فإن لحيته فليس عليه دم ولكن إن خاف من قتل الدواب أعطى شيئاً لأن فيه معنى الجناية من الوجه لكونه غير متكامل فيلزمه الدم والصدقة منهما أي من خضاب الرأس فإنه مضمون بالدم، وخضاب اللحية فإنه مضمون بالصدقة كما ذكر في المبسوط اهـ. وكيف يكون ما في الجامع دليلاً على أن كلاً منهما مضمون على ما توهم ولا اشتراك بينهما إذ وجوب الدم يغاير وجوب الصدقة ويلزمه إيجاب الصدقة أيضاً فيما لو دهنها بالخطمي وقد جزموا فيه بوجوب الدم عنده ا هـ. وقال في الشرنبلالية قلت : والمراد بالصدقة هنا غير المصطلح عليها بتقديرها بنصف صاع بل أعم لقوله في المعراج «أعطي شيئاً فإطلاق صاحب البحر فيه ما فيه من هذا القبيل أيضاً قوله : (باعتبار أنه يغلف رأسه) أي يغطيه. وقوله وهذا أي تأويل أبي يوسف بالتغليف لأن تغطية الرأس توجب الجزاء .

كتاب الحج باب 9 الطيب باعتبار أنه يلقى فيه الأنوار كالورد والبنفسج فيصير نفسه طيباً ولا يخلو عن نوع طيب ويقتل الهوام ويلين الشعر ويزيل التفث والشعث. وأراد بالزيت دهن الزيتون والسمسم وهو المسمى بالشيرج فخرج بقية الأدهان كالشحم والسمن وقيد بالأدهان لأنه لو أكله أو داوى به شقوق رجليه أو أقطر في أذنه لا يجب دم ولا صدقة بخلاف المسك والعنبر والغالية والكافور ونحوها حيث يلزم الجزاء بالاستعمال على وجه التداوي لكنه يتخير إذا كان لعذر كما سيأتي، وكذا إذا أكل الكثير من الطيب وهو ما يلتزق بأكثر فمه فعليه الدم. قال في فتح القدير : وهذه تشهد لعدم اعتبار العضو مطلقاً في لزوم الدم بل ذاك إذا لم يبلغ مبلغ الكثرة في نفسه على ما قدمناه وقد قدمنا عن قاضيخان أنه لو خلط الطيب بطعام من غير طبخ فالعبرة للغالب، فإن كان الطيب مغلوباً فلا شيء أصلاً، زاد بعضهم إلا أنه يكره إذا كان رائحته توجد فيه، وإن كان غالباً فهو كالخالص، وهكذا في المحيط وغيره. وقالوا: ولو خلطه بمشروب وهو غالب ففيه الدم، وإن كان مغلوباً فصدقة إلا أن يشرب مراراً فدم، فإن كان للتداوي خير. وينبغي أن يسوي بين المأكول والمشروب المخلوط كل منهما بطيب مغلوب، إما بعدم شيء أصلاً كما هو الحكم في المأكول أو بوجوب الصدقة فيهما كما الحكم في المشروب وما فرق به في المحيط من أن الطيب مما يقصد شربه فإذا خلطه بمشروب لم يصر تبعاً لمشروب وما فرق به في المحيط من أن الطيب مما يقصد شربه فإذا خلط بمشروب لم يصر تبعاً لمشروب مثله إلا أن يكون المشروب غالباً كما لو خلط اللبن بالماء فشربه الصبي تثبت حرمة الرضاع إلا أن يكون الماء غالباً بخلاف أكله فإنه ليس مما يقصد عادة، فإذا خلط بالطعام صار تبعاً للطعام وسقط حكمه، ففيه نظر من وجهين: الأول أن من الطيب ما يقصد أكلاً إذا كان من المأكولات للمعنى القائم به وهو الطيبية إما مداواة أو تنعماً منفرداً أو مخلوطاً كما يقصد شرباً. الثاني أن القصد من هذا الباب ليس بشرط لأن هو
قوله : (لكنه يتخير إذا كان لعذر) أي يتخير بين الدم والصوم والإطعام قوله : (وكذا إذا أكل الكثير من الطيب الخ) وإن كان قليلاً بأن لم يلتصق بأكثر فمه فعليه الصدقة. وهذا كله إذا أكله كما هو أي من غير خلط أو طبخ ، أما إذا خلطه بطعام قد طبخ كالزعفران فلا شيء عليه، سواء مسه النار أو لا، وسواء يوجد ريحه أولا إلا أنه يكره إن وجد ريحه. وإن خلط بما يؤكل بلا طبخ كالزعفران بالملح فالعبرة بالغلبة، فإن كان الغالب الملح فلا شيء عليه غير أنه إن كان رائحته موجودة كره أكله، وإن كان الغالب الطيب ففيه الدم (لباب) قوله : (فهو كالخالص) أي فيجب الجزاء وإن لم تظهر رائحته . كذا في الفتح قوله : (وينبغي أن يسوي الخ) أقول : لم يفرق الزيلعي في المخلوط بالمأكول بين الغالب والمغلوب، وظاهر كلامه عدم الفرق بينه وبين المشروب فإنه قال : لو أكل زعفراناً مخلوطاً بطعام أو طيب آخر ولم تمسه النار يلزمه دم، وإن مسته فلا شيء عليه. وعلى هذا التفصيل في المشروب ا هـ . وهو ظاهر ما يأتي عن الحلبي أيضاً
Book of Hajj, Chapter of Offenses: If she dyes her hand or palm, then she owes dam if it is excessive much, and if it is little then she owes sadaqah as mentioned by al-Usbjabi and others, contrary to dyeing the head with henna for it necessitates dam absolutely. As for dyeing the beard, it occurs in al-Hidayah that both head and beard are guaranteed [by penalty] and he did not say dam, and the commentator added that both are guaranteed by dam, but that is an oversight from him because the beard is guaranteed by sadaqah as in Miraj al-Dirayah quoting al-Mabsut. It is restricted to henna because if he dyed with wasma then there is no dam on him but if he fears killing insects he feeds something because it contains the meaning of offense from this aspect but it is incomplete so sadaqah is necessary as in al-Mabsut. Wasma - with sukun of sin and kasrah which is more eloquent - is a tree whose leaf is used for dyeing. In al-Hidayah: From Abu Yusuf, if he dyed his head with wasma for treatment of headache then he owes jaza' considering that it covers his head, and this is correct. End. Meaning there should be no dispute because covering necessitates [penalty] by agreement except that it is for treatment, so he mentioned jaza' and did not mention dam. Henna is declinable in the author's phrase because it is fi'al not fa'la' to prevent the feminine alif. He said: And his saying: 'or oiled with oil' is coordinated to his saying 'perfume' - he made it absolute including whether cooked or uncooked, perfumed or unperfumed, and he did not restrict it to much because of what is known from his restriction in perfume because if he differentiated in perfume between the limb and less than it, then oil is more appropriate because there is no dispute in perfume, and in oil that is not perfumed nor cooked there is dispute between them: they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: sadaqah is necessary because the offense is deficient because it is from foods except that in it there is benefit for the meaning of killing insects and removing dishevelment, and Imam (Abu Hanifa) said: dam is necessary because it is origin of head and hand. He said: Likewise if she dyed her hand with it and he did not restrict it to little or much. And what is in al-Usbjabi is based on considering abundance in the perfume itself. Do not forget that reconciliation. His saying: (It is an oversight from him). He said in al-Nahr: He is the one overlooking, because the author of Miraj only transmitted this from al-Mabsut concerning dyeing with wasma, and he said verbatim: 'Mentioned in al-Mabsut: He dyed his head with wasma, then ... for dyeing but for covering the head. This is correct. For his beard, then no dam on him but if he fears killing insects he gives something because it contains meaning of offense from the aspect because it is incomplete, so dam and sadaqah are necessary from them' i.e. from dyeing the head it is guaranteed by dam, and dyeing the beard it is guaranteed by sadaqah as mentioned in al-Mabsut. End. How can what is in al-Jami' be evidence that both are guaranteed as he imagined? There is no commonality between them because obligation of dam differs from obligation of sadaqah, and it would require obligation of sadaqah also in case of oiling with khutmi (marshmallow) while they ruled for obligation of dam in it. End. He said in al-Shurnabulaliyya: I say: what is meant by sadaqah here is not the technical one measured by half a sa', but more general because of his saying in al-Miraj 'he gives something'; so al-Bahr's absolute statement has something in it from this category also. His saying: (considering that it covers his head) i.e. covers it. His saying: 'And this' i.e. interpretation of Abu Yusuf by covering because covering the head necessitates jaza'. Book of Hajj, Chapter: 9 Perfume: Because it (oil) receives floral essences like rose and violet, becoming itself perfumed and not free from a type of perfume, and it kills insects and softens hair and removes dirt and dishevelment. He meant by oil: olive oil and sesame oil which is called shiraj. So the rest of oils like animal fat and ghee are excluded. It is restricted to oils because if he eats it or treats cracks of his feet with it or puts drops in his ear, no dam or sadaqah is necessary, contrary to musk, ambergris, ghaliyah, camphor and the like where penalty is necessary by use for treatment, but he chooses if there is an excuse as will come. Likewise if he eats much perfume, which is what sticks to most of his mouth, then dam is on him. He said in Fath al-Qadir: This testifies to not considering the limb absolutely in obligation of dam, but that is when it does not reach the level of plenty in itself as we have presented. We have presented from Qadikhan that if he mixes perfume with food without cooking, the criterion is the predominant (ghalaba). If the perfume is overcome, then nothing at all; some added that it is disliked if its smell is found in it; and if it is predominant, then it is like pure. Thus in al-Muhit and others. They said: If he mixes it with a drink and it is predominant, then in it is dam; if it is overcome, then sadaqah unless he drinks repeatedly, then dam. If it is for treatment, he chooses. It should be equalized between food and drink mixed each with overcome perfume: either with nothing at all as is the ruling in food, or with obligation of sadaqah in both as is the ruling in drink. What al-Muhit differentiated by that perfume is intended for drinking, so when mixed with a drink it does not become a follower of the drink... except if the drink is predominant, like mixing milk with water and a child drinks it; the prohibition of breastfeeding is established unless water is predominant. Contrary to eating it, for it is not usually intended. So if mixed with food it becomes a follower of food and its ruling falls. This is objectionable in two ways: first, that some perfume is intended for eating if it is from edibles for the meaning inherent in it which is perfume, either for treatment or enjoyment alone or mixed as it is intended for drinking. Second, that intent in this chapter is not a condition because... His saying: (but he chooses if there is an excuse) i.e. chooses between dam, fasting, and feeding. His saying: (Likewise if he eats much perfume etc.) And if little, such that it does not stick to most of his mouth, then sadaqah is on him. This all when he eats it as is, i.e. without mixing or cooking. But if he mixes it with cooked food like saffron, then nothing on him, whether fire touched it or not, whether its smell is found or not, except that it is disliked if its smell is found. And if mixed with what is eaten without cooking like saffron with salt, the criterion is predominance. If salt is predominant, then nothing on him except that if its smell is present, eating it is disliked. If perfume is predominant, then in it is dam (from Lubab). His saying: (so it is like pure) i.e. penalty is obligatory even if its smell does not appear. Thus in al-Fath. His saying: (It should be equalized etc.) I say: al-Zayla'i did not differentiate in mixing with food between predominant and overcome, and his apparent words do not differentiate from drink; he said: If he eats saffron mixed with food or other perfume and fire did not touch it, dam is necessary; if fire touched it, nothing on him. And this detail applies to drink. End. And it is apparent from what al-Halabi also says.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion probe on the chapter of offenses (jinayat) during Hajj, specifically concerning the application of dyes, oils, and perfumes. The author first discusses dyeing (khidab) with henna and wasma, distinguishing between women dyeing hands/feet (dam if excessive, sadaqah if little) and dyeing the head with henna (always dam). For the beard, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: the Hidayah states both head and beard are 'guaranteed' but does not specify dam, while some commentators mistakenly assert dam for both. The correct view, from al-Mabsut via Miraj al-Dirayah, is that the beard incurs sadaqah, not dam, because its offense is less complete. Dyeing with wasma (a plant) incurs nothing unless there is fear of insects, then sadaqah, due to the partial offense. Abu Yusuf's approach regarding medicinal use (for headache) treats it as head covering, necessitating jaza' (penalty), which is agreed upon. The passage then addresses oiling (idhan) with oils like olive and sesame. The ruling differentiates between perfumed and unperfumed oil; for unperfumed oil, Imam Abu Hanifa mandates dam (because it is the basis for head and hand), while the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) mandate sadaqah (because it is essentially food, though beneficial for killing insects). The author reconciles by noting that the criterion is the oil's quantity in relation to perfume. Finally, the passage discusses mixing perfume with food or drink, emphasizing the principle of ghalabah (predominance). If perfume is predominant, the penalty is dam; if overcome, sadaqah or nothing if food is cooked. There is debate on equalizing food and drink rulings, with some scholars like al-Zayla'i treating them similarly. Throughout, the commentary emphasizes that these rulings are based on the nature of the act (whether it is direct perfume use or incidental), with istihsan playing a role in mitigating penalties for medicinal or necessary uses.

Key Terms
خضاب (khidāb): Dyeing or coloring hair or skin with substances like henna
دم (dam): Blood sacrifice (usually a sheep) as penalty for major offenses in ihram
صدقة (ṣadaqah): Charity of food (not necessarily half a sa') as a lesser penalty
وسمة (wasma): A plant used for dyeing, unscented

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what penalty is due for a male pilgrim who dyes his beard with henna during ihram?
A) Dam (slaughter a sheep)
B) Sadaqah (charity)
C) Fasting three days
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
The beard is treated leniently in ihram dyeing: sadaqah suffices, not dam.

Oiling and Perfume Mixtures in Ihram
Explaining penalties for oiling and mixing perfumes during Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate between the Hanafi rulings for applying unperfumed oil during ihram and determine the penalty when perfume is mixed with food or drink using the principle of ghalabah.

Core Idea
Unperfumed oil incurs dam according to Abu Hanifa (mufta bihi) but sadaqah according to the Sahibayn; mixed substances are judged by the predominant element (ghalabah).

Applying oil during ihram is prohibited if it is perfumed, but there is a dispute over unperfumed oil. Additionally, when perfume is mixed with food or drink, the penalty depends on which substance predominates. This lesson clarifies these rulings and the underlying qiyas reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Type of Oil
Determine whether the oil is perfumed or unperfumed, cooked or raw. Perfumed oil is treated as perfume and incurs a penalty.
The text focuses on unperfumed, uncooked oil.
2
Note the Ikhtilaf on Unperfumed Oil
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that unperfumed oil requires dam because it is the 'origin' for head and hand and has benefits like killing insects. The Sahibayn say sadaqah because it is essentially food.
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view: dam.
3
Understand the Reasoning (Qiyas Khafi)
The ruling is based on qiyas: oil is compared to perfume because it beautifies and removes dirt, but it also has nutritional aspects. Abu Hanifa prioritizes the former, the Sahibayn the latter.
This is a classic example of qiyas khafi (hidden analogy).
4
Learn the Principle of Ghalabah for Mixtures
When perfume is mixed with food or drink, the penalty is determined by whichever substance is predominant (ghalabah). If perfume predominates, dam; if overcome, sadaqah or nothing (if cooked).
The criterion is the effect and intention, but if cooked, the perfume is considered overcome.
5
Apply to Cases of Eating/Drinking Mixed Substances
If a pilgrim eats or drinks a mixture where the perfume is overcome, no penalty or sadaqah; if predominant, dam. Repeated drinking even if overcome may trigger dam.
There is a dispute on whether food and drink are treated identically; al-Zayla'i equates them.

يدها أو كفها فعليها دم إن كان كثيراً فاحشاً، وإن كان قليلاً فعليها صدقة كما ذكره الأسبيجابي وغيره بخلاف خضاب الرأس بالحناء فإنه موجب للدم مطلقاً. وأما خضاب اللحية فوقع في الهداية أن كلاً من الرأس واللحية مضمون ولم يقل بالدم، وزاد الشارح أن كلا منهما مضمون بالدم وهو سهو منه لأن اللحية مضمونة بالصدقة كما في معراج الدراية معزياً للمبسوط، وقيد بالحناء لأنه لو خضب بالوسمة فليس عليه دم ولكن إن خاف أن يقتل الهوام أطعم شيئاً لأن فيه معنى الجناية من هذا الوجه ولكنه غير متكامل فيلزمه الصدقة كما في المبسوط والوسمة - بسكون السين وكسرها وهو الأفصح - شجر يخضب بورقه. وفي الهداية : وعن أبي يوسف إذا خضب رأسه بالوسمة لأجل المعالجة من الصداع فعليه الجزاء باعتبار أنه يغلف رأسه وهذا صحيح .اهـ. يعني ينبغي أن لا يكون فيه خلاف لأن التغطية موجبة بالاتفاق غير أنها للعلاج فلهذا ذكر الجزاء ولم يذكر الدم. والحناء منون في عبارة المصنف لأنه فعال لا فعلاء ليمنع فه ألف التأنيث . صر
وقوله : «أو ادهن بزيت معطوف على قوله «طيب» أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان مطبوخاً أو غير مطبوخ مطيباً أو غير مطيب، ولم يقيده بالكثير لما علم من تقييده في الطيب لأنه إذا فرق في الطيب بين العضو وما دونه فالزيت أولى لأنه لا خلاف في الطيب، وفي الزيت الذي ليس بمطيب ولا مطبوخ خلافهما فقالا : يجب فيه صدقة لأن الجناية فيه قاصرة لأنه من الأطعمة إلا أن فيه ارتفاقاً لمعنى قتل الهوام وإزالة الشعث وقال الإمام: يجب دم لأنه أصل هذا الرأس واليد فقال : وكذا لو خضبت يدها بها ولم يقيده بقلة ولا كثرة وما في الأسبيجابي مبني على اعتبار الكثرة في نفس الطيب ولا تنس ذلك التوفيق قوله : (وهو سهو منه) قال في النهر : هو الساهي وذلك أن صاحب المعراج إنما نقل هذا عن المبسوط فيما لو اختضب بالوسمة فقال ما لفظه : ذكر في المبسوط خضب رأسه بالوسمة فعليه . للخضاب بل لتغطية الرأس. هذا هو الصحيح فإن لحيته فليس عليه دم ولكن إن خاف من قتل الدواب أعطى شيئاً لأن فيه معنى الجناية من الوجه لكونه غير متكامل فيلزمه الدم والصدقة منهما أي من خضاب الرأس فإنه مضمون بالدم، وخضاب اللحية فإنه مضمون بالصدقة كما ذكر في المبسوط اهـ. وكيف يكون ما في الجامع دليلاً على أن كلاً منهما مضمون على ما توهم ولا اشتراك بينهما إذ وجوب الدم يغاير وجوب الصدقة ويلزمه إيجاب الصدقة أيضاً فيما لو دهنها بالخطمي وقد جزموا فيه بوجوب الدم عنده ا هـ. وقال في الشرنبلالية قلت : والمراد بالصدقة هنا غير المصطلح عليها بتقديرها بنصف صاع بل أعم لقوله في المعراج «أعطي شيئاً فإطلاق صاحب البحر فيه ما فيه من هذا القبيل أيضاً قوله : (باعتبار أنه يغلف رأسه) أي يغطيه. وقوله وهذا أي تأويل أبي يوسف بالتغليف لأن تغطية الرأس توجب الجزاء .

كتاب الحج باب 9 الطيب باعتبار أنه يلقى فيه الأنوار كالورد والبنفسج فيصير نفسه طيباً ولا يخلو عن نوع طيب ويقتل الهوام ويلين الشعر ويزيل التفث والشعث. وأراد بالزيت دهن الزيتون والسمسم وهو المسمى بالشيرج فخرج بقية الأدهان كالشحم والسمن وقيد بالأدهان لأنه لو أكله أو داوى به شقوق رجليه أو أقطر في أذنه لا يجب دم ولا صدقة بخلاف المسك والعنبر والغالية والكافور ونحوها حيث يلزم الجزاء بالاستعمال على وجه التداوي لكنه يتخير إذا كان لعذر كما سيأتي، وكذا إذا أكل الكثير من الطيب وهو ما يلتزق بأكثر فمه فعليه الدم. قال في فتح القدير : وهذه تشهد لعدم اعتبار العضو مطلقاً في لزوم الدم بل ذاك إذا لم يبلغ مبلغ الكثرة في نفسه على ما قدمناه وقد قدمنا عن قاضيخان أنه لو خلط الطيب بطعام من غير طبخ فالعبرة للغالب، فإن كان الطيب مغلوباً فلا شيء أصلاً، زاد بعضهم إلا أنه يكره إذا كان رائحته توجد فيه، وإن كان غالباً فهو كالخالص، وهكذا في المحيط وغيره. وقالوا: ولو خلطه بمشروب وهو غالب ففيه الدم، وإن كان مغلوباً فصدقة إلا أن يشرب مراراً فدم، فإن كان للتداوي خير. وينبغي أن يسوي بين المأكول والمشروب المخلوط كل منهما بطيب مغلوب، إما بعدم شيء أصلاً كما هو الحكم في المأكول أو بوجوب الصدقة فيهما كما الحكم في المشروب وما فرق به في المحيط من أن الطيب مما يقصد شربه فإذا خلطه بمشروب لم يصر تبعاً لمشروب وما فرق به في المحيط من أن الطيب مما يقصد شربه فإذا خلط بمشروب لم يصر تبعاً لمشروب مثله إلا أن يكون المشروب غالباً كما لو خلط اللبن بالماء فشربه الصبي تثبت حرمة الرضاع إلا أن يكون الماء غالباً بخلاف أكله فإنه ليس مما يقصد عادة، فإذا خلط بالطعام صار تبعاً للطعام وسقط حكمه، ففيه نظر من وجهين: الأول أن من الطيب ما يقصد أكلاً إذا كان من المأكولات للمعنى القائم به وهو الطيبية إما مداواة أو تنعماً منفرداً أو مخلوطاً كما يقصد شرباً. الثاني أن القصد من هذا الباب ليس بشرط لأن هو
قوله : (لكنه يتخير إذا كان لعذر) أي يتخير بين الدم والصوم والإطعام قوله : (وكذا إذا أكل الكثير من الطيب الخ) وإن كان قليلاً بأن لم يلتصق بأكثر فمه فعليه الصدقة. وهذا كله إذا أكله كما هو أي من غير خلط أو طبخ ، أما إذا خلطه بطعام قد طبخ كالزعفران فلا شيء عليه، سواء مسه النار أو لا، وسواء يوجد ريحه أولا إلا أنه يكره إن وجد ريحه. وإن خلط بما يؤكل بلا طبخ كالزعفران بالملح فالعبرة بالغلبة، فإن كان الغالب الملح فلا شيء عليه غير أنه إن كان رائحته موجودة كره أكله، وإن كان الغالب الطيب ففيه الدم (لباب) قوله : (فهو كالخالص) أي فيجب الجزاء وإن لم تظهر رائحته . كذا في الفتح قوله : (وينبغي أن يسوي الخ) أقول : لم يفرق الزيلعي في المخلوط بالمأكول بين الغالب والمغلوب، وظاهر كلامه عدم الفرق بينه وبين المشروب فإنه قال : لو أكل زعفراناً مخلوطاً بطعام أو طيب آخر ولم تمسه النار يلزمه دم، وإن مسته فلا شيء عليه. وعلى هذا التفصيل في المشروب ا هـ . وهو ظاهر ما يأتي عن الحلبي أيضاً
Book of Hajj, Chapter of Offenses: If she dyes her hand or palm, then she owes dam if it is excessive much, and if it is little then she owes sadaqah as mentioned by al-Usbjabi and others, contrary to dyeing the head with henna for it necessitates dam absolutely. As for dyeing the beard, it occurs in al-Hidayah that both head and beard are guaranteed [by penalty] and he did not say dam, and the commentator added that both are guaranteed by dam, but that is an oversight from him because the beard is guaranteed by sadaqah as in Miraj al-Dirayah quoting al-Mabsut. It is restricted to henna because if he dyed with wasma then there is no dam on him but if he fears killing insects he feeds something because it contains the meaning of offense from this aspect but it is incomplete so sadaqah is necessary as in al-Mabsut. Wasma - with sukun of sin and kasrah which is more eloquent - is a tree whose leaf is used for dyeing. In al-Hidayah: From Abu Yusuf, if he dyed his head with wasma for treatment of headache then he owes jaza' considering that it covers his head, and this is correct. End. Meaning there should be no dispute because covering necessitates [penalty] by agreement except that it is for treatment, so he mentioned jaza' and did not mention dam. Henna is declinable in the author's phrase because it is fi'al not fa'la' to prevent the feminine alif. He said: And his saying: 'or oiled with oil' is coordinated to his saying 'perfume' - he made it absolute including whether cooked or uncooked, perfumed or unperfumed, and he did not restrict it to much because of what is known from his restriction in perfume because if he differentiated in perfume between the limb and less than it, then oil is more appropriate because there is no dispute in perfume, and in oil that is not perfumed nor cooked there is dispute between them: they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: sadaqah is necessary because the offense is deficient because it is from foods except that in it there is benefit for the meaning of killing insects and removing dishevelment, and Imam (Abu Hanifa) said: dam is necessary because it is origin of head and hand. He said: Likewise if she dyed her hand with it and he did not restrict it to little or much. And what is in al-Usbjabi is based on considering abundance in the perfume itself. Do not forget that reconciliation. His saying: (It is an oversight from him). He said in al-Nahr: He is the one overlooking, because the author of Miraj only transmitted this from al-Mabsut concerning dyeing with wasma, and he said verbatim: 'Mentioned in al-Mabsut: He dyed his head with wasma, then ... for dyeing but for covering the head. This is correct. For his beard, then no dam on him but if he fears killing insects he gives something because it contains meaning of offense from the aspect because it is incomplete, so dam and sadaqah are necessary from them' i.e. from dyeing the head it is guaranteed by dam, and dyeing the beard it is guaranteed by sadaqah as mentioned in al-Mabsut. End. How can what is in al-Jami' be evidence that both are guaranteed as he imagined? There is no commonality between them because obligation of dam differs from obligation of sadaqah, and it would require obligation of sadaqah also in case of oiling with khutmi (marshmallow) while they ruled for obligation of dam in it. End. He said in al-Shurnabulaliyya: I say: what is meant by sadaqah here is not the technical one measured by half a sa', but more general because of his saying in al-Miraj 'he gives something'; so al-Bahr's absolute statement has something in it from this category also. His saying: (considering that it covers his head) i.e. covers it. His saying: 'And this' i.e. interpretation of Abu Yusuf by covering because covering the head necessitates jaza'. Book of Hajj, Chapter: 9 Perfume: Because it (oil) receives floral essences like rose and violet, becoming itself perfumed and not free from a type of perfume, and it kills insects and softens hair and removes dirt and dishevelment. He meant by oil: olive oil and sesame oil which is called shiraj. So the rest of oils like animal fat and ghee are excluded. It is restricted to oils because if he eats it or treats cracks of his feet with it or puts drops in his ear, no dam or sadaqah is necessary, contrary to musk, ambergris, ghaliyah, camphor and the like where penalty is necessary by use for treatment, but he chooses if there is an excuse as will come. Likewise if he eats much perfume, which is what sticks to most of his mouth, then dam is on him. He said in Fath al-Qadir: This testifies to not considering the limb absolutely in obligation of dam, but that is when it does not reach the level of plenty in itself as we have presented. We have presented from Qadikhan that if he mixes perfume with food without cooking, the criterion is the predominant (ghalaba). If the perfume is overcome, then nothing at all; some added that it is disliked if its smell is found in it; and if it is predominant, then it is like pure. Thus in al-Muhit and others. They said: If he mixes it with a drink and it is predominant, then in it is dam; if it is overcome, then sadaqah unless he drinks repeatedly, then dam. If it is for treatment, he chooses. It should be equalized between food and drink mixed each with overcome perfume: either with nothing at all as is the ruling in food, or with obligation of sadaqah in both as is the ruling in drink. What al-Muhit differentiated by that perfume is intended for drinking, so when mixed with a drink it does not become a follower of the drink... except if the drink is predominant, like mixing milk with water and a child drinks it; the prohibition of breastfeeding is established unless water is predominant. Contrary to eating it, for it is not usually intended. So if mixed with food it becomes a follower of food and its ruling falls. This is objectionable in two ways: first, that some perfume is intended for eating if it is from edibles for the meaning inherent in it which is perfume, either for treatment or enjoyment alone or mixed as it is intended for drinking. Second, that intent in this chapter is not a condition because... His saying: (but he chooses if there is an excuse) i.e. chooses between dam, fasting, and feeding. His saying: (Likewise if he eats much perfume etc.) And if little, such that it does not stick to most of his mouth, then sadaqah is on him. This all when he eats it as is, i.e. without mixing or cooking. But if he mixes it with cooked food like saffron, then nothing on him, whether fire touched it or not, whether its smell is found or not, except that it is disliked if its smell is found. And if mixed with what is eaten without cooking like saffron with salt, the criterion is predominance. If salt is predominant, then nothing on him except that if its smell is present, eating it is disliked. If perfume is predominant, then in it is dam (from Lubab). His saying: (so it is like pure) i.e. penalty is obligatory even if its smell does not appear. Thus in al-Fath. His saying: (It should be equalized etc.) I say: al-Zayla'i did not differentiate in mixing with food between predominant and overcome, and his apparent words do not differentiate from drink; he said: If he eats saffron mixed with food or other perfume and fire did not touch it, dam is necessary; if fire touched it, nothing on him. And this detail applies to drink. End. And it is apparent from what al-Halabi also says.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion probe on the chapter of offenses (jinayat) during Hajj, specifically concerning the application of dyes, oils, and perfumes. The author first discusses dyeing (khidab) with henna and wasma, distinguishing between women dyeing hands/feet (dam if excessive, sadaqah if little) and dyeing the head with henna (always dam). For the beard, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: the Hidayah states both head and beard are 'guaranteed' but does not specify dam, while some commentators mistakenly assert dam for both. The correct view, from al-Mabsut via Miraj al-Dirayah, is that the beard incurs sadaqah, not dam, because its offense is less complete. Dyeing with wasma (a plant) incurs nothing unless there is fear of insects, then sadaqah, due to the partial offense. Abu Yusuf's approach regarding medicinal use (for headache) treats it as head covering, necessitating jaza' (penalty), which is agreed upon. The passage then addresses oiling (idhan) with oils like olive and sesame. The ruling differentiates between perfumed and unperfumed oil; for unperfumed oil, Imam Abu Hanifa mandates dam (because it is the basis for head and hand), while the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) mandate sadaqah (because it is essentially food, though beneficial for killing insects). The author reconciles by noting that the criterion is the oil's quantity in relation to perfume. Finally, the passage discusses mixing perfume with food or drink, emphasizing the principle of ghalabah (predominance). If perfume is predominant, the penalty is dam; if overcome, sadaqah or nothing if food is cooked. There is debate on equalizing food and drink rulings, with some scholars like al-Zayla'i treating them similarly. Throughout, the commentary emphasizes that these rulings are based on the nature of the act (whether it is direct perfume use or incidental), with istihsan playing a role in mitigating penalties for medicinal or necessary uses.

Key Terms
زيت (zayt): Olive or sesame oil used for oiling hair or skin
غلبة (ghalabah): Predominance of one substance over another when mixed
دم (dam): Blood sacrifice as penalty for major offenses in ihram
صدقة (ṣadaqah): Charity of food as a lesser penalty

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what penalty is due for a pilgrim who applies unperfumed olive oil to his head during ihram?
A) Dam (slaughter a sheep)
B) Sadaqah (charity)
C) Nothing
D) Expiation by fasting

Key Takeaway
Unperfumed oil triggers dam (mufta bihi), and the principle of ghalabah governs mixed substances.

Muhrim Mixing Perfume with Food/Drink: Dominance and Penalty
Expansion of the ruling on perfume mixtures for Muhrim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a Muhrim consumes a mixture containing perfume, distinguish between dominant and subordinate perfume, and determine the appropriate penalty (blood or charity) based on quantity and mixture type.

Core Idea
The penalty for a Muhrim depends on which ingredient dominates the mixture—not just the presence of perfume.

A Muhrim is prohibited from using perfume, but what happens when perfume is mixed with food or drink? The ruling is not uniform; it hinges on whether the perfume is dominant or subordinate in the mixture. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the criteria for dominance, the penalties (blood or charity), and the differences among Hanafi scholars. You'll learn to apply the principle of 'ghalaba' to determine the ruling in various scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and prohibited substance
First, recognize that the act is consumption of a mixture containing perfume (tayyib) by a person in ihram. Perfume includes substances like musk, camphor, saffron, etc. The ruling depends on whether the perfume is dominant (ghalib) or subordinate (maghlub) in the mixture.
The focus is on eating or drinking, not applying to the body.
2
Distinguish between cooked and uncooked mixtures
If the perfume is mixed with cooked food (e.g., saffron in a cooked dish), there is no penalty regardless of dominance, because cooking transforms the perfume. If the mixture is uncooked (e.g., saffron with salt), the dominance matters.
The passage cites Lubab: if cooked, no penalty even if smell is present, though it may be disliked (makruh).
3
Apply the criterion for dominance
Dominance is determined by the abundance of parts (kathrat al-ajza')—the physical quantity of perfume relative to other ingredients. According to al-Halabi, if the smell and taste are clearly present, it is dominant; otherwise subordinate. The mufta bihi view is that quantity is the measure.
Some scholars (al-Zayla'i) did not require dominance for food; they imposed blood even if perfume is subordinate. But the preferred view is the one based on abundance.
4
Determine the penalty based on dominance and amount consumed
If perfume is dominant: eating/drinking a large amount requires blood (dam); a small amount requires charity (sadaqah). If perfume is subordinate: eating/drinking a large amount requires charity; a small amount requires nothing. The definition of 'large' is what a just, knowledgeable person would consider large.
This is the detailed ruling from al-Halabi, adopted as mufta bihi.
5
Consider exceptional cases and intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Note that if the mixture is for medicinal purposes, the Muhrim has a choice between blood, fasting, or feeding. Also, Qadi Khan distinguished dominance without requiring smell, while al-Zayla'i did not differentiate between dominant and subordinate in uncooked food. The practical difference (thamarah) is that a Muhrim may owe blood even if no smell is detectable, as long as the perfume quantity is greater.
This ikhtilaf is legitimate; the tarjih follows al-Halabi.

غالباً كما لو خلط اللبن بالماء فشربه الصبي تثبت حرمة الرضاع إلا أن يكون الماء غالباً بخلاف أكله فإنه ليس مما يقصد عادة، فإذا خلط بالطعام صار تبعاً للطعام وسقط حكمه، ففيه نظر من وجهين: الأول أن من الطيب ما يقصد أكلاً إذا كان من المأكولات للمعنى القائم به وهو الطيبية إما مداواة أو تنعماً منفرداً أو مخلوطاً كما يقصد شرباً. الثاني أن القصد من هذا الباب ليس بشرط لأن هو قوله : (لكنه يتخير إذا كان لعذر) أي يتخير بين الدم والصوم والإطعام قوله : (وكذا إذا أكل الكثير من الطيب الخ) وإن كان قليلاً بأن لم يلتصق بأكثر فمه فعليه الصدقة. وهذا كله إذا أكله كما هو أي من غير خلط أو طبخ ، أما إذا خلطه بطعام قد طبخ كالزعفران فلا شيء عليه، سواء مسه النار أو لا، وسواء يوجد ريحه أولا إلا أنه يكره إن وجد ريحه. وإن خلط بما يؤكل بلا طبخ كالزعفران بالملح فالعبرة بالغلبة، فإن كان الغالب الملح فلا شيء عليه غير أنه إن كان رائحته موجودة كره أكله، وإن كان الغالب الطيب ففيه الدم (لباب) قوله : (فهو كالخالص) أي فيجب الجزاء وإن لم تظهر رائحته . كذا في الفتح قوله : (وينبغي أن يسوي الخ) أقول : لم يفرق الزيلعي في المخلوط بالمأكول بين الغالب والمغلوب، وظاهر كلامه عدم الفرق بينه وبين المشروب فإنه قال : لو أكل زعفراناً مخلوطاً بطعام أو طيب آخر ولم تمسه النار يلزمه دم، وإن مسته فلا شيء عليه. وعلى هذا التفصيل في المشروب ا هـ . وهو ظاهر ما يأتي عن الحلبي أيضاً

وذكر الحلبي في مناسكه أني لم أرهم تعرضوا بماذا تعتبر الغلبة وظهر لي أنه إن وجد في المخالط رائحة الطيب كما قبل الخلط وحس الذوق السليم بطعمه فيه حساً ظاهراً فهو غالب وإلا فهو مغلوب لأن المناط كثرة الأجزاء. ثم قال: لم أرهم تعرضوا في هذه المسألة في التفصيل أيضاً بين القليل والكثير كما في مسألة أكل الطيب وحده وأنه بإثباته فيها أيضاً لجدير. ويقال : إن كان الطيب غالباً وأكل منه أو شرب كثيراً فعليه الكفارة وإلا فصدقة وإن كان مغلوباً وأكل منه أو شرب كثيراً فصدقة وإلا فلا شيء عليه. ولعل الكثير ما يعده العارف العدل الذي لا يشوبه شره ونحوه كثيراً والقليل ما عداه ثم قال : ولا شيء في أكل ما يتخذ من الحلواء المبخرة بالعود ونحوه، وإنما يكره إذا كانت رائحته توجد منه بخلاف الحلواء المسمى بالقاووت المضاف إلى أجزائها الماورد والمسك، فإن في أكل الكثير دماً والقليل صدقة والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم بحقائق الأحوال.
Perfume, considering that it contains aromatic substances like rose and violet, makes itself fragrant and is not devoid of a type of perfume, and it kills insects, softens hair, and removes dirt and dishevelment. By oil is meant olive oil and sesame oil, called shiraj, so the remaining oils like fat and ghee are excluded, and it is restricted to oils because if he eats it or uses it as a medicine for cracks in his feet or puts drops in his ear, no blood sacrifice or charity is required, unlike musk, ambergris, ghaliyah, camphor, and similar substances where compensation is necessary when used medicinally, but he has a choice if there is an excuse, as will come. Similarly, if he eats a large amount of perfume, which is that which sticks to most of his mouth, then blood is required. In Fath al-Qadir: 'These points testify to the non-consideration of the limb absolutely in the obligation of blood, but rather that is when it does not reach the level of abundance in itself, as we have mentioned. We have mentioned from Qadi Khan that if he mixes perfume with food without cooking, the consideration is for the dominant. If the perfume is subordinate, there is nothing at all; some added except that it is disliked if its smell is present in it. And if it is dominant, then it is like pure, and similarly in al-Muhit and others. And they said: If he mixes it with a drink and it is dominant, then blood is required; if it is subordinate, then charity, unless he drinks it repeatedly, then blood; if it is for treatment, he has a choice. And it is appropriate to equate the mixed food and drink, each with subordinate perfume, either with nothing at all as is the ruling for food, or with the obligation of charity in both as is the ruling for drink. And what al-Muhit differentiated, that perfume is intended for drinking, so if he mixes it with a drink, it does not become a follower of a drink like it unless the drink is dominant, just as if he mixes milk with water and a child drinks it, the prohibition of rada' is established unless the water is dominant, unlike eating it, for it is not usually intended. So if he mixes it with food, it becomes a follower of the food and its ruling drops. This is open to criticism from two aspects: first, some perfume is intended for eating if it is from edibles due to the meaning inherent in it, which is fragrance, either as medicine or pleasure, alone or mixed, as it is intended for drinking. Second, the intention in this chapter is not a condition because... He said: (But he has a choice if there is an excuse) meaning he has a choice between blood, fasting, and feeding. He said: (And similarly if he eats a lot of perfume etc.) And if it is little, such that it does not stick to most of his mouth, then charity is required. All this is if he eats it as is, i.e., without mixing or cooking. As for if he mixes it with cooked food like saffron, there is nothing on him, whether fire touched it or not, and whether its smell is found or not, except that it is disliked if its smell is found. And if he mixes it with something eaten without cooking, like saffron with salt, then the consideration is for the dominant. If the salt is dominant, there is nothing on him, except that if its smell is present, eating it is disliked. If the perfume is dominant, then blood is required. (Lubab) He said: (So it is like pure) meaning compensation is obligatory even if its smell does not appear. Thus in al-Fath. He said: (And it is appropriate to equate etc.) I say: al-Zayla'i did not differentiate in the mixture with food between dominant and subordinate, and his apparent statement shows no difference between it and the drink, for he said: If he eats saffron mixed with food or another perfume and fire did not touch it, blood is required; if it touched it, there is nothing. And this detail applies to the drink. This is what appears from al-Halabi as well. And al-Halabi mentioned in his Manasik: 'I did not see them discussing how to determine dominance. It appears to me that if the smell of perfume is found in the mixture as before mixing, and the sound taste perceives its taste manifestly, then it is dominant; otherwise it is subordinate, because the criterion is the abundance of parts.' Then he said: 'I did not see them discussing in this issue the detail between little and much, as in the issue of eating perfume alone, and it is worthy to establish it here as well. It is said: If the perfume is dominant and he eats or drinks much of it, then atonement is required; otherwise charity. If it is subordinate and he eats or drinks much of it, then charity; otherwise nothing. Perhaps much is what a just knowledgeable person, not influenced by greed or similar, considers much; little is what is other than that.' Then he said: 'There is nothing in eating what is made from sweetmeat perfumed with oud and similar, but it is disliked if its smell is found from it. Unlike sweetmeat called qawut, to whose parts rosewater and musk are added, for in eating much is blood, and little is charity. And Allah, the Exalted, knows best the realities of rulings.
Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling for a Muhrim who uses perfume (طيب) mixed with food or drink. The author, al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah, explains the distinctions based on whether the perfume is dominant (غالب) or subordinate (مغلوب) in the mixture. The passage begins by discussing the nature of perfume, then moves to specific rulings: eating pure perfume (without mixing) requires blood (دم) if a large amount is eaten; otherwise charity (صدقة). When mixed with food or drink, the key is the concept of 'ghalaba' (dominance). If the perfume is dominant in an uncooked mixture (like saffron with salt), the ruling is the same as pure perfume (blood for large amounts, charity for small). If the perfume is subordinate and mixed with food that is not cooked, there is no penalty (though it may be disliked if smell persists). For cooked mixtures (like saffron in cooked food), there is no penalty at all, regardless of dominance, due to the transformation by cooking. The text also cites differences among Hanafi scholars: Qadi Khan distinguishes based on dominance; al-Zayla'i does not differentiate between dominant and subordinate in uncooked mixtures, requiring blood for any perfume; al-Halabi proposes that dominance should be determined by the noticeable presence of smell and taste, arguing that the criterion is the abundance of parts. The passage concludes by addressing the issue of little vs. much consumption even in mixed cases, suggesting a need for further specification. The overall hanafi position is that the penalty depends on the quantity and dominance of perfume, with the mufta bihi view (as per al-Halabi) relying on the quantity of parts.

Key Terms
الطيب (al-tayyib): Perfume or aromatic substance prohibited for a Muhrim, including musk, camphor, saffron, etc.
الغلبة (al-ghalaba): Dominance: the state where the perfume component in a mixture is more abundant in quantity than the other ingredients.
الدم (al-dam): Blood sacrifice (a sheep or equivalent) required as penalty for certain violations during Ihram.
الصدقة (al-sadaqah): Charity: a penalty of feeding the poor, usually half a sa' of wheat or equivalent, for minor violations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A Muhrim eats an uncooked mixture of saffron and salt where the saffron is dominant (by quantity) and he eats a large amount. What is the penalty?
A) Nothing because it is mixed with salt.
B) Charity (sadaqah) because it is mixed.
C) Blood sacrifice (dam) because the perfume is dominant and amount is large.
D) He has a choice between blood, fasting, and charity.

Key Takeaway
The penalty for a Muhrim consuming a perfume mixture hinges on the dominance (quantity) of perfume and whether the mixture is cooked, with blood for dominant large amounts and charity for subordinate large amounts.

Penalty for Wearing Sewn Garment or Covering Head for a Day
Commentary on the penalty for a Muhrim who wears sewn garment or covers head for a day or less.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a Muhrim who wears a sewn garment or covers his head for a full day versus less than a day, and explain the legal reasoning behind the time-based distinction.

Core Idea
Penalty for these Ihram violations depends on duration: a full day requires blood sacrifice, less requires charity.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling for a Muhrim who violates the prohibitions of wearing sewn garments or covering the head. The key factor is duration: a full day triggers a blood sacrifice (dam), while less than a day requires charity (sadaqah). We will explore the underlying principle that the completeness of the penalty mirrors the completeness of the offense, and how this is applied through the concept of a full day of benefit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and ruling
Recognize that the two prohibited acts are wearing sewn garments and covering the head. The ruling: for a full day, a blood sacrifice (dam) is wajib; for less, charity (sadaqah) is wajib.
The text states 'يوماً' for full day and 'وإلا تصدق' for less.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a talil (legal reasoning): 'لما علم أن كمال العقوبة بكمال الجناية' – the completeness of punishment is tied to completeness of the offense.
No direct Quran or hadith is cited; the reasoning is derived from the nature of the prohibitions.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Completeness of the offense is defined by uninterrupted benefit over a full day. The purpose of the garment/covering is to repel heat and cold, which is fully achieved over a day cycle.
The text explicitly says 'لأن المقصود من كل منهما دفع الحر والبرد واليوم يشتمل عليهما'.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The text hints at a difference of opinion: other schools may not require a full day for the full penalty. For example, the Shafi'i school may require a sacrifice for any wearing, regardless of duration.
This is implied by the need to 'تفصيل' and the comparison with perfume ruling.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The Hanafi position as stated in the matn is accepted by the commentator without dispute. The mufta bihi is the time-based distinction.
The authority weight is zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (أو لبس مخيطاً أو غطى رأسه يوماً وإلا تصدق معطوف على «طيب» بيان للثاني والثالث من النوع الأول، وجمع بينهما لأن الحكم فيهما واحد من حيث التقدير بالزمان، فإن قوله «يوماً راجع إلى اللبس والتغطية، وكذا قوله وإلا تصدق» أي وإن كان لبس المخيط وتغطية الرأس أقل من يوم لزمه صدقة لما علم أن كمال العقوبة بكمال الجناية وهو بكمال الارتفاق وهو بالدوام لأن المقصود من كل منهما دفع الحر والبرد واليوم يشتمل عليهما من قوله : وظهر لي أن وجد الخ) انظر هل يمكن أن يجري هنا ما مر عن الفتح من الفرق بين القليل والكثير في الثوب . ثم إن هذا الفرق ينافيه ما قدمناه عن الفتح من أنه إذا كان الطيب غالباً يجب الجزاء وإن لم تظهر رائحته فإنه يقتضي أن المناط كثرة الأجزاء لا وجود الرائحة تأمل قوله : (ثم قال الخ) يعني أنهم أوجبوا الكفارة فيما إذا أكل أو شرب مما كان الطيب فيه غالباً ولم يفصلوا بين ما إذا أكل أو شرب ذلك قليلاً أو كثيراً، وكذا فيما إذا كان مغلوباً، وينبغي التفصيل المذكور فإنه يبعد أن يجب بأكل لقمة مثلاً كما يجب بأكل الكثير قوله : (وأكل منه أو شرب كثيراً) الضمير يعود إلى المخلوط بالطيب الغالب طعاماً أو شراباً قوله : (فإن في أكمل الكثير دماً والقليل صدقة قال في الشرنبلالية : يتأمل في الحكم المسك المضاف إلى الحلوى مع ما قدمناه من اختلاطه بما يؤكل ويطبخ وفيما إذا لم يطبخ ا هـ . فإن الذي تقدم أنه إن جعله في طعام وطبخ فلا شيء عليه، وإن خلطه بما يؤكل بلا طبخ فإن كان مغلوباً فلا شيء عليه، وإن كان غالباً وجب الجزاء وإن لم تظهر رائحته. وعلى هذا فالظاهر أن هذه الحلوى غير مطبوخة وأن طيبها غالب ليوافق ما تقدم قوله : (لما علم إن العقوبة بكمال الجناية الخ) مقتضاه أنه لو أحرم بنسك وهو لابس المخيط وأدى ذلك النسك بتمامه في أقل من يوم وحل منه أن تلزمه صدقة إلا أن يوجد نص صريح بخلافه. فإن قلت : التجرد عن المخيط في النسك واجب مطلقاً، سواء طال زمن إحرامه أم قصر، والتقدير باليوم والليلة إنما هو فيما إذا طال زمن الإحرام إما إذا قصر أي
His saying: (Or if he wears a sewn garment or covers his head for a day, else he gives charity) is conjoined to 'perfume', an explanation of the second and third of the first type, and he combined them because the ruling for both is one in terms of temporal estimation. For his saying 'a day' refers to wearing and covering, and likewise his saying 'else he gives charity' means that if wearing a sewn garment and covering the head is less than a day, he is obligated to give charity, because it is known that the completeness of the punishment is with the completeness of the offense, and that is with the completeness of the benefit, which is continuity, because the purpose of each is to repel heat and cold, and a day encompasses them. From his saying: (And it appeared to me that if found etc.) Consider whether the distinction made by al-Fath regarding little and much in the garment can apply here. Then this distinction contradicts what we previously mentioned from al-Fath that if the perfume is dominant, compensation is required even if its scent does not appear, because it implies that the criterion is the abundance of parts, not the presence of smell. Reflect. His saying: (Then he said etc.) meaning they obligated atonement when he eats or drinks something in which perfume is dominant, and they did not distinguish between whether he ate or drank that little or much, and similarly when it is subordinate, and the mentioned distinction is appropriate, for it is unlikely that eating a single morsel should require what eating much requires. His saying: (And he ate or drank much of it) the pronoun refers to the mixture with dominant perfume, food or drink. His saying: (For in eating much is blood, and little is charity) He said in al-Sharnablaliyyah: 'One should reflect on the ruling of musk added to sweetmeat with what we have mentioned about mixing it with what is eaten and cooked, and in case it is not cooked.' For what preceded is that if he puts it in food and cooks it, there is nothing; if he mixes it with what is eaten without cooking, then if it is subordinate, there is nothing; if it is dominant, compensation is required even if its scent does not appear. Accordingly, it appears that this sweetmeat is uncooked and its perfume is dominant to agree with what preceded. His saying: (Because it is known that the punishment is with the completeness of the offense) Its implication is that if he enters Ihram for a ritual while wearing a sewn garment and completes that ritual entirely in less than a day and is released from it, then charity is required unless there is explicit text to the contrary. For you might say: Abstaining from sewn garment in the ritual is absolutely obligatory, whether his Ihram period is long or short, but the estimation by a day and night is only when the Ihram period is long; if it is short, then...
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn ruling regarding a Muhrim who wears a sewn garment (مخيط) or covers his head (تغطية الرأس). The author explains that both violations are measured by time: if done for a full day (i.e., from dawn to sunset or similar), a blood sacrifice (دم) is required; if done for less than a day, charity (صدقة) is required. The reasoning is that the completeness of the penalty corresponds to the completeness of the offense—the benefit derived from the garment/covering is maximal when sustained over a day, which includes both heat and cold protection. The commentary then digresses into a comparison with the perfume mixing discussion, noting a potential contradiction regarding the criterion of quantity vs. smell, but ultimately affirms the temporal distinction for sewn garments. The passage also addresses a hypothetical scenario: if a person enters Ihram already wearing a sewn garment and completes the entire pilgrimage in less than a day, charity is required (since the violation was not a full day). This shows that the time-based penalty applies even if the Ihram itself is short. The text concludes with a partial statement about the estimation by day and night when the Ihram period is long.

Key Terms
المخيط (al-makheet): Sewn garment, specifically tailored clothing that conforms to the body, prohibited for men during Ihram.
تغطية الرأس (taghtiyat al-ra's): Covering the head with a cap, turban, or anything that shelters the head, prohibited for male Muhrim.
اليوم (al-yawm): A full day, from dawn to sunset (or from sunrise to sunset according to some interpretations).
كمال العقوبة بكمال الجناية (kamaal al-‘uqubah bi kamaal al-jinaayah): The perfection of the punishment is tied to the perfection of the offense.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A Muhrim wears a sewn shirt during his Ihram for only two hours. What must he do?
A) Nothing, because it was less than a day.
B) He must give a blood sacrifice (دم).
C) He must give charity (صدقة).
D) He must repeat the Ihram.

Key Takeaway
The penalty for wearing sewn garment or covering head during Ihram is proportional to the duration of the violation: a full day requires a blood sacrifice; less than a day requires charity.

Determining Dominance of Perfume in Food During Ihram
Al-Halabi's investigation on the criterion for dominance and gradation of expiation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply al-Halabi's sensory criteria to determine whether perfume is dominant in a mixture and state the required expiation based on quantity.

Core Idea
Dominance of perfume is judged by smell and taste, not weight; expiation depends on both dominance and quantity.

When a pilgrim in ihram eats food mixed with perfume, the expiation required depends on whether the perfume is dominant (ghalib) or overpowered (maghlub) and whether the quantity eaten is large or small. The earlier scholars did not specify how to determine dominance, so al-Halabi (author of a manasik work) investigated and proposed a clear sensory test. This lesson unpacks his criteria and the resulting gradation of expiation, an important refinement for those issuing fatwas on ihram violations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
Recognize that eating or drinking food mixed with perfume during ihram triggers expiation. The ruling depends on two factors: whether the perfume is dominant and the quantity consumed.
This builds on the general prohibition of using perfume in ihram.
2
Understand the criterion for dominance
Al-Halabi states that dominance is determined by sensory detection: if the smell and taste of the perfume are clearly perceptible in the mixture as they were before mixing, then it is dominant (ghalib); otherwise it is overpowered (maghlub). The underlying principle is that the criterion is the abundance of perfume parts, not mere presence.
The test is holistic: both smell and taste must be manifest.
3
Distinguish between dominant and overpowered
Apply the sensory test to a given mixture. If the perfume's scent and flavor are clearly detectable, it is dominant. If not, it is overpowered. This distinction determines the expiation scale.
Cooked mixtures: if perfume is added before cooking, the cooking may nullify the perfume; but if added after, the original ruling applies.
4
Apply the gradation of expiation
Once dominance is determined, consider quantity. For dominant perfume: large quantity → dam (full expiation), small quantity → sadaqah. For overpowered perfume: large quantity → sadaqah, small quantity → nothing. Al-Halabi also distinguishes a special sweet called qawut (with rosewater and musk) which follows the same rules as dominant perfume.
Large quantity is defined by what a just, non-greedy expert considers large; small is other than that.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذكر الحلبي في مناسكه أني لم أرهم تعرضوا بماذا تعتبر الغلبة وظهر لي أنه إن وجد في المخالط رائحة الطيب كما قبل الخلط وحس الذوق السليم بطعمه فيه حساً ظاهراً فهو غالب وإلا فهو مغلوب لأن المناط كثرة الأجزاء. ثم قال: لم أرهم تعرضوا في هذه المسألة في التفصيل أيضاً بين القليل والكثير كما في مسألة أكل الطيب وحده وأنه بإثباته فيها أيضاً لجدير. ويقال : إن كان الطيب غالباً وأكل منه أو شرب كثيراً فعليه الكفارة وإلا فصدقة وإن كان مغلوباً وأكل منه أو شرب كثيراً فصدقة وإلا فلا شيء عليه. ولعل الكثير ما يعده العارف العدل الذي لا يشوبه شره ونحوه كثيراً والقليل ما عداه ثم قال : ولا شيء في أكل ما يتخذ من الحلواء المبخرة بالعود ونحوه، وإنما يكره إذا كانت رائحته توجد منه بخلاف الحلواء المسمى بالقاووت المضاف إلى أجزائها الماورد والمسك، فإن في أكل الكثير دماً والقليل صدقة والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم بحقائق الأحوال.
And al-Halabi mentioned in his Manasik: I have not seen them address by what the dominance is considered, and it appeared to me that if in the mixture the scent of perfume is found as before mixing, and the sound taste senses its flavor with a manifest sensation, then it is dominant, otherwise it is overpowered, because the criterion is the abundance of parts. Then he said: I have not seen them address in this issue the detail between little and much as in the issue of eating perfume alone, and that it is worthy to establish it therein as well. And it is said: if the perfume is dominant and he ate from it or drank a lot, then upon him is expiation, otherwise charity; and if it is overpowered and he ate from it or drank a lot, then charity, otherwise nothing. And perhaps the much is what the just expert who is not tainted by greed and the like considers much, and the little is other than that. Then he said: There is nothing in eating what is made of sweets perfumed with oud and the like; it is only disliked if its scent is emitted from it. Unlike the sweet called qawut, to whose parts are added rosewater and musk, for in eating much there is blood, and little charity. And Allah Most High knows the realities of states.
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents an investigation by al-Halabi (author of a manasik) regarding eating food mixed with perfume during ihram. The key issue is determining when the perfume is considered 'dominant' (ghalib) in the mixture. Al-Halabi proposes a sensory test: if the smell and taste of the perfume are clearly perceptible in the mixture as they were before mixing, then it is dominant; otherwise, it is overpowered (maghlub). The underlying principle is that the criterion is not just presence but abundance of perfume particles. He then addresses a gap in earlier scholarship: the detail between a small and large quantity. He suggests that if the perfume is dominant and one eats or drinks a large amount, full expiation (kaffarah/dam) is required; if only a small amount, then sadaqah. If the perfume is overpowered, a large amount requires sadaqah, and a small amount incurs nothing. He also distinguishes between types of sweets: those merely scented (e.g., with oud) are not forbidden but disliked if the scent remains; however, a sweet called qawut that contains musk and rosewater is subject to the expiation rules. This builds on earlier discussion in the text about the difference between cooked and uncooked mixtures: if perfume is added and then cooked, it nullifies the perfume (since cooking changes it), but if added without cooking, the original ruling applies.

Key Terms
غالب (ghālib): In a mixture, the component that is perceptible by smell and taste, indicating it is present in sufficient quantity to be considered dominant.
مغلوب (maghlūb): The component in a mixture that is not perceptible by smell or taste, indicating it is present in smaller quantity.
قاووت (qāwūt): A type of sweet made with rosewater and musk, specifically mentioned as triggering expiation rules.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Halabi, how is the dominance of perfume in a mixture determined?
A) By the weight of the perfume in grams
B) By whether the smell and taste of the perfume are clearly perceptible after mixing
C) By the seller's declaration
D) By the color of the mixture

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses sensory detection (smell and taste) to determine the dominance of perfume in food, and expiation is graded by both dominance and quantity.

Ruling on Wearing Sewn Garment and Covering Head During Ihram
Commentary expanding the ruling on wearing sewn garment and covering head with expiation details

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for wearing a sewn garment or covering the head during ihram, and distinguish between the expiation required for a full day versus less than a day.

Core Idea
A muhrim who wears a sewn garment or covers his head for a full day owes a dam; for less, sadaqah is sufficient.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the commentator expands on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, clarifying the graded expiation for wearing sewn garments or covering the head during ihram. The key factor is duration: a full day's benefit triggers a blood sacrifice, while a shorter period requires only charity. We will explore the underlying rationale based on the completeness of benefit (irtifaq) and the precise definition of 'wearing a sewn garment'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited acts and their ruling
Determine which acts are prohibited by the matn: wearing a sewn garment and covering the head. Both are haram during ihram and incur expiation graded by duration.
The text states that both acts have the same temporal estimation.
2
Understand the expiation gradation
A full day (or more) of wearing or covering requires a dam (blood sacrifice); less than a day requires sadaqah (charity). The reason is that complete benefit (irtifaq) from heat/cold protection is achieved over a full day.
The commentator links punishment to the completeness of the offense.
3
Define 'wearing a sewn garment' (makhit)
A makhit is a garment that encompasses the body and is held by stitching (or any joining of parts). Wrapping or draping without proper wear (e.g., placing a shirt like a cloak) is not considered makhit.
The text gives examples: inserting arms into sleeves or buttoning constitutes proper wear.
4
Apply the ruling to scenarios
Multiple garments worn in one sitting count as one offense. Continuous wearing across days counts as one offense unless the muhrim intends to stop. Forgetfulness, coercion, or ignorance do not waive the expiation, only remove sin.
The ruling includes all circumstances; the intention matters only for the number of expiations when re-wearing.

His statement: 'or he wore a sewn garment or covered his head for a day, otherwise he gives charity' is conjoined to 'perfume', explaining the second and third of the first type. He combined them because the ruling for both is the same in terms of temporal estimation. His statement 'a day' refers to both wearing and covering, and likewise his statement 'otherwise he gives charity' means if wearing a sewn garment or covering the head was less than a day, charity is incumbent upon him, because it is known that complete punishment is for complete offense, and complete offense is complete benefit, because the purpose of each is repelling heat and cold, and a day encompasses them. From his statement: 'and it appeared to me that if found...' Consider: can what was mentioned from al-Fath regarding the distinction between small and large amounts in clothing apply here? Then this distinction contradicts what we quoted from al-Fath that if perfume is dominant, expiation is obligatory even if its scent does not appear, for it necessitates that the criterion is abundance of parts, not presence of scent. Ponder. His statement: 'then he said...' means they obligated expiation when one eats or drinks from that in which perfume is dominant, and they did not differentiate between eating or drinking a small or large amount, and likewise when it is overpowered, but the mentioned differentiation is necessary, for it is far-fetched that a single morsel should obligate the same as a large amount. His statement: 'and he ate from it or drank much' the pronoun refers to the mixture with dominant perfume, whether food or drink. His statement: 'for in eating much is blood, and little is charity' said in al-Sharnublaliyyah: one should ponder the ruling on musk added to sweets with what we have mentioned about mixing it with food that is eaten and cooked, and when it is not cooked. For what preceded is that if he puts it in food and cooks, nothing is upon him; if he mixes it with food eaten without cooking, then if it is overpowered, nothing is upon him, and if it is dominant, expiation is obligatory even if its scent does not appear. On this basis, apparently this sweet is uncooked and its perfume is dominant to agree with what preceded. His statement: 'since it is known that punishment is for completeness of the offense...' its implication is that if he enters ihram for a ritual while wearing a sewn garment and performs that ritual completely in less than a day and exits ihram, that charity is incumbent upon him unless an explicit text exists to the contrary. If you say: being free of sewn garment in the ritual is obligatory absolutely, whether his ihram period is long or short, and the estimation by a day and night is only when the ihram period is long; as for when it is short, then blood is obligatory, and for a lesser offense charity is obligatory. The verification is that covering the head is part of wearing a sewn garment, so it is one offense, as will come that if he wears a shirt and turban, one blood is incumbent upon him; they reasoned that the offense is one. The reality of wearing a sewn garment is that by means of sewing, encompassing of the body and retention occurs. Hence if he wraps a shirt around himself or puts it on like a cloak or wears trousers as a waist-wrapper, there is no harm, because he did not wear it as a sewn garment due to lack of encompassing. Likewise if he inserts his shoulders into a cloak but does not insert his hands into the sleeves and does not button it, due to lack of encompassing. But if he inserts his hands or buttons it, it is wearing a sewn garment due to their existence, unlike the upper garment if he wears it as a waist-wrapper, he should not tie it with a rope or otherwise; even if he does, nothing is upon him because he did not wear it as a sewn garment due to lack of encompassing. He made 'wearing' absolute, so it includes whether he wears after ihram or enters ihram while wearing and continues. Unlike benefiting after ihram from perfume applied before ihram, due to the text; otherwise we would obligate it also. It includes whether he is forgetful, deliberate, knowledgeable, ignorant, voluntary, or coerced; expiation is obligatory on one who sleeps if someone covers his head, because benefit accrued to him, and lack of choice removes sin from him, like a sleeping person who rolls onto something he destroys. It includes whether he wears one garment or all garments together: shirt, turban, and socks. Hence he did not say 'wears a garment' like others. The author (al-Kanz) mentioned the ruling of a day and less, but did not mention the ruling of more, to indicate that it is like a day. So if he wears a sewn garment and continues for days, or removes it at night and repeats during the day or vice versa, one blood is incumbent upon him unless he intends to stop when removing. If he intends to stop and then wears again, expiation multiple, expiating for the first first time? And in the second is the disagreement of Muhammad. If he wears for a day and offers the blood, then continues wearing for another day, another blood is upon him without disagreement, because continuation has the ruling of initiation. And regarding: 'for him in his ritual there is complete benefit, so he would be leaving an obligation of his ihram, so should blood be obligatory?' I say: no doubt it is exquisite, but it needs an explicit transmission. This is a summary from the hashiyah of al-Madani from the commentary on al-Mansak by Shaykh Abd Allah al-Afif, and in it from the fatawa of his student al-Fadil Abd Allah Afandi Ataqi that he inclined to the obligation of blood. His statement: 'and the verification that covering the head...' said in al-Nahr: the verification is that between wearing a sewn garment and covering the head there is general and specific in absolute terms; they meet in covering like a sewn skullcap, and covering is unique by placing something like muslin that is not sewn on the head, and this suffices for the portion of difference. His statement: 'by means of sewing' is objected to by felt that is attached by adhesion, for it has no sewing yet it is considered sewn, unless by sewing is meant joining some parts to others (Sharh al-Lubab). His statement: 'or he gathered all the clothing' meaning in one sitting. Likewise in Sharh al-Lubab. Its implication is that if the sitting differs within one day, multiple expiations, and we will mention soon what contradicts it. His statement: 'as long as he did not intend to stop' i.e., he did not remove it with the intention to stop but removed it with the intention to wear again or removed it to replace it. Likewise in Sharh al-Lubab. It indicates that removing it to replace it does not make multiple expiations, so memorize, for it occurs often. His statement: 'and in the second' i.e., when he did not expiate for the first. His statement: 'and 'indi al-mudi'' in this manuscript with 'indi' added to the first person pronoun, and thus I saw it in...
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the ruling for a muhrim who wears a sewn garment or covers his head. The matn (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) states that if done for a full day, a dam (blood sacrifice) is obligated; if less than a day, sadaqah (charity) is required. The commentator clarifies that this ruling applies to both actions equally because the underlying benefit (irtifaq) of protection from heat and cold is achieved fully by a full day's duration. The passage then explores various details: the definition of 'wearing a sewn garment' requires the garment to encompass the body and be held by sewing — wrapping or draping without proper wear is not considered wearing. It emphasizes that the ruling applies regardless of intent (forgetful, deliberate, ignorant, coerced) except for perfume applied before ihram, which is excluded by textual evidence. A significant portion addresses the case of multiple garments: wearing a shirt, turban, and socks together counts as one offense and requires only one dam, as long as done in one sitting. If the removal and re-wearing are done with the intention to permanently stop (and then later re-wear), multiple expiations are due; this is the position of Abu Hanifa, with a disagreement from Imam Muhammad. The text also discusses the scenario of continuous wearing across multiple days: if one wears for a day, offers the dam, and then continues wearing, another day requires another dam by consensus. There is also a discussion about a hypothetical case where a muhrim completes his entire ihram in less than a day while wearing a sewn garment — some scholars inclined to obligate blood, but the commentator notes this needs explicit textual support.

Key Terms
مخيط (makhīṭ): A sewn garment that encompasses the body and is held by stitching, as opposed to a draped or wrapped cloth.
ارتفاق (irtifāq): Benefit or protection achieved by wearing a garment or covering, specifically from heat and cold.
دم (dam): A blood sacrifice (usually a sheep) required as expiation for major infractions during ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What expiation is due for a muhrim who wears a sewn garment for exactly 24 hours?
A) Dam
B) Sadaqah
C) Nothing
D) Repeat the day

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school grades expiation for wearing sewn garment or covering head during ihram by duration: a full day requires a blood sacrifice, less requires charity, based on the completeness of benefit.

Multiple Expiations When Re-Wearing: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Commentary expansion detailing the intra-Hanafi dispute on multiple expiations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the intra-Hanafi dispute on multiple expiations when a muhrim removes and re-wears a sewn garment, and evaluate the practical consequence.

Core Idea
If a muhrim removes a sewn garment intending to stop and then re-wears, Abu Hanifa requires multiple dams; Imam Muhammad requires only one unless a new intention is formed.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq delves into a subtle intra-Hanafi disagreement: when a muhrim removes a sewn garment with the intention to permanently stop but then later puts it back on, does he owe one expiation or multiple? The commentator presents Abu Hanifa's view requiring multiple and notes Imam Muhammad's dissent. Understanding this dispute clarifies the importance of intention (niyyah) in determining the number of violations.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario
A muhrim removes a sewn garment with the intention to stop permanently, then later re-wears it. The question is whether this counts as one or multiple violations.
If removal is for replacement or temporary, only one expiation.
2
Identify the default rule
If the muhrim does not intend to stop (e.g., removes to change), it is considered one continuous act. Multiple expiations only arise when there is a clear cessation of the violation.
The text says: 'if he intends to stop when removing, then wears again, multiple expiations.'
3
Recognize the dispute
Abu Hanifa holds that re-wearing after intentional cessation is a new independent act, requiring a separate expiation. Imam Muhammad holds that it remains part of the same violation unless a new intention is formed.
The passage marks it as 'khilaf Muhammad'.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Abu Hanifa, multiple dams (or sadaqas) are due; under Imam Muhammad, only one. This affects the total expiation amount.
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view, so multiple expiations are required in practice.

قوله : (فإن في أكمل الكثير دماً والقليل صدقة قال في الشرنبلالية : يتأمل في الحكم المسك المضاف إلى الحلوى مع ما قدمناه من اختلاطه بما يؤكل ويطبخ وفيما إذا لم يطبخ ا هـ . فإن الذي تقدم أنه إن جعله في لأن الارتفاق حصل له وعدم الاختيار أسقط الإثم عنه كالنائم المنقلب على شيء أتلفه وشمل ما إذا لبس ثوباً واحداً أو جمع اللباس كله القميص والعمامة والخفين ولذا لم يقل لبس ثوباً كغيره وبين المصنف حكم اليوم الجزاء كفر للأول أولاً وفي الثاني خلاف محمد ولو لبس يوماً فأراق دماً ثم داوم على لبسه يوماً آخر كان عليه دم آخر بلا خلاف لأن للدوام فيه حكم الابتداء. وفي فقد حصل له في نسكه ارتفاق كامل فيكون تاركاً الأجزاء ببعضها (شرح اللباب قوله : (أو جمع اللباس كله أي في مجلس واحد. كذا في شرح اللباب. ومفاده أنه لو اختلف المجلس في يوم واحد تعدد الجزاء وسنذكر عنه قريباً ما يخالفه قوله : (ما لم يعزم على الترك
