A) All of the head.
B) A quarter of the head.
C) More than half of the head.
D) Any amount, even a single hair.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, covering a quarter of the head in ihram obligates a dam according to Abu Hanifa, while Muhammad and Abu Yusuf require the majority; the quarter is preponderant in transmission.

Shaving and Covering During Ihram: Rulings on Hair Removal and Face Covering
Rulings on shaving and covering during ihram, with thresholds for expiation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on shaving a quarter of the head/beard versus less, and distinguish the rules for covering the face versus other body parts during ihram.

Core Idea
A quarter of the head/beard triggers a dam; less triggers sadaqah. Covering a quarter of the face also triggers a dam.

This lesson examines the detailed Hanafi rulings on shaving and covering during ihram. The text distinguishes between shaving a quarter of the head or beard, which requires a dam, and lesser amounts, which only require sadaqah. It also explains that covering the face (included in the head prohibition) similarly triggers a dam for a quarter coverage, while covering other body parts is permissible though makruh without excuse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their consequences
The text lists shaving the head, beard, neck, armpits, cupping place, and taking the mustache. For each, determine if the ruling is dam, sadaqah, or hukumat 'adl.
Focus on the threshold: quarter of head/beard = dam; less = sadaqah.
2
Understand the rationale for the threshold
The text explains that the completion of the violation (takamil al-jinaya) does not occur with less than the majority, except for shaving a quarter of the head because it is customary.
Appreciate the distinction between general principle and customary exception.
3
Apply the bandage analogy
The text applies the quarter rule to bandaging the head: if the bandage covers a quarter of the head, dam; otherwise sadaqah. This illustrates the principle's application.
Understand that the bandage case is derived from the shaving rule.
4
Distinguish covered areas
The text specifies that the face is part of the head for covering prohibition, so covering a quarter of the face requires dam. Ears, back of neck, and beard below chin are not prohibited to cover.
Memorize the list: what is prohibited to cover and what is not.
5
Note the exception for necessity
Covering other body parts is makruh without excuse but becomes permissible with necessity.
Keep in mind the broader principle of udhr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو حلق ربع رأسه أو لحيته وإلا تصدق كالحالق أو رقبته أو إبطيه أو أحدهما أو محجمة وفي أخذ شاربه حكومة عدل راجح دراية باعتبار أن تكامل الجناية لا يحصل بما دون الأكثر بخلاف حلق ربع الرأس فإنه معتاد. ويتفرع على هذا ما لو عصب رأسه بعصابة فعلى اعتبار الربع إن أخذت قدره من الرأس لزمه دم، وإن كان أقل فصدقة فما في المبسوط والظهيرية من أنه لو عصب يوماً فعليه صدقة محمول على ما إذا لم تأخذ قدر الربع أو مفرع على اعتبار الأكثر. وأراد بالرأس عضواً يحرم تغطيته على المحرم فدخل الوجه، فلو غطى ربعه لزمه دم رجلاً كان أو امرأة، وخرج ما لا يحرم تغطيته فلا شيء عليه لو عصب موضعاً آخر من جسده ولو كثر لكنه يكره من غير عذر كعقد الإزار وتخليل الرداء، ولا بأس بأن يغطي أذنيه وقفاه ومن لحيته هو أسفل من الذقن بخلاف فيه وعارضه وذقنه، ولا بأس بأن يضع يده على أنفه دون ثوب. وبين المصنف حكم اليوم وما دونه فأفاد أن الليلة كاليوم كما صرح به في غاية البيان والمحيط لأن الارتفاق الكامل الحاصل في اليوم حاصل في الليلة وأن ما دونها كما دونه . وأطلق في وجوب الصدقة فيما دون اليوم فشمل الساعة الواحدة وما دونها خلافاً لما في خزانة الأكمل أنه في ساعة واحدة نصف صاع وفي أقل من ساعة قبضة من بر ولما روي عن محمد أن في لبس بعض اليوم قسطه من الدم كثلث اليوم فيه ثلث الدم وفي نصفه نصفه
Or if he shaved a quarter of his head or his beard, otherwise he gives sadaqah like the shaver; or his neck, or his armpits, or one of them, or his cupping place. And regarding taking his mustache, the ruling is a fair value (hukumat 'adl). [This is] preponderant in insight, because the completion of the violation is not achieved with less than the majority, contrary to shaving a quarter of the head, for it is customary. And based on this, if he bandages his head with a bandage: according to the quarter, if it takes a quarter of the head, a dam is due; if less, then sadaqah. What is in al-Mabsut and al-Zahiriyyah that if he bandages for a day, sadaqah is due, is interpreted as when it does not take the quarter, or it is derived from the majority. He meant by 'head' a limb whose covering is prohibited for the muhrim, so the face is included. If he covers a quarter of it, a dam is due, whether man or woman. Excluded is what is not prohibited to cover, so nothing is due if he bandages another place on his body, even if large, but it is makruh without excuse, like tying the lower garment or interlacing the upper garment. There is no harm in covering his ears, back of neck, and the part of his beard below the chin, contrary to the part on the face, cheek, and chin. There is no harm in placing his hand on his nose without a cloth. And the author explained the ruling of the day and less, so he taught that the night is like the day, as stated in Ghayat al-Bayan and al-Muhit, because the complete comfort attained in the day is attained in the night, and less than that is like less than it. He spoke generally about the obligation of sadaqah for less than a day, so it includes one hour and less, contrary to what is in Khizanat al-Akmal that in one hour it is half a sa', and in less than an hour a handful of wheat. And it has been narrated from Muhammad that wearing part of a day gives a proportion of the blood, like one-third of a day has one-third of the blood, and half has half.
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq provides a detailed parsing of multiple rulings related to ihram violations. First, shaving: shaving a quarter of the head or beard requires a dam; less requires sadaqah. Shaving the neck, both armpits, or one armpit, or the cupping spot (mahjimah) also requires a dam. Taking the mustache (hadf al-sharib) requires a fair value (hukumat 'adl). The principle that the completion of the violation is not achieved with less than the majority is applied, but shaving a quarter of the head is an exception because it is customary. The author then applies the bandage case. Next, covering the face: since the face is included in the head for covering prohibition, covering a quarter of the face also requires a dam. The ears, back of neck, and beard below the chin are exempt from covering prohibition. Then, the duration for wearing stitched clothes: wearing for a full day or night requires a dam; less than a day requires sadaqah. This is based on the complete comfort (irtifaq kamil) attained in both day and night. The Mufta bihi position is that a full day or night requires a dam; for less, sadaqah. Muhammad is reported to have calculated by proportion (e.g., one-third day gives one-third dam), but this is not the relied-upon view.

Key Terms
حلق (halq): Shaving or removing hair; in this context, specifically shaving the head, beard, or other body parts during ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a muhrim shaves his entire beard during ihram, what is required?
A) Dam for a quarter or more; sadaqah for less.
B) No expiation because beard is not part of the head.
C) Dam for any amount, since beard is part of the head.
D) Only kaffarah if it is shaved with a razor.

Key Takeaway
A quarter of the head or beard shaved, or a quarter of the face covered, triggers a dam; less triggers sadaqah.

Duration for Wearing Stitched Clothes During Ihram: Day and Night
Ruling on the duration threshold for wearing stitched clothes during ihram, with equivalence of day and night.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a full day or night of wearing stitched clothes requires a dam, while less requires sadaqah, and evaluate the contradictory riwayah from Muhammad.

Core Idea
A full day or night triggers the same dam; less than a day triggers only sadaqah, regardless of the fraction.

This lesson focuses on the duration of wearing stitched clothes (al-makheet) during ihram. The author establishes that the night is equivalent to the day because complete comfort (irtifaq kamil) is attained in both. For any period shorter than a day, sadaqah is due. The text also notes a transmission from Muhammad that suggests proportional dam, but this is not the mufta bihi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
Wearing stitched clothes for a full day or night requires a dam. Less than that requires sadaqah.
2
Understand the equivalence of night and day
The author states that the night is like the day because the complete benefit is attained in both periods.
This is a key principle: al-laylah ka al-yawm.
3
Recognize the general scope of 'less than a day'
It includes even one hour or less, as the text says 'includes one hour and less' (shamila al-sa'ah al-wahidah wa ma dunaha).
Contrary to the view in Khizanat al-Akmal that different amounts apply for one hour vs less.
4
Note the alternative view from Muhammad
Muhammad is reported to have said that wearing part of a day gives a proportion of the dam, e.g., one-third day gives one-third dam. This is not the relied-upon position.
The Mufta bihi is that sadaqah is due for any period less than a full day/night, not a proportional dam.
5
Apply to a scenario
If a muhrim wears stitched clothes for 30 minutes, sadaqah is due. If he wears them for a full night, dam is due.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The Minimum Measure for Hair Removal during Ihram: Quarter vs. Third vs. Majority
Ruling with proof: halaq measure and definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relied-upon Hanafi ruling on the minimum measure of hair shaving during ihram that obligates a dam, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding quarter vs. third vs. majority.

Core Idea
Shaving a quarter of the head or beard obligates a dam in ihram; this is the relied-upon Hanafi position.

When a muhrim shaves or shortens his hair during ihram, a penalty is due. But how much hair must be removed to trigger the heavier penalty of a blood sacrifice (dam)? This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position on the minimum measure, which is a quarter of the head or beard, and explores why some Hanafi narrations mention a third or the majority. The key is the completion of benefit (al-irtifaq) that justifies the obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon (shaving head/beard) and the primary ruling: dam is obligatory when a quarter is shaved, sadaqah for less.
Dam is a wajib penalty, not fard, due to zanni evidence.
2
Locate the measure within the passage
Find where the text specifies the measure: 'rub' al-ra's' (quarter of head) or 'rub' al-lihyah' (quarter of beard). Note the source (al-Jami' al-Saghir).
The passage cites this as the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view.
3
Trace the intra-Hanafi dispute on the measure
Identify the alternative narrations: al-Asl says a third; Abu Hanifa in al-Muhit says the majority (al-akthar). Understand the evidence for each.
The quarter view is preferred by the mashayikh (later scholars).
4
Understand the definition of 'shaving' (halaq)
Note that halaq includes any removal of hair, not just shaving with a razor, as long as it is intentional and for adornment.
Accidental loss due to illness or fire is exempt because it is not for adornment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كان حلق ربع الرأس أو ربع اللحية موجباً للدم لتكامل الجناية بتكامل الارتفاق لأن بعض الناس يعتاده بخلاف تطييب ربع العضو فإن الجناية فيه قاصرة وكذا تغطية ربع الرأس على قول من اعتبر الأكثر. وإذا حلق أقل من الربع فيهما تقاصرت الجناية فوجبت الصدقة، واعتبار الربع في الحلق رواية الجامع الصغير اعتمدها المشايخ وأما رواية الأصل فاعتبار الثلث. وفي المحيط : وعند أبي حنيفة يجب الدم بحلق الأكثر اهـ . وأراد المصنف بالحلق الإزالة سواء كان بالموسى أو بغيره، وسواء كان مختاراً أولاً، فلو أزاله بالنورة أو نتف لحيته واحترق شعره بخبزة أو مسه بيده فسقط فهو كالحلق كما في المحيط وغيره بخلاف ما إذا تناثر شعره بالمرض أو النار فلا شيء عليه لأنه ليس للزينة وإنما هو شين. كذا في المحيط أيضاً. وأطلق في وجوب الصدقة فيما إذا حلق أقل من ربع الرأس أو اللحية فشمل ما إذا بقي شيء بعد الحلق أولا، فكذا لو كان أصلع على ناصيته أقل من ربع الرأس فإنما فيه صدقة، وكذا لو حلق كل رأسه وما عليه أقل من ربع شعره كما أطلق وجوب الدم بحلق الربع، فلذا لو كان على رأسه قدر ربع شعره لو كان شعر رأسه كاملاً ففيه قال دم . في فتح القدير : وعلى هذا يجيء مثله فيمن بلغت لحيته الغاية في الخفة وعلم من إيجابه الدم بحلق أحد الإبطين أو الإبطين أن جناية الحلق واحدة وإن تعددت في البدن، فلذا لو حلق رأسه ولحيته وإبطيه بل كل بدنه في مجلس واحد قدم واحد بشرطين الأول أن لا يكون كفر للأول، فلو أراق دماً لحلق رأسه ثم حلق لحيته نزمه آخر الثاني أن يتحد المجلس فإذا اختلف المجلس فلكل مجلس موجب جنايته إن تعدد المحل كما ذكرنا، وإن اتحد فدم واحد. اللباب أن حكمه حكم الحلق في وجوب الدم به والصدقة ، فلو قصر كل الرأس أو ربعه فعليه دم وفي أقل من الربع صدقة، ولو قصرت المرأة قدر أنملة من ربع شعرها فعليها دم. قال شارحه : أي على ما صرح به في الكافي والكرماني وهو الصواب قياساً على التحلل، ووقع في الكفاية شرح الهداية أن التقصير لا يوجب الدم ا هـ قوله : (وعلى هذا يجيء الخ) أي إن كان قدر ربعها كاملة ففيه دم وإلا فصدقة كما في اللباب قوله : (الثاني أن يتحد المجلس هذا مستغنى عنه لأن فرض المسألة فيه فلو أسقط أولاً من كلامه قوله «في مجلس واحد لاستقام قوله : ( وإن اختلف المجلس) «إن وصلية ولو حذف هذه الجملة لكان أقرب للفهم لأن قوله « وإن اتحد تصريح بمفهوم قوله إن تعدد المحل وهو مفروض فيما إذا اختلف المجلس وحكم ما إذا اتحد المجلس مفهوم بالأولى قوله : (كما إذا حلق الرأس في مجالس) قال في اللباب : فعليه دم واحد اتفاقاً. وكذا نقل المؤلف الاتفاق فيما سيأتي عند الكلام على قص الأظفار . قال في شرح اللباب : لأنها أجناس متفقة ولو كانت في مجالس مختلفة. كذا في الفتح ومنسك الفارسي وغيرهما، وإليه أشار في الكافي وشرح الكنز وفي البحر الزاخر ، فدم واحد بالإجماع ويخالفه بظاهره ما ذكره الخبازي في حاشيته على الهداية إذا حلق ربع الرأس ثم حلق ثلاثة أرباعه في أزمان متفرقة تجب عليه أربعة دماء، وإن اختلف المجلس كما إذا حلق الرأس في مجالس وخالف محمد فيما إذا تعدد المحل فألحقه بما إذا اتحد، وظاهر قول المصنف وإلا تصدق أن في إزالته لشعر الرأس أو اللحية إذا كان أقل من الربع نصف صاع ولو كان شعرة واحدة فإنهم قالوا كل صدقة في الإحرام غير مقدرة فهي نصف صاع من بر إلا ما يجب بقتل القملة والجرادة كما أن واجب الدم يتأدى بالشاة في جميع المواضع إلا في موضعين من طاف للزيارة جنباً أو حائضاً أو نفساء، ومن جامع بعد الوقوف بعرفة قبل الطواف فإنه بدنة . كذا في الهداية وغيرها لكن ذكر قاضيخان في فتاواه أنه إن نتف من رأسه أو من أنفه أو لحيته شعرات فلكل شعرة كف من طعام. وفي خزانة الأكمل : في خصلة نصف صاع فظهر بهذا أن في كلام المصنف اشتباهاً لأنه لم يبين شعر الصدقة ولم يفصلها. وأطلق في لزوم الصدقة على الحالق فشمل ما إذا كان محرماً، سواء كان المحلوق محرماً أولا أو حلالاً والمحلوق رأسه محرم، ولا يرد عليه ما إذا كانا حلالين لأنه ليس بجناية منهما وكلامه فيما يكون جناية. وإنما لزمه الصدقة فقط لقصور جنايته لأنه ينتفع بإزالة شعر غيره انتفاعاً قليلاً بخلاف المحلوق وإنما صار جناية من الحالق الحلال باعتبار أن المحرم لأن حلق كل ربع جناية موجبة للدم فإذا اختلف أزمان وجودها نزل ذلك بمنزلة اختلاف المكان في تلاوة آية السجدة فلا يتداخل ا.هـ. والظاهر أن مراده بالأزمان الأيام لا المجالس المتعددة في يوم واحد اهـ قوله : (وخالف محمد فيما إذا تعدد المحل كذا في بعض النسخ ، وفي بعضها «المجلس» بدل «المحل» وكلاهما صحيح لأن خلافه فيما إذا تعدد المحل والمجلس قوله : (فشمل ما إذا كان محرماً الخ) قال في النهر : إن في كلامه اشتباهاً أيضاً وذلك أن المحلوق رأسه لو كان حلالاً وكان الحالق محرماً تصدق بما شاء وفي غيره نصف صاع ا هـ . وسينبه عليه المؤلف قبيل قوله «أو قص أظفار يديه قوله : (أو حلالاً) أي أو كان الحالق حلالاً والمحلوق رأسه محرم فتلزمه صدقة. ومشى في اللباس على أنه لا شيء على الحالق في هذه الصورة ثم قال : وقيل عليه صدقة. ونقل شارحه ما مشى عليه في اللباب عن البدائع والكرماني والعناية والحاوي ونقل ما عبر عنه بقيل عن الزيلعي وابن اهمام والشمني ثم قال : ووجهه غير ظاهر إذ الحلال غير داخل في موجبات محظورات الإحرام، وهل يحرم عليه أو يباح فعله هذا أو يكره؟ الظاهر الآخر وذكر وجهه. وذكر أيضاً وجه الفرق بين ما إذا حلق المحرم رأس غيره حيث تجب الجناية وبين ما إذا ألبس المحرم محرماً لباساً مخيطاً حيث لا يجب عليه شيء فراجعه قوله : (لأنه ينتفع الخ) قال في الفتح : إذ لا شك في تأذي الإنسان بتفث غيره يجده من رأس إنساناً ثائر الرأس شعثها وسخ الثوب تفل الرائحة وما سن غسل الجمعة إلا لذلك قوله : (باعتبار أن شعر المحرم استحق الأمن الخ) أي بخلاف ما إذا لبس المحرم محرماً مخيطاً أو طيبه فإنه لا شيء عليه بالإجماع كما قدمه المؤلف عن الظهيرية وكذا لو غطى رأسه ووجهه كما في اللباب فلا شيء على الفاعل لأنه لم يزل الأمن عن مستحقه لكن يرد عليه ما في عبارة الظهيرية
Shaving a quarter of the head or a quarter of the beard necessitates a dam due to the completeness of the offense by the completeness of the benefit because some people are accustomed to it, unlike perfuming a quarter of a limb for the offense is deficient. Similarly, covering a quarter of the head according to the one who considers the majority. And if he shaves less than a quarter in both, the offense is reduced so sadaqah is obligated. The consideration of a quarter in shaving is the narration of al-Jami' al-Saghir which the scholars relied upon, while the narration of al-Asl considers a third. In al-Muhit: According to Abu Hanifa, the dam is obligated by shaving the majority. The author intended by shaving removal, whether with a razor or otherwise, whether willingly or not. So if he removes it with nurrah (lime) or plucks his beard or his hair burns from bread or he touches it with his hand and it falls, it is like shaving as in al-Muhit and others, unlike if his hair falls due to illness or fire, then nothing is upon him because it is not for adornment but rather a defect. Likewise in al-Muhit. And he made absolute the obligation of sadaqah when shaving less than a quarter of the head or beard, so it includes whether anything remains after shaving or not. So likewise if one is bald with less than a quarter of hair on his forelock, then there is only sadaqah, and likewise if he shaves his entire head and there is less than a quarter of hair, as he made absolute the obligation of dam by shaving a quarter. Therefore if on his head there is the amount of a quarter of hair if his head hair were complete, then there is a dam. In Fath al-Qadir: Upon this, its like comes for one whose beard is extremely thin. And it is known from his obligating dam by shaving one armpit or both armpits that the offense of shaving is one even if multiple on the body. So if he shaves his head, beard, armpits, or even his entire body in one sitting, one [dam] is due with two conditions: first that it is not expiated for the first [act]; so if he sacrificed a dam for shaving his head then shaved his beard, another [dam] is required. Second that the sitting is the same; so if the sitting differs, then for each sitting there is the due of its offense if the location is multiple as we mentioned, and if it is one then one dam. Al-Lubab: Its ruling is the ruling of shaving in the obligation of dam and sadaqah. So if he shortens all the head or a quarter, then he owes a dam, and for less than a quarter sadaqah. And if a woman shortens the amount of a fingertip from a quarter of her hair, she owes a dam. Its commentator said: That is as stated in al-Kafi and al-Kirmani, and it is correct by analogy to tahlul, but in al-Kifayah Sharh al-Hidayah that taqsir does not obligate a dam. His statement: (And upon this comes etc.) i.e., if its quarter amount is complete then a dam, otherwise sadaqah as in al-Lubab. His statement: (Second that the sitting is the same) this is needless because the premise of the issue is in it; if he first dropped from his statement 'in one sitting' it would be consistent. His statement: (And if the sitting differs) 'in' is conjunctive, and if he omitted this sentence it would be closer to understanding because his statement 'and if it is one' is a clarification of the implication of his statement 'if the location is multiple', and it is assumed when the sitting differs, and the ruling when the sitting is one is understood a fortiori. His statement: (as if he shaves the head in multiple sittings) said in al-Lubab: there is one dam by agreement. And similarly the author transmitted agreement in what will come regarding clipping nails. He said in Sharh al-Lubab: Because they are agreeing types even if in different sittings. Likewise in al-Fath and Munsik al-Farisi and others, and it is alluded to in al-Kafi and Sharh al-Kanz and in al-Bahr al-Zakhir, so one dam by consensus, and it is apparently opposed by what al-Khabbazi mentioned in his gloss on al-Hidayah: if he shaved a quarter of the head then shaved three quarters in separate times, four dams are obligatory upon him, even if the sitting differs, as if he shaves the head in multiple sittings. And Muhammad opposed in the case of multiplicity of location, equating it to when it is one. And the apparent meaning of the author's statement 'otherwise he gives sadaqah' is that for removing hair of the head or beard if less than a quarter, [the sadaqah is] half a sa', even if it is a single hair. Because they said: every sadaqah in ihram that is not specified is half a sa' of wheat, except what is obligatory for killing a louse or locust, just as the obligation of dam is fulfilled by a sheep in all places except two: one who performs tawaf al-ziyarah while junub or menstruating or postpartum, and one who has intercourse after standing at Arafah before tawaf, then it is a badanah. Likewise in al-Hidayah and others, but Qadikhan mentioned in his Fatawa that if he plucks from his head or nose or beard a few hairs, then for each hair a handful of food. And in Khizanat al-Akmal: for a single hair half a sa'. So it appears from this that there is confusion in the author's speech because he did not specify the sadaqah nor detail it. And he made absolute the obligation of sadaqah on the shaver, so it includes if he is muhrim, whether the one shaved is muhrim or not, or halal and the one shaved is muhrim. And it is not refuted by the case when both are halal because there is no offense from them, and his speech concerns what is an offense. And only sadaqah is obligatory for him due to the deficiency of his offense because he benefits slightly by removing another's hair, unlike the one shaved. And it only becomes an offense from the halal shaver by considering that the muhrim [is the one harmed]. Because shaving a quarter is an offense obligating a dam. So if the times of its existence differ, it takes the ruling of difference of place in reciting the verse of sajdah, so they do not overlap. And it appears that by 'times' he means days, not multiple sittings in one day. His statement: (And Muhammad opposed regarding multiplicity of location) thus in some copies, and in some 'sitting' instead of 'location', and both are correct because his opposition is when the location and sitting are multiple. His statement: (So it includes if he is muhrim etc.) said in al-Nahr: There is confusion in his speech as well, because if the one shaved is halal and the shaver is muhrim, he gives sadaqah as he wishes, and in other cases half a sa'. And the author will alert to it shortly before his statement 'or clips his fingernails'. His statement: (or halal) i.e., or if the shaver is halal and the one shaved is muhrim, then sadaqah is obligatory on him. And al-Labbas followed the opinion that there is nothing on the shaver in this case, then said: and it is said: sadaqah. And its commentator transmitted what al-Lubab followed from al-Bada'i', al-Kirmani, al-'Inayah, and al-Hawi, and transmitted what he expressed as 'it is said' from al-Zayla'i, Ibn al-Humam, and al-Shumunni. Then he said: its basis is not apparent since the halal is not included in the causes of prohibitions of ihram, and is it prohibited for him or permitted or disliked? The apparent is the other, and he mentioned its basis. And he also mentioned the basis of difference between when a muhrim shaves another's head where the offense is obligatory, and when a muhrim dresses a muhrim in sewn clothing where nothing is obligatory upon him. So refer to it. His statement: (because he benefits etc.) said in al-Fath: There is no doubt that a person is harmed by another's untidiness, finding from a person's head disheveled hair, dirtiness, foul smell, and the custom of Friday bath is only for that. His statement: (considering that the muhrim's hair deserves security etc.) i.e., unlike when a muhrim dresses a muhrim in sewn clothing or perfumes him, then there is nothing on him by consensus as the author presented from al-Zahiriyyah, and likewise if he covers his head and face as in al-Lubab, then nothing on the doer because he did not remove security from its deserving. But there is an objection to it from the statement of al-Zahiriyyah.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, expanding on the rulings of shaving (halaq) and shortening (taqsir) hair during ihram. The passage type is a ruling with proof, including intra-Hanafi disputes and multiplicity issues. The main ruling: shaving a quarter of the head or beard obligates a dam (blood sacrifice), while less than a quarter requires sadaqah. This is based on the principle that the offense is complete when the benefit (removal of hair for adornment) is complete, as some people are accustomed to shaving a quarter. The measure of a quarter is from the narration of al-Jami' al-Saghir (Zahir al-Riwayah), relied upon by the scholars, while another narration from al-Asl considers a third. According to Abu Hanifa in al-Muhit, shaving the majority obligates a dam. The definition of 'shaving' (halaq) includes any removal, whether by razor, lime, plucking, or accidental touch, as long as it is intentional; but if hair falls due to illness or fire, no penalty because it is not for adornment. The same ruling applies to shortening (taqsir): shortening a full head or a quarter requires a dam; less than a quarter requires sadaqah. For a woman, shortening the amount of a fingertip from a quarter of her hair obligates a dam, by analogy to tahlul. The passage then discusses multiplicity: if multiple acts are done in one sitting (majlis), only one dam is due, provided the acts are of the same type (e.g., shaving head, beard, armpits). If the sitting differs, separate penalties apply if the location is multiple. This is by consensus, except for a narration from al-Khabbazi that separate times require separate dams. Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani) opposed in cases where the location is multiple, equating it to a single sitting. Regarding sadaqah, the amount is generally half a sa' of wheat, as per al-Hidayah, but Qadikhan mentions a handful per hair, and Khizanat al-Akmal says half a sa' for a single hair, causing confusion. The passage also addresses cases where the shaver is muhrim and the shaved is halal or vice versa: if a muhrim shaves another muhrim's hair, the muhrim shaver owes dam or sadaqah; if a halal shaves a muhrim, sadaqah is due due to slight benefit. The halal is not bound by ihram prohibitions, so the liability is based on benefiting from the muhrim's hair. This is contrasted with dressing a muhrim in sewn clothing, where nothing is owed by the assistant because the muhrim's security is not removed.

Key Terms
الحلق (al-halaq): Removal of hair by any means (razor, lime, plucking, etc.), intended for adornment, during ihram.
الدم (al-dam): A blood sacrifice (sheep) required as penalty for violations during ihram.
الصدقة (al-sadaqah): A charity penalty of half a sa' of wheat for minor violations during ihram.
الربع (al-rub'): One quarter of the head or beard hair, the minimum measure for dam obligation (relied-upon view).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the minimum amount of head hair shaved during ihram that obligates a dam?
A) A single hair
B) A quarter of the head
C) A third of the head
D) The entire head

Key Takeaway
Shaving a quarter of the head or beard during ihram obligates a dam; this is the relied-upon Hanafi position, validated by the completion of benefit.

Multiplicity of Offenses and Special Cases in Hair Removal Penalties
Ruling with proof: multiplicity and special cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine whether multiple hair-removal acts during ihram require multiple penalties or just one, and identify the rulings when a halal person shaves a muhrim.

Core Idea
Multiple shaving acts in one sitting require only one dam, but separate sittings trigger separate penalties.

What happens when a muhrim shaves his head, beard, and armpits all in one go? Does he owe one dam or several? The Hanafi school rules that if the acts are in one sitting (majlis), only one dam is due, provided the acts are of the same type (removing hair). But if the sitting differs, separate penalties apply. This lesson also covers the ruling on taqsir (shortening) and the special case of a halal person shaving a muhrim, where only sadaqah is owed due to the slight benefit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle of unity of offense
The passage states that shaving multiple body parts (head, beard, armpits) in one sitting counts as one offense, so one dam suffices.
This is based on the idea that all hair removal is a single type of violation.
2
Understand the two conditions for one dam
First: no dam has been offered for the first act yet. Second: the acts are in the same sitting. If the sitting differs, each sitting's acts are separate.
If the acts are in different sittings but same location (e.g., head shaved in two sittings), there is ikhtilaf.
3
Apply the same ruling to taqsir (shortening)
Taqsir is equivalent to halaq in requiring dam for a quarter or full head, and sadaqah for less. A woman shortening a fingertip-length from a quarter of her hair owes dam.
This is the view from al-Kafi and al-Kirmani, opposed by al-Kifayah.
4
Analyze the sadaqah amount and confusion
The passage notes confusion: some say half a sa' per incident, others say a handful per hair. The relied-upon is half a sa' for general sadaqah, but for single hairs there is difference.
Qadikhan reports a handful per hair; Khizanat al-Akmal says half a sa' per hair.
5
Distinguish the case of halal shaving muḥrim
If a halal person shaves a muhrim's hair, sadaqah is owed (not dam) because the benefit is slight. This is separate from other violations like dressing a muhrim in sewn clothing.
The liability is based on benefiting from the muhrim's hair, not on ihram prohibitions.

كان حلق ربع الرأس أو ربع اللحية موجباً للدم لتكامل الجناية بتكامل الارتفاق لأن بعض الناس يعتاده بخلاف تطييب ربع العضو فإن الجناية فيه قاصرة وكذا تغطية ربع الرأس على قول من اعتبر الأكثر. وإذا حلق أقل من الربع فيهما تقاصرت الجناية فوجبت الصدقة، واعتبار الربع في الحلق رواية الجامع الصغير اعتمدها المشايخ وأما رواية الأصل فاعتبار الثلث. وفي المحيط : وعند أبي حنيفة يجب الدم بحلق الأكثر اهـ . وأراد المصنف بالحلق الإزالة سواء كان بالموسى أو بغيره، وسواء كان مختاراً أولاً، فلو أزاله بالنورة أو نتف لحيته واحترق شعره بخبزة أو مسه بيده فسقط فهو كالحلق كما في المحيط وغيره بخلاف ما إذا تناثر شعره بالمرض أو النار فلا شيء عليه لأنه ليس للزينة وإنما هو شين. كذا في المحيط أيضاً. وأطلق في وجوب الصدقة فيما إذا حلق أقل من ربع الرأس أو اللحية فشمل ما إذا بقي شيء بعد الحلق أولا، فكذا لو كان أصلع على ناصيته أقل من ربع الرأس فإنما فيه صدقة، وكذا لو حلق كل رأسه وما عليه أقل من ربع شعره كما أطلق وجوب الدم بحلق الربع، فلذا لو كان على رأسه قدر ربع شعره لو كان شعر رأسه كاملاً ففيه قال دم . في فتح القدير : وعلى هذا يجيء مثله فيمن بلغت لحيته الغاية في الخفة وعلم من إيجابه الدم بحلق أحد الإبطين أو الإبطين أن جناية الحلق واحدة وإن تعددت في البدن، فلذا لو حلق رأسه ولحيته وإبطيه بل كل بدنه في مجلس واحد قدم واحد بشرطين الأول أن لا يكون كفر للأول، فلو أراق دماً لحلق رأسه ثم حلق لحيته نزمه آخر الثاني أن يتحد المجلس فإذا اختلف المجلس فلكل مجلس موجب جنايته إن تعدد المحل كما ذكرنا، وإن اتحد فدم واحد. اللباب أن حكمه حكم الحلق في وجوب الدم به والصدقة ، فلو قصر كل الرأس أو ربعه فعليه دم وفي أقل من الربع صدقة، ولو قصرت المرأة قدر أنملة من ربع شعرها فعليها دم. قال شارحه : أي على ما صرح به في الكافي والكرماني وهو الصواب قياساً على التحلل، ووقع في الكفاية شرح الهداية أن التقصير لا يوجب الدم ا هـ قوله : (وعلى هذا يجيء الخ) أي إن كان قدر ربعها كاملة ففيه دم وإلا فصدقة كما في اللباب قوله : (الثاني أن يتحد المجلس هذا مستغنى عنه لأن فرض المسألة فيه فلو أسقط أولاً من كلامه قوله «في مجلس واحد لاستقام قوله : ( وإن اختلف المجلس) «إن وصلية ولو حذف هذه الجملة لكان أقرب للفهم لأن قوله « وإن اتحد تصريح بمفهوم قوله إن تعدد المحل وهو مفروض فيما إذا اختلف المجلس وحكم ما إذا اتحد المجلس مفهوم بالأولى قوله : (كما إذا حلق الرأس في مجالس) قال في اللباب : فعليه دم واحد اتفاقاً. وكذا نقل المؤلف الاتفاق فيما سيأتي عند الكلام على قص الأظفار . قال في شرح اللباب : لأنها أجناس متفقة ولو كانت في مجالس مختلفة. كذا في الفتح ومنسك الفارسي وغيرهما، وإليه أشار في الكافي وشرح الكنز وفي البحر الزاخر ، فدم واحد بالإجماع ويخالفه بظاهره ما ذكره الخبازي في حاشيته على الهداية إذا حلق ربع الرأس ثم حلق ثلاثة أرباعه في أزمان متفرقة تجب عليه أربعة دماء، وإن اختلف المجلس كما إذا حلق الرأس في مجالس وخالف محمد فيما إذا تعدد المحل فألحقه بما إذا اتحد، وظاهر قول المصنف وإلا تصدق أن في إزالته لشعر الرأس أو اللحية إذا كان أقل من الربع نصف صاع ولو كان شعرة واحدة فإنهم قالوا كل صدقة في الإحرام غير مقدرة فهي نصف صاع من بر إلا ما يجب بقتل القملة والجرادة كما أن واجب الدم يتأدى بالشاة في جميع المواضع إلا في موضعين من طاف للزيارة جنباً أو حائضاً أو نفساء، ومن جامع بعد الوقوف بعرفة قبل الطواف فإنه بدنة . كذا في الهداية وغيرها لكن ذكر قاضيخان في فتاواه أنه إن نتف من رأسه أو من أنفه أو لحيته شعرات فلكل شعرة كف من طعام. وفي خزانة الأكمل : في خصلة نصف صاع فظهر بهذا أن في كلام المصنف اشتباهاً لأنه لم يبين شعر الصدقة ولم يفصلها. وأطلق في لزوم الصدقة على الحالق فشمل ما إذا كان محرماً، سواء كان المحلوق محرماً أولا أو حلالاً والمحلوق رأسه محرم، ولا يرد عليه ما إذا كانا حلالين لأنه ليس بجناية منهما وكلامه فيما يكون جناية. وإنما لزمه الصدقة فقط لقصور جنايته لأنه ينتفع بإزالة شعر غيره انتفاعاً قليلاً بخلاف المحلوق وإنما صار جناية من الحالق الحلال باعتبار أن المحرم لأن حلق كل ربع جناية موجبة للدم فإذا اختلف أزمان وجودها نزل ذلك بمنزلة اختلاف المكان في تلاوة آية السجدة فلا يتداخل ا.هـ. والظاهر أن مراده بالأزمان الأيام لا المجالس المتعددة في يوم واحد اهـ قوله : (وخالف محمد فيما إذا تعدد المحل كذا في بعض النسخ ، وفي بعضها «المجلس» بدل «المحل» وكلاهما صحيح لأن خلافه فيما إذا تعدد المحل والمجلس قوله : (فشمل ما إذا كان محرماً الخ) قال في النهر : إن في كلامه اشتباهاً أيضاً وذلك أن المحلوق رأسه لو كان حلالاً وكان الحالق محرماً تصدق بما شاء وفي غيره نصف صاع ا هـ . وسينبه عليه المؤلف قبيل قوله «أو قص أظفار يديه قوله : (أو حلالاً) أي أو كان الحالق حلالاً والمحلوق رأسه محرم فتلزمه صدقة. ومشى في اللباس على أنه لا شيء على الحالق في هذه الصورة ثم قال : وقيل عليه صدقة. ونقل شارحه ما مشى عليه في اللباب عن البدائع والكرماني والعناية والحاوي ونقل ما عبر عنه بقيل عن الزيلعي وابن اهمام والشمني ثم قال : ووجهه غير ظاهر إذ الحلال غير داخل في موجبات محظورات الإحرام، وهل يحرم عليه أو يباح فعله هذا أو يكره؟ الظاهر الآخر وذكر وجهه. وذكر أيضاً وجه الفرق بين ما إذا حلق المحرم رأس غيره حيث تجب الجناية وبين ما إذا ألبس المحرم محرماً لباساً مخيطاً حيث لا يجب عليه شيء فراجعه قوله : (لأنه ينتفع الخ) قال في الفتح : إذ لا شك في تأذي الإنسان بتفث غيره يجده من رأس إنساناً ثائر الرأس شعثها وسخ الثوب تفل الرائحة وما سن غسل الجمعة إلا لذلك قوله : (باعتبار أن شعر المحرم استحق الأمن الخ) أي بخلاف ما إذا لبس المحرم محرماً مخيطاً أو طيبه فإنه لا شيء عليه بالإجماع كما قدمه المؤلف عن الظهيرية وكذا لو غطى رأسه ووجهه كما في اللباب فلا شيء على الفاعل لأنه لم يزل الأمن عن مستحقه لكن يرد عليه ما في عبارة الظهيرية
Shaving a quarter of the head or a quarter of the beard necessitates a dam due to the completeness of the offense by the completeness of the benefit because some people are accustomed to it, unlike perfuming a quarter of a limb for the offense is deficient. Similarly, covering a quarter of the head according to the one who considers the majority. And if he shaves less than a quarter in both, the offense is reduced so sadaqah is obligated. The consideration of a quarter in shaving is the narration of al-Jami' al-Saghir which the scholars relied upon, while the narration of al-Asl considers a third. In al-Muhit: According to Abu Hanifa, the dam is obligated by shaving the majority. The author intended by shaving removal, whether with a razor or otherwise, whether willingly or not. So if he removes it with nurrah (lime) or plucks his beard or his hair burns from bread or he touches it with his hand and it falls, it is like shaving as in al-Muhit and others, unlike if his hair falls due to illness or fire, then nothing is upon him because it is not for adornment but rather a defect. Likewise in al-Muhit. And he made absolute the obligation of sadaqah when shaving less than a quarter of the head or beard, so it includes whether anything remains after shaving or not. So likewise if one is bald with less than a quarter of hair on his forelock, then there is only sadaqah, and likewise if he shaves his entire head and there is less than a quarter of hair, as he made absolute the obligation of dam by shaving a quarter. Therefore if on his head there is the amount of a quarter of hair if his head hair were complete, then there is a dam. In Fath al-Qadir: Upon this, its like comes for one whose beard is extremely thin. And it is known from his obligating dam by shaving one armpit or both armpits that the offense of shaving is one even if multiple on the body. So if he shaves his head, beard, armpits, or even his entire body in one sitting, one [dam] is due with two conditions: first that it is not expiated for the first [act]; so if he sacrificed a dam for shaving his head then shaved his beard, another [dam] is required. Second that the sitting is the same; so if the sitting differs, then for each sitting there is the due of its offense if the location is multiple as we mentioned, and if it is one then one dam. Al-Lubab: Its ruling is the ruling of shaving in the obligation of dam and sadaqah. So if he shortens all the head or a quarter, then he owes a dam, and for less than a quarter sadaqah. And if a woman shortens the amount of a fingertip from a quarter of her hair, she owes a dam. Its commentator said: That is as stated in al-Kafi and al-Kirmani, and it is correct by analogy to tahlul, but in al-Kifayah Sharh al-Hidayah that taqsir does not obligate a dam. His statement: (And upon this comes etc.) i.e., if its quarter amount is complete then a dam, otherwise sadaqah as in al-Lubab. His statement: (Second that the sitting is the same) this is needless because the premise of the issue is in it; if he first dropped from his statement 'in one sitting' it would be consistent. His statement: (And if the sitting differs) 'in' is conjunctive, and if he omitted this sentence it would be closer to understanding because his statement 'and if it is one' is a clarification of the implication of his statement 'if the location is multiple', and it is assumed when the sitting differs, and the ruling when the sitting is one is understood a fortiori. His statement: (as if he shaves the head in multiple sittings) said in al-Lubab: there is one dam by agreement. And similarly the author transmitted agreement in what will come regarding clipping nails. He said in Sharh al-Lubab: Because they are agreeing types even if in different sittings. Likewise in al-Fath and Munsik al-Farisi and others, and it is alluded to in al-Kafi and Sharh al-Kanz and in al-Bahr al-Zakhir, so one dam by consensus, and it is apparently opposed by what al-Khabbazi mentioned in his gloss on al-Hidayah: if he shaved a quarter of the head then shaved three quarters in separate times, four dams are obligatory upon him, even if the sitting differs, as if he shaves the head in multiple sittings. And Muhammad opposed in the case of multiplicity of location, equating it to when it is one. And the apparent meaning of the author's statement 'otherwise he gives sadaqah' is that for removing hair of the head or beard if less than a quarter, [the sadaqah is] half a sa', even if it is a single hair. Because they said: every sadaqah in ihram that is not specified is half a sa' of wheat, except what is obligatory for killing a louse or locust, just as the obligation of dam is fulfilled by a sheep in all places except two: one who performs tawaf al-ziyarah while junub or menstruating or postpartum, and one who has intercourse after standing at Arafah before tawaf, then it is a badanah. Likewise in al-Hidayah and others, but Qadikhan mentioned in his Fatawa that if he plucks from his head or nose or beard a few hairs, then for each hair a handful of food. And in Khizanat al-Akmal: for a single hair half a sa'. So it appears from this that there is confusion in the author's speech because he did not specify the sadaqah nor detail it. And he made absolute the obligation of sadaqah on the shaver, so it includes if he is muhrim, whether the one shaved is muhrim or not, or halal and the one shaved is muhrim. And it is not refuted by the case when both are halal because there is no offense from them, and his speech concerns what is an offense. And only sadaqah is obligatory for him due to the deficiency of his offense because he benefits slightly by removing another's hair, unlike the one shaved. And it only becomes an offense from the halal shaver by considering that the muhrim [is the one harmed]. Because shaving a quarter is an offense obligating a dam. So if the times of its existence differ, it takes the ruling of difference of place in reciting the verse of sajdah, so they do not overlap. And it appears that by 'times' he means days, not multiple sittings in one day. His statement: (And Muhammad opposed regarding multiplicity of location) thus in some copies, and in some 'sitting' instead of 'location', and both are correct because his opposition is when the location and sitting are multiple. His statement: (So it includes if he is muhrim etc.) said in al-Nahr: There is confusion in his speech as well, because if the one shaved is halal and the shaver is muhrim, he gives sadaqah as he wishes, and in other cases half a sa'. And the author will alert to it shortly before his statement 'or clips his fingernails'. His statement: (or halal) i.e., or if the shaver is halal and the one shaved is muhrim, then sadaqah is obligatory on him. And al-Labbas followed the opinion that there is nothing on the shaver in this case, then said: and it is said: sadaqah. And its commentator transmitted what al-Lubab followed from al-Bada'i', al-Kirmani, al-'Inayah, and al-Hawi, and transmitted what he expressed as 'it is said' from al-Zayla'i, Ibn al-Humam, and al-Shumunni. Then he said: its basis is not apparent since the halal is not included in the causes of prohibitions of ihram, and is it prohibited for him or permitted or disliked? The apparent is the other, and he mentioned its basis. And he also mentioned the basis of difference between when a muhrim shaves another's head where the offense is obligatory, and when a muhrim dresses a muhrim in sewn clothing where nothing is obligatory upon him. So refer to it. His statement: (because he benefits etc.) said in al-Fath: There is no doubt that a person is harmed by another's untidiness, finding from a person's head disheveled hair, dirtiness, foul smell, and the custom of Friday bath is only for that. His statement: (considering that the muhrim's hair deserves security etc.) i.e., unlike when a muhrim dresses a muhrim in sewn clothing or perfumes him, then there is nothing on him by consensus as the author presented from al-Zahiriyyah, and likewise if he covers his head and face as in al-Lubab, then nothing on the doer because he did not remove security from its deserving. But there is an objection to it from the statement of al-Zahiriyyah.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, expanding on the rulings of shaving (halaq) and shortening (taqsir) hair during ihram. The passage type is a ruling with proof, including intra-Hanafi disputes and multiplicity issues. The main ruling: shaving a quarter of the head or beard obligates a dam (blood sacrifice), while less than a quarter requires sadaqah. This is based on the principle that the offense is complete when the benefit (removal of hair for adornment) is complete, as some people are accustomed to shaving a quarter. The measure of a quarter is from the narration of al-Jami' al-Saghir (Zahir al-Riwayah), relied upon by the scholars, while another narration from al-Asl considers a third. According to Abu Hanifa in al-Muhit, shaving the majority obligates a dam. The definition of 'shaving' (halaq) includes any removal, whether by razor, lime, plucking, or accidental touch, as long as it is intentional; but if hair falls due to illness or fire, no penalty because it is not for adornment. The same ruling applies to shortening (taqsir): shortening a full head or a quarter requires a dam; less than a quarter requires sadaqah. For a woman, shortening the amount of a fingertip from a quarter of her hair obligates a dam, by analogy to tahlul. The passage then discusses multiplicity: if multiple acts are done in one sitting (majlis), only one dam is due, provided the acts are of the same type (e.g., shaving head, beard, armpits). If the sitting differs, separate penalties apply if the location is multiple. This is by consensus, except for a narration from al-Khabbazi that separate times require separate dams. Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani) opposed in cases where the location is multiple, equating it to a single sitting. Regarding sadaqah, the amount is generally half a sa' of wheat, as per al-Hidayah, but Qadikhan mentions a handful per hair, and Khizanat al-Akmal says half a sa' for a single hair, causing confusion. The passage also addresses cases where the shaver is muhrim and the shaved is halal or vice versa: if a muhrim shaves another muhrim's hair, the muhrim shaver owes dam or sadaqah; if a halal shaves a muhrim, sadaqah is due due to slight benefit. The halal is not bound by ihram prohibitions, so the liability is based on benefiting from the muhrim's hair. This is contrasted with dressing a muhrim in sewn clothing, where nothing is owed by the assistant because the muhrim's security is not removed.

Key Terms
التقصير (al-taqsir): Shortening hair during ihram, considered equivalent to halaq in requiring dam or sadaqah.
المجلس (al-majlis): A sitting or session; legal unit for determining multiplicity of penalties.
المحل (al-mahall): Location on the body where the act is performed (head, beard, armpit).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A muhrim shaves his head and beard in one sitting. How many dams does he owe?
A) Two dams, because there are two locations.
B) One dam, because the acts are of the same type and in one sitting.
C) No dam, because he did not shave the entire head.
D) One dam for the head and sadaqah for the beard.

Key Takeaway
Multiple hair removal acts in one sitting require one dam; separate sittings require separate penalties, but there is a consensus on one dam for the same location even in different sittings.

Fidyah for Shaving Head/Beard and Liability of the Shaver
Ruling on hair removal fidyah and shaver liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the fidyah required for removing hair from the head or beard during ihram, distinguish between compensation for less than a quarter and a quarter or more, and explain the liability of the shaver versus the one shaved.

Core Idea
For hair removal in ihram, less than a quarter requires half a sa' wheat; a quarter or more requires blood.

This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq addresses a common scenario: a muhrim shaves or plucks hair from the head or beard. The ruling depends on the quantity removed and who performs the act. We will unpack the fidyah amounts, the shaver's liability, and an intra-Hanafi difference on multiple sessions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what prohibited act is being evaluated (hair removal during ihram) and whether the compensation is sadaqah or dam based on the amount removed.
Less than a quarter = half sa' wheat (sadaqah); a quarter or more = dam.
2
Locate the dalil
The general rule for unspecified sadaqah in ihram is half a sa' of wheat, as derived from the sunnah. The distinction between sadaqah and dam is based on the magnitude of harm.
The specific evidence is not quoted but is from the established principles of ihram violations.
3
Analyze the shaver's liability
Understand why the shaver owes sadaqah instead of dam: the shaver's violation is minor (benefit is slight), while the one shaved (if he did it himself) would owe dam for a quarter or more.
If the muhrim is coerced, the coercer owes dam.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on multiple sessions
Compare Abu Hanifa's view (same day = one act, different days = separate) with Imam Muhammad's view (each place/session is separate).
The relied-upon view is Abu Hanifa's.

And it becomes a violation from the non-muhrim shaver because the muhrim's right to safety has been removed, and he has removed it from him, so he is a violator. And if the one shaved is coerced, blood (dam) is obligatory upon the shaver and he has no recourse against the one who shaved according to us; this is as in al-Muhit.

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq addresses the fidyah for shaving or plucking hair during ihram. The author explains that when the ruling is described as 'charity' for removal of less than a quarter of head or beard hair, the amount is half a sa' of wheat, even for a single hair. This is the general rule for unspecified charities in ihram, except for the specific cases of killing a louse or locust, which require separate rulings. Qadi Khan's Fatawa is cited for a different opinion: for plucking individual hairs, each hair requires a handful (kaf) of food, while Khazanat al-Akmal says for a lock of hair half a sa'. The commentator notes an ambiguity in the author's wording regarding whether the charity is for the act of shaving or the hair quantity. The discussion then turns to the liability of the shaver (al-haaliq). The commentator clarifies that the shaver owes charity (not blood) because his violation is minor: he only benefits slightly from removing another's hair, whereas the one shaved (the muhrim) would owe blood for removing his own hair. The ruling applies whether the shaver is muhrim or not, as long as the one shaved is muhrim. If both are non-muhrim, there is no violation. A key point is that if the muhrim is coerced into being shaved, the blood (dam) obligation falls on the one who shaves, not the muhrim, and the muhrim has no recourse against the shaver. The commentator also notes a difference of opinion with Imam Muhammad regarding multiple sessions or places: if hair is removed in multiple settings, Muhammad considers them separate acts requiring separate charity, whereas Abu Hanifa sees them as a single act. The reasoning analogizes to the recitation of a prostration verse in different locations.

Key Terms
صدقة (sadaqah): Obligatory charitable compensation of half a sa' of wheat for minor ihram violations.
جناية (jinayah): A violation during ihram requiring fidyah.
دم (dam): Blood sacrifice (sheep) required for major ihram violations.
ربع (rub'): Quarter of the head or beard; the threshold for sadaqah vs. dam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a muhrim plucks three hairs from his beard during ihram, what compensation is required according to the relied-upon Hanafi position?
A) Dam (blood)
B) Half a sa' of wheat for the act
C) A handful of food per hair
D) Nothing at all

Key Takeaway
Removing less than a quarter of head/beard hair during ihram requires half a sa' of wheat (sadaqah), while a quarter or more requires dam (blood).

Shaving Non-Head Body Parts and Cutting Nails in Ihram
Rulings on shaving neck, armpit, cupping site, chest, leg, and cutting nails

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the distinction between intended (maqsud) and non-intended body parts to determine whether a muhrim owes blood or sadaqah for shaving or cutting nails.

Core Idea
For non-head/beard body parts, only complete removal triggers dam; partial removal requires sadaqah.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies the fidyah obligations for a muhrim who shaves body parts other than the head and beard. The key principle is whether the shaved organ is 'intended' (maqsud) for shaving and whether the entire organ is removed. Understanding this distinction is essential for applying the correct compensation (dam or sadaqah). The passage also addresses cutting nails of another person, where the majority view equates it to shaving.

Guided Path
1
Identify the body part and its category
Is the shaved area part of the head/beard, or another body part like neck, armpit, chest, leg, or cupping site? Each category has different rules for when dam vs. sadaqah applies.
Head/beard use a quarter threshold; other parts use a whole organ threshold.
2
Determine if the part is 'intended' (maqsud) for shaving
An intended part is one customarily shaved for its own benefit (e.g., head, beard, armpit) or as a means to an end (e.g., cupping site for cupping). Non-intended parts (e.g., chest, leg) are shaved only incidentally as part of a larger grooming (tanwir).
The classification affects whether partial shaving can trigger dam.
3
Check whether the entire organ was shaved
For intended body parts other than head/beard, dam is only due if the whole organ (e.g., entire armpit, entire neck) is shaved. If any part remains, even if most is shaved, only sadaqah is due.
For head/beard, shaving a quarter triggers dam.
4
Apply the ruling based on completeness
If the entire intended organ (non-head) is shaved → dam. If less than the whole, or a non-intended organ → sadaqah. For cupping site, if shaved without cupping, it is non-intended → sadaqah.
The 'illa (effective cause) is complete benefit (irtifaq).
5
For cutting nails of another, apply the majority view
The majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf) equate cutting another’s nails to shaving the same organ. If a muhrim cuts another’s nails, he owes sadaqah (since nails are small, not a full organ). A narration from Muhammad says nothing is due.
The relied-upon position follows the majority.

Source Text

وظاهر كلامه أنه لا بد من حلق جميع الرقبة والإبط والمحجمة في لزوم الدم بكل منهم، فلو بقي من الرقبة أو الإبط شيء لا يلزمه دم وإن كان قليلاً ولهذا قال الأسبيجابي : ولو حلق من أحد الإبطين أكثره وجبت الصدقة. فعلى هذا فما صرح به من المحيط من أن الأكثر من الرقبة كالكل في لزوم الدم وأن الأصل أن كل عضو له نظير في البدن لا يقوم أكثره مقام كله وكل عضو لا نظير له في البدن كالرقبة يقوم أكثره مقام كله وما في فتاوى قاضيخان من أن في الإبط إذا كان كثير الشعر يعتبر فيه الربع لوجوب الدم وإلا فالأكثر ضعيف لأنه لم يقيد أحد حلق ربع غير اللحية والرأس فليس فيه ارتفاق كامل، ولهذا قال الشارح: ثم الربع من هذه الأعضاء لا يعتبر بالكل لأن العادة لم تجر في هذه الأعضاء بالاقتصار على البعض فلا يكون حلق البعض ارتفاقاً كاملاً حتى لو حلق أكثر الإبط لا يجب عليه إلا صدقة بخلاف الرأس واللحية ! فالمذهب ما في الكتاب من اعتبار الربع في الرأس واللحية والكل في غيرها في لزوم الدم. وأراد بالرقبة وما عطف عليها ما عدا الرأس واللحية كالصدر والساق والعانة كالرقبة لكن في فتاوى قاضيخان وفي حلق العانة دم إن كان الشعر كثيراً ! فشرط كثرة الشعرة فصار الحاصل أن فيما عدا الرأس واللحية إن حلق عضواً كاملاً فعليه دم، وإن كان أقل فعليه صدقة . المبسوط : ومتى حلق عضواً مقصوداً بالحلق فعليه دم وإن حلق ما ليس بمقصود فصدقة : ثم قال: ومما ليس بمقصود حلق الصدر والساق ورجحه في فتح القدير، ودفع ما في الهداية أنه مقصود بطريق التنور بأن القصد إلى حلقهما إنما هو من في ضمن غيرهما إذ ليست العادة الساق وحده بل تنوير المجموع من الصلب إلى القدم فكان بعض المقصود بالحلق، فالحق أن يجب كل منهما الصدقة ا هـ . فعلى هذا فالتقييد بالرقبه وما عطف عليه للاحتراز عن الصدر والساق بما ليس بمقصود وأطلق في المحجمة وهو مقيد بما إذا كان الحلق لهذا الموضع وسيلة إلى الحجامة، فلو حلقها ولم يحتجم لزمه صدقة لأنه غير مقصود كما في فتح السابقة من قوله : وكذا لو قتل قملة على غيره فإنها مستحقة الأمن تأمل. وأما لو قلم أظافير غيره فإن حكمه حكم الحلق . قال في شرح اللباب وفي المحيط وقاضيخان وجوامع الفقه إذا قص المحرم أظافير غيره فحكمه كحكم الحلق وعن محمد رواية أنه لا شيء عليه. وفي البدائع : وإن قلم المحرم أظافير حلال أو حلال أظافير محرم فحكمه كحكم الحلق ا هـ . وفي أظافير حلال أو كذا في نسخة، وفي عامة النسخ والحلق وهو تحريف والصواب الأولى قوله: (وأطلق في المحجمة إلى قوله كما في فتح القدير ) قال في النهر : لم أجده في نسختي منه ا هـ . وكأنه نظر في غير محله أو من نسخته ونصه قوله لأنه لا يتوسل إلى المقصود إلا به يفيد أنه إذا لم تترتب الحجامة على موضع المحاجم لا يجب الدم لأنه أفاد أن كونه مقصوداً إنما هو للتوسل به إلى الحجامة فإذا لم تعقبه البحر الرائق ج٣/ ٢٥ سقط
And the apparent meaning of his speech: it is necessary to shave the entire neck, armpit, and cupping site for the obligation of blood (dam) for each of them. So if anything from the neck or armpit remains, he does not owe blood even if it is a little. For this reason al-Asbijabi said: If he shaves most of one armpit, sadaqah is obligatory. So according to this, what is stated in al-Muhit that most of the neck is like the whole in obligating blood, and the principle that every organ has a counterpart in the body, its majority does not stand in for the whole, and every organ that has no counterpart in the body like the neck, its majority does stand in for the whole, and what is in Fatawa Qadi Khan that in the armpit, if the hair is thick, a quarter is considered for the obligation of blood, otherwise most [is considered], is weak because no one has restricted shaving a quarter to other than the beard and head, so there is no complete benefit. For this reason the commentator said: Then the quarter of these organs is not considered as the whole because the custom has not been to limit to a part in these organs, so shaving a part is not a complete benefit. Therefore, if he shaves most of the armpit, nothing is obligatory but sadaqah, unlike the head and beard. So the madhhab is what is in the book: considering a quarter in the head and beard, and the whole in other than them for the obligation of blood. And by 'neck' and what is joined to it, he means other than the head and beard, such as the chest, leg, and pubic area like the neck. But in Fatawa Qadi Khan, for shaving the pubic area, blood is required if the hair is thick. So he conditions thick hair. The summary is that for other than the head and beard, if he shaves a complete organ, he owes blood; if less, he owes sadaqah. Al-Mabsut: Whenever he shaves an organ that is intended (maqsud) for shaving, he owes blood; if he shaves what is not intended, sadaqah. Then he said: Among what is not intended is shaving the chest and leg. And this was preferred in Fath al-Qadir, and he refuted what is in al-Hidayah that it is intended by way of tanwir (hair removal for grooming) because the intention to shave them is only incidental to other things, since custom is not to shave the leg alone, but to shave the entire area from the back to the foot, so it is part of the intended shaving. The correct view is that each of them requires sadaqah. So according to this, the restriction to the neck and what is joined to it is to exclude the chest and leg as not intended. And the cupping site is mentioned absolutely, but it is restricted to when shaving that area is a means to cupping. So if he shaves it without cupping, he owes sadaqah because it is not intended, as in Fath al-Qadir from his statement: 'And similarly, if he kills a louse on another, it is entitled to safety.' Reflect. As for trimming the nails of another, its ruling is like that of shaving. In Sharh al-Lubab, al-Muhit, Qadi Khan, and Jami' al-Fiqh: if a muhrim cuts the nails of another, its ruling is like that of shaving. From Muhammad, there is a narration that nothing is due on him. In al-Bada'i': if a muhrim cuts the nails of a non-muhrim, or a non-muhrim cuts the nails of a muhrim, its ruling is like that of shaving. And in [the case of] nails of a non-muhrim? Or as in some copies, and in most copies 'shaving' is mentioned but that is a distortion; the correct is the first. His statement: (And he used absolutely for the cupping site up to his statement 'as in Fath al-Qadir') said in al-Nahr: I did not find it in my copy of it. It seems he looked elsewhere or from his copy. And its text: 'because the intended act cannot be reached except by it' indicates that if cupping does not follow from the cupping site, blood is not obligatory because it being intended is only as a means to cupping. So if it is not followed by cupping, then [the ruling is as mentioned]. Al-Bahr al-Raiq, vol. 3, p. 25, missing.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on jinaayat (violations) during ihram, focusing on body parts other than the head and beard. The commentator explains that for the neck, armpit, and cupping site (mahajim), the obligation of blood (dam) only arises if the entire area is shaved. If any part remains, even if the shaved portion is most, only sadaqah is due. This is a key distinction from the head and beard, where a quarter triggers blood. The reason is that customarily, people do not shave only part of these areas; shaving them for benefit is only complete when the entire area is shaved. For the armpit, there is a weak view in Qadi Khan's Fatawa that if the hair is thick, a quarter suffices for blood, but the commentator dismisses this, insisting that the full organ must be shaved. For the chest and leg, they are considered 'not intended' for shaving (ghayr maqsud), meaning people do not shave them independently; rather, they are shaved as part of a larger grooming (tanwir). Therefore, shaving them only requires sadaqah, not blood. The cupping site is intended only when used for cupping; if shaved without cupping, it is not intended, and sadaqah is due. The passage then addresses cutting nails (taqlid al-azafir) of another person. The majority view (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad in a narration) equates it to shaving: if a muhrim cuts another's nails, the ruling is the same as shaving hair. However, a narration from Muhammad states that nothing is due. The commentator notes a textual variant where 'shaving' (al-halq) is mentioned but is likely a distortion; the correct text refers to nails. Finally, there is a note that in al-Bahr al-Raiq, the section on cupping site from Fath al-Qadir was missing in some copies, causing confusion.

Key Terms
مقصود (maqsud): Intended organ for shaving - an area that people customarily shave for its own sake (like head/beard) or as a means to an end (like cupping site for cupping).
تنوير (tanwir): The practice of removing body hair from the entire area from navel to knees, often including legs and pubic area.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a muhrim shaves less than the entire armpit during ihram, what compensation is due according to the relied-upon Hanafi position?
A) Dam (blood)
B) Sadaqah (charity)
C) Nothing
D) A full sacrificial animal

Key Takeaway
For non-head/beard body parts, only complete shaving of an intended organ triggers dam; all other cases require sadaqah.

Liability of a Coerced Muhrim for Shaving
Ruling on coerced shaving and dam liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on who must offer the dam when a muhrim is coerced into shaving, and explain why the shaver is not liable.

Core Idea
A coerced muhrim owes dam because he performs the act; the shaver has no liability.

In the Hanafi school, coercion (ikrah) does not remove the obligation of compensation for violating the sanctity of ihram. This lesson examines the specific case of a muhrim forced to shave his head, clarifying that the coerced person himself must offer a dam, not the one who shaves him. This ruling is based on the principle that the coerced person remains the agent of the prohibited act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is shaving the head of a muhrim under coercion. The ruling is that dam (a sacrificial animal) is wajib on the coerced muhrim, not on the shaver.
The passage states: 'إذا كان المحلوق رأسه مكرهاً وجب الدم عليه' (if the one whose head is shaved is coerced, dam is due on him).
2
Locate the implied proof
The passage does not quote a specific dalil but implies the basis: the coerced muhrim still performs the action of being shaved, and the sanctity of ihram is violated by the shaving itself. The shaver is merely an instrument.
This is consistent with the Hanafi rule that ikrah does not nullify the act's legal effect for compensation purposes.
3
Note the consequence of no recourse
The coerced muhrim has no right to seek compensation from the shaver for the dam he owes. This is because the shaver is not considered the liable party.
The text explicitly says: 'ولا له رجوع على الحالق' (and he has no recourse against the shaver).
4
Distinguish from other schools
Other madhahib may hold the coercer or shaver liable, but the Hanafi position places responsibility on the coerced person himself.
This is a point of ikhtilaf that affects practical fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا كان المحلوق رأسه مكرهاً وجب الدم عليه ولا له رجوع على الحالق عندنا كذا في المحيط. وظاهر كلامه أنه لا بد من حلق جميع الرقبة والإبط والمحجمة في لزوم الدم بكل منهم، فلو بقي من الرقبة أو الإبط شيء لا يلزمه دم وإن كان قليلاً ولهذا قال الأسبيجابي : ولو حلق من أحد الإبطين أكثره وجبت الصدقة. فعلى هذا فما صرح به من المحيط من أن الأكثر من الرقبة كالكل في لزوم الدم وأن الأصل أن كل عضو له نظير في البدن لا يقوم أكثره مقام كله وكل عضو لا نظير له في البدن كالرقبة يقوم أكثره مقام كله وما في فتاوى قاضيخان من أن في الإبط إذا كان كثير الشعر يعتبر فيه الربع لوجوب الدم وإلا فالأكثر ضعيف لأنه لم يقيد أحد حلق ربع غير اللحية والرأس فليس فيه ارتفاق كامل، ولهذا قال الشارح: ثم الربع من هذه الأعضاء لا يعتبر بالكل لأن العادة لم تجر في هذه الأعضاء بالاقتصار على البعض فلا يكون حلق البعض ارتفاقاً كاملاً حتى لو حلق أكثر الإبط لا يجب عليه إلا صدقة بخلاف الرأس واللحية ! فالمذهب ما في الكتاب من اعتبار الربع في الرأس واللحية والكل في غيرها في لزوم الدم.
And if the one whose head is shaved is coerced, then the dam is obligatory upon him, and he has no recourse against the shaver according to us. This is stated in al-Muhit. And his apparent statement indicates that it is necessary to shave the entire neck, armpit, and cupping place for the dam to be due for each of them. If any part of the neck or armpit remains, no dam is due upon him even if it is small. For this reason, al-Asbijabi said: 'If he shaved most of one armpit, sadaqah is obligatory.' Based on this, what he explicitly stated in al-Muhit that the majority of the neck is like the whole in causing dam, and that the principle is that every limb that has a counterpart in the body, its majority does not stand in place of the whole; and every limb that has no counterpart in the body like the neck, its majority stands in place of the whole. And what is in the Fatawa of Qadikhan, that in the armpit if the hair is abundant, one-quarter is considered for the obligation of dam, otherwise the majority is weak, because no one restricted shaving a quarter to other than the beard and head, so there is no complete benefit. For this reason, the commentator said: 'Then the quarter from these limbs is not considered equivalent to the whole because custom has not established restricting to part in these limbs, so shaving part is not a complete benefit, even if he shaves most of the armpit, only sadaqah is due upon him, unlike the head and beard.' So the madhhab is what is in the book: consideration of the quarter in the head and beard, and the whole in others for the obligation of dam.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof type. It discusses two issues: (1) if a muhrim is coerced into having his head shaved, the dam for shaving is due on the coerced person himself, not on the one who shaves him (this is the Hanafi position); (2) the conditions for dam to be due when shaving specific body parts — neck, armpit, and the cupping place (mahjamah). The rule is that for limbs that have a counterpart in the body (like armpits, which come in pairs), shaving more than half does not suffice; the entire limb must be shaved. For limbs without a counterpart (like the neck), shaving the majority counts as the whole. However, Qadikhan's view that the armpit requires only a quarter if the hair is abundant is considered weak. The relied-upon view (madhhab) is that for the head and beard, shaving a quarter obligates dam; for all other limbs, the whole limb must be shaved. The reasoning (ta'lil) is based on custom (urf): people do not customarily shave only part of these limbs for benefit, so partial shaving does not constitute complete relief (irtifaq) to warrant dam. This passage is from the commentary of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, expanding on the rulings of shaving during ihram.

Key Terms
محلوق (mahlūq): The person whose head is shaved (active participle passive sense).
مكره (mukrah): One who is coerced into an action under threat.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (sheep or goat) required as a penalty for leaving a wajib or committing a prohibited act during ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The coerced muhrim
B) The person who shaved him
C) Both must offer a dam
D) No dam is required

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, coercion does not remove the obligation of dam for shaving during ihram; the coerced muhrim himself must offer the sacrifice.

Majority vs. Whole Limbs for Shaving During Ihram
Principle of majority vs. whole limbs for shaving during ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that for a limb without a counterpart (e.g., neck), shaving the majority suffices for dam; for a limb with a counterpart (e.g., armpit), the whole must be shaved; and distinguish the quarter rule for head/beard.

Core Idea
Limbs without counterpart: majority = whole; paired limbs: only whole obligates dam.

The Hanafi school has established precise rules for the amount of shaving required to incur dam during ihram. The principle hinges on whether the limb has a counterpart in the body. For limbs like the neck (with no pair), shaving the majority is treated like shaving the whole. For limbs like the armpit (which come in pairs), only shaving the entire limb triggers dam. Additionally, the head and beard have a special rule: shaving a quarter suffices. This lesson unpacks these distinctions and the reasoning based on custom (urf) and benefit (irtifaq).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of limbs
Limbs are divided into those with a counterpart (like armpits, eyebrows) and those without (like the neck, the cupping place on the back). The ruling differs between them.
The passage explicitly states: 'كل عضو له نظير في البدن لا يقوم أكثره مقام كله وكل عضو لا نظير له في البدن كالرقبة يقوم أكثره مقام كله'.
2
Apply the principle to the neck and armpit examples
For the neck (no counterpart), shaving the majority counts as the whole and obligates dam. For the armpit (has a counterpart), only shaving the entire armpit obligates dam; the majority does not suffice.
Al-Asbijabi's statement is quoted: if he shaves most of one armpit, only sadaqah (charity) is due, not dam.
3
Examine the quarter rule for head and beard
The head and beard are exceptions: due to widespread custom (urf) of shaving only part for benefit, shaving a quarter of the head or beard obligates dam.
The commentator says: 'الربع يعتبر في الرأس واللحية' because custom has established that partial shaving provides complete benefit (irtifaq) for these areas.
4
Evaluate Qadikhan's view on the armpit
Qadikhan proposed that if armpit hair is abundant, shaving a quarter should obligate dam by analogy with the head. This view is rejected because custom does not support partial shaving of the armpit for benefit.
The passage calls this view 'ضعيف' (weak) and affirms the madhhab: quarter for head/beard, whole for all other limbs.
5
Synthesize the complete rule
The mufta bihi: Shaving a quarter of the head or beard obligates dam. Shaving the majority of a limb without a counterpart (neck, cupping place) obligates dam. Shaving any amount less than the whole of a limb with a counterpart obligates only sadaqah (if the majority) or nothing (if less than majority).
This is the relied-upon position in the book (al-Muhit and Kanz al-Daqaiq).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And if the one whose head is shaved is coerced, then the dam is obligatory upon him, and he has no recourse against the shaver according to us. This is stated in al-Muhit. This passage is a ruling-with-proof type. Key Terms
رقبة (raqabah): The neck area, including the front and sides; used as an example of a limb without a counterpart.
إبط (ibṭ): Armpit; a limb with a counterpart (two armpits).
محجمة (maḥjamah): The place where cupping (hijamah) is performed, typically on the back or neck; treated as a limb that may be intended for shaving if it is a means to cupping.
ارتفاق (irtifāq): Benefit or relief achieved by removing hair; used to justify the threshold for compensation.

Checkpoint

Dam vs. Sadaqah: Maqsud and Ghayr Maqsud Limbs in Ihram
Ruling on dam vs sadaqah based on limb type

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between limbs that are maqsud and ghayr maqsud and apply the correct ruling (dam or sadaqah) for shaving during ihram.

Core Idea
Shaving a limb intended for shaving requires dam; shaving what is not intended requires sadaqah, based on custom.

Shaving or removing hair during ihram is a prohibited act that requires compensation, but the amount depends on which body part is shaved and the intention. The Hanafi school categorizes limbs as 'maqsud' (customarily shaved for their own sake, like the head and beard) and 'ghayr maqsud' (not customarily shaved alone, like the chest or calf). This lesson unpacks the principle from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, including the dispute about whether shaving the chest or calf as part of full body hair removal (tanwir) makes them maqsud, and the special case of shaving for cupping.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Principle
From the passage, extract the ruling from al-Mabsut: 'Whenever he shaves a limb that is intended for shaving, dam is due; if he shaves what is not intended, sadaqah.' Understand that 'intended' is determined by custom (urf).
This is a qiyas-based rule; the proof is the analogy to the head (maqsud) and the principle of lesser compensation for lesser violations.
2
Apply the Principle to Specific Limbs
Chest and calf are explicitly mentioned as ghayr maqsud, so shaving them alone requires sadaqah. However, note the counter-view from al-Hidayah that they become maqsud when done as part of tanwir (full body hair removal). Follow the preferred view (Fath al-Qadir) that each limb is still ghayr maqsud and requires sadaqah.
The passage sides with Fath al-Qadir: 'al-ḥaqqu an yajiba kullun minhumā al-ṣadaqah' – the correct view is that each requires sadaqah.
3
Analyze the Cupping Exception
Shaving the cupping site (mahjamah) is normally ghayr maqsud, but if the shaving is a means to cupping, it becomes maqsud (requiring dam). If cupping does not follow, the shaving reverts to ghayr maqsud and only sadaqah is due. This shows the ruling depends on actual intention and outcome.
The passage states: 'if he shaves it and does not cup, sadaqah is due because it is not intended.'
4
Note the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
There is a narration from Imam Muhammad that cutting a muhrim's nails (analogous to shaving) requires nothing. The preferred view treats it like shaving, so if it is a means to something else, it may incur sadaqah. Also, the disagreement with al-Hidayah on chest/calf shows the spectrum of opinions within the school.
The passage cites al-Bada'i' treating nail cutting like shaving, but notes the riwayah from Muhammad.

Source Text
