And he intended by 'neck' and what is joined to it other than the head and beard, like the chest, calf, and pubic area is like the neck. However, in the Fatawa of Qadikhan, there is a ruling that shaving the pubic area requires dam if the hair is abundant — so he conditioned abundance. So the conclusion is that for other than the head and beard, if he shaves an entire limb, dam is due; if less, sadaqah. In al-Mabsut: 'Whenever he shaves a limb that is intended for shaving, dam is due; if he shaves what is not intended, sadaqah.' Then he said: 'Among what is not intended is shaving the chest and calf.' And he preferred this in Fath al-Qadir, rebutting what is in al-Hidayah that it is intended by way of 'tanwir' (body hair removal), because the intention to shave them is subsumed under other parts — it is not custom to shave the calf alone, but rather to remove hair from the whole area from the spine to the foot, so it is part of the intended shaving. The correct view is that each requires sadaqah. Based on this, the restriction to neck and what is joined with it is to exclude the chest and calf as not intended. And he spoke absolutely about the cupping place, but it is restricted to when shaving that spot is a means to cupping. If he shaves it and does not cup, sadaqah is due because it is not intended, as in the previous passage from Fath al-Qadir: 'And likewise if he kills a louse on someone else, for it is entitled to security [from ihram] — reflect.' And as for cutting another's nails, its ruling is like that of shaving. It is stated in Sharh al-Lubab, al-Muhit, Qadikhan, and Jami' al-Fiqh: If a muhrim cuts another's nails, its ruling is like that of shaving. From Muhammad (al-Shaybani) there is a narration that nothing is due. And in al-Bada'i': 'If a muhrim cuts...' — his statement: (the correct view is that) or a non-muhrim cuts a muhrim's nails, its ruling is like that of shaving. (Page 18 continues:) In Fath al-Qadir: 'And know that scattered parts are combined in shaving just as in perfume.' And in al-Hidayah, shaving the armpits is mentioned here, but in the original (text) plucking is the sunnah. And in al-Nihayah: 'As for the pubic area, the sunnah is to shave it due to the hadith: Ten from the sunnah, among them is istihdad (shaving pubic hair wit...' — (the text continues with commentary on the cupping place). The statement in Fath al-Qadir: 'He said: because one cannot reach the intended except through it, so if cupping does not follow, dam is not due, because being intended was only as a means to cupping, so if cupping does not follow, it did not become a means and thus was not intended, so only sadaqah is due.' The expression of Sharh al-Kanz is clear in this, where he said in its evidence: 'And because it is little, it does not obligate dam, just as if he shaves it without cupping.' And in its evidence: 'Shaving for one who cups is intended, and that is considered, unlike shaving for other purposes.' Verbally.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof type, treating the distinction between body parts that are 'maqsud' (intended for shaving) and those that are 'ghayr maqsud' (not intended). It begins by summarizing the previous rule: for limbs other than head and beard, shaving the entire limb requires dam; less requires sadaqah. It then cites al-Mabsut's general principle: shaving a limb that is customarily shaved (like beard or head) requires dam; shaving a limb not customarily shaved requires sadaqah. The chest (sadr) and calf (saq) are given as examples of ghayr maqsud, but there is a disagreement with al-Hidayah, which considered them maqsud as part of full body hair removal (tanwir). The commentator sides with Fath al-Qadir that shaving these alone requires only sadaqah. The cupping place (mahjamah) is treated as maqsud only if the shaving is a means to cupping; otherwise, it is ghayr maqsud. Similarly, cutting nails of another muhrim is treated like shaving: if it is a means to something else (like grooming), it may incur sadaqah unless it is part of a full haircut? According to Muhammad, there is a narration that nothing is due. The passage further clarifies that if cupping does not actually follow the shaving, then the shaving was not a means and only sadaqah is required. This follows the principle that the ruling is based on the actual intention and customary practice.

Key Terms
مقصود بالحلق (maqsūd bil-ḥalq): A body part that is customarily shaved for its own sake (e.g., head, beard).
صدقة (ṣadaqah): A charitable payment (usually half a sa' or similar) required as compensation for minor violations during ihram.
تنوير (tanwīr): Removal of body hair (from chest, legs, etc.) using depilatory agents or shaving, often done as part of grooming.
أظافير (aẓāfīr): Fingernails (plural of zufr). Cutting nails of another muhrim is analogous to shaving hair.
حجامة (ḥijāmah): Cupping therapy; shaving the site is a preparatory act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Dam
B) Sadaqah
C) Nothing
D) Fidyah

Key Takeaway
The compensation for shaving during ihram depends on whether the limb is maqsud (intended) or ghayr maqsud, determined by custom: dam for maqsud, sadaqah for ghayr maqsud.

Shaving the Mustache in Ihram: Three Hanafi Opinions
Intra-Hanafi dispute on mustache shaving penalty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi opinions on shaving the mustache during ihram and identify the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
Shaving the mustache in ihram triggers sadaqah in the relied-upon Hanafi view, not a full dam.

Shaving the mustache during ihram is a common action that raises a question: does it require the same penalty as shaving the head? The Hanafi school has three distinct opinions on this, ranging from sadaqah (the madhhab) to dam. This lesson unpacks these opinions, their proofs, and the practical fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The act is shaving the mustache (or part of it) while in ihram. The dispute is about the required compensation: sadaqah, proportional sadaqah, or dam.
The mustache is considered part of the beard in Hanafi fiqh.
2
State the madhhab (first opinion)
The relied-upon view is that sadaqah is obligatory, whether the entire mustache or part is shaved. It is based on the mustache being a small part of the beard.
Supported by al-Hakim al-Shahid, al-Mabsut, and Ghayat al-Bayan.
3
Explain the proportional approach (second opinion)
Some scholars, as mentioned in al-Hidayah, say sadaqah is proportional: measure the mustache as a fraction of a quarter of the beard, then pay that fraction of the value of a sheep.
Fath al-Qadir refines: the proportion should be based on the total beard plus mustache together.
4
Explain the dam opinion (third opinion)
A third view holds that shaving the mustache requires a full dam because it is intentionally shaved (e.g., by Sufis).
This opinion is considered weak and not mufta bihi.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical consequence
The mufta bihi is the first opinion: sadaqah. Thus, a muhrim who shaves his mustache owes sadaqah, not dam.
The tarjih is based on the authority of al-Hakim al-Shahid and the compilations of Imam Muhammad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وفي أخذ شاربه حكومة عدل) مخالف لما أفاده أولاً بقوله «وإلا تصدق» فإن الشارب بعض اللحية وهو إذاكان أقل من الربع ففيه الصدقة ومبني على ضعيف وهو قول محمد في تطييب بعض العضو حيث قال : يجب بقدره من الدم، وأما المذهب فوجوب الصدقة. فالحاصل كما في المحيط أن في حلق الشارب ثلاثة أقوال: المذهب وجوب الصدقة كما ذكره في الكافي للحاكم الشهيد الذي هو جمع كلام محمد وصححه في غاية البيان والمبسوط لأنه تبع للحية وهو قليل لأنه عضو صغير، وسواء حلقه كله أو بعضه. والقول الثاني ما ذكره في الكتاب تبعاً لما في الهداية أنه ينظر إلى الشارب كم يكون من ربع اللحية الصدقة بقدره حتى لو كان مثل ربع ربعها لزمه ربع قيمة الشاة أو ثمنها فثمنها . وفي فتح القدير والواجب أن ينظر إلى نسبة المأخوذ من ربع اللحية معتبراً معها الشارب كما يفيده ما في المبسوط من كون الشارب طرفاً من اللحية هو معها عضوا واحد لا أنه ينسب إلى ربع اللحية غير معتبر الشارب معها، فعلى هذا إنما يجب ربع قيمة الشاة إذا بلغ المأخوذ من الشارب ربع المجموع من اللحية مع الشارب لا دونه ا هـ . القول الثالث لزوم الدم يحلقه لأنه مقصود بالحلق يفعله الصوفية ،وغيرهم، وقد ظن صاحب الهداية من تعبير محمد في الجامع الصغير هنا بالأخذ أن السنة قص الشارب لا حلقه رداً على الطحاوي القائل بسنية الحلق.
His statement: (And in taking his mustache, [there is] a just estimation) contradicts what he first indicated by his statement 'otherwise he gives sadaqah'. Indeed, the mustache is part of the beard, and if it is less than a quarter, then sadaqah is due. But it is based on a weak view, which is the statement of Muhammad regarding perfuming a part of a limb, where he said: proportional dam is due. But the madhhab is obligation of sadaqah. So the conclusion, as in al-Muhit, is that there are three opinions regarding shaving the mustache: The madhhab is obligation of sadaqah, as mentioned in al-Kafi by al-Hakim al-Shahid, which collects the statements of Muhammad, and he authenticated it in Ghayat al-Bayan and al-Mabsut, because it follows the beard and it is little, being a small limb; whether he shaves all of it or part of it. The second opinion is what is mentioned in the book following al-Hidayah: that one looks at how much of the quarter of the beard the mustache is, and sadaqah is proportional; even if it is like a quarter of a quarter, he owes a quarter of the value of a sheep or an eighth of it. In Fath al-Qadir, the obligation is to look at the proportion taken from the quarter of the beard, considering the mustache along with it, as is indicated in al-Mabsut that the mustache is a part of the beard and together they are one limb — not that it is proportioned to the quarter of the beard without considering the mustache. Therefore, the quarter of the value of a sheep is only due if what is taken from the mustache reaches a quarter of the total of beard and mustache together, not less. The third opinion: obligation of dam, because it is intended for shaving, and it is done by Sufis and others. The author of al-Hidayah thought from Muhammad's expression 'akhdh' (taking) in al-Jami' al-Saghir that the sunnah is to trim (qass) the mustache, not shave, as a rebuttal to al-Tahawi who said shaving is sunnah.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the ruling for shaving the mustache during ihram. It presents three opinions within the Hanafi school. The first opinion, considered the madhhab (relied-upon view), is that sadaqah is obligatory, whether one shaves the entire mustache or part of it, because the mustache is part of the beard and is small. This is based on the principle that shaving a small part of a limb does not warrant full dam. The second opinion, found in al-Hidayah, uses a proportional calculation: the mustache is measured as a fraction of a quarter of the beard, and sadaqah is due proportionally. For example, if the mustache is one-eighth of the quarter, one-eighth of the value of a sheep is due. Fath al-Qadir refines this: the proportion should be based on the total beard plus mustache together, not just the beard. The third opinion holds that shaving the mustache obligates a full dam because it is considered 'maqsud' (intended) for shaving, especially among Sufis who shave it completely. The author also notes that al-Hidayah's use of the word 'akhdh' (taking) in the hadith implies trimming rather than shaving, in response to al-Tahawi's view that shaving is sunnah. The passage highlights the complexity of applying general principles to specific body parts.

Key Terms
شارب (shārib): Mustache; considered part of the beard in fiqh.
حكومة عدل (ḥukūmatu 'adl): A just estimation of value or compensation; in fiqh, an expert assessment.
قص (qaṣṣ): Trimming (of hair or nails); used for mustache trimming.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi ruling for a muhrim who shaves his entire mustache?
A) Dam
B) Sadaqah
C) Proportional sadaqah based on quarter of beard
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
Shaving the mustache during ihram requires sadaqah (not dam) in the mufta bihi Hanafi view, because the mustache is part of the beard and is considered a small amount.

Penalty for a Muhrim Shaving His Mustache: Three Intra-Hanafi Opinions
Analyzing three Hanafi opinions on penalty for a Muhrim shaving mustache

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi opinions on the penalty for a Muhrim who shaves his mustache and identify the mufta bihi position with its evidence.

Core Idea
Shaving a small part of the beard (mustache) in Ihram requires charity, not blood.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq tackles an intra-Hanafi dispute: what penalty does a Muhrim incur for shaving his mustache? Is it charity, proportional charity, or blood? The answer hinges on whether the mustache is a trivial part of the beard and whether shaving is an intentional violation. By examining the three opinions and their proofs, you will learn to navigate similar disputes within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the three opinions
Locate where the text states the three views: (1) charity for any amount (madhhab), (2) proportional charity based on a quarter of the beard, (3) blood because shaving is deliberate.
The mustache is considered part of the beard in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Examine the evidence for each opinion
For opinion 1: mustache is small, so charity suffices. For opinion 2: ratio of mustache to beard determines value. For opinion 3: shaving is an intentional act analogous to cupping, requiring blood.
The hadith 'Ahfu al-shawarib' is interpreted as hyperbole in cutting.
3
Understand the tarjih (preference) mechanism
The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq favours the madhhab (opinion 1) because it aligns with Zahir al-Riwayah and the generality of 'taking' in Imam Muhammad's wording.
Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah leans toward opinion 2, but the mufta bihi is opinion 1.
4
Apply the ruling to a concrete scenario
If a Muhrim shaves his entire mustache (a small amount), the mufta bihi is charity (sadaqah). If he shaves a large portion including part of the beard, blood may be due.
The amount removed is measured relative to a quarter of the full beard.

الصوفية ،وغيرهم، وقد ظن صاحب الهداية من تعبير محمد في الجامع الصغير هنا بالأخذ أن السنة قص الشارب لا حلقه رداً على الطحاوي القائل بسنية الحلق فيلزمه من الجحامة لم يقع وسيلة فلم يكن مقصوداً فلا تجب إلا الصدقة وعبارة شرح الكنز واضحة في ذلك حيث قال في دليلهما ولأنه قليل فلا يوجب الدم كما إذا حلقه بغير الحجامة، وفي دليله أن حلقه لمن يحتجم مقصود وهو المعتبر بخلاف الحلق لغيرها . ا هـ بحروفه قوله : (وفي النهاية وأما العانة الخ) اختلف في العانة التي يسن حلقها، فالمشهور الذي عليه الجمهور أنه ما حول ذكر الرجل وفرج المرأة من الشعر، وقيل يسن حلق جميع ما على القبل والدبر وحولهما. ويحصل أصل السنة بأي وجه كان من الحلق والقص والنتف واستعمال النورة إذ المقصود حصول النظافة إلا أن الأحسن في هذه السنة الحلق بالموسى لأنه أنظف . كذا في حاشية نوح أفندي قوله : (رداً على الطحاوي الخ) حيث قال : القص حسن وتفسيره أن يقص حتى ينتقص عن الإطار وهو بكسر الهمزة لمتقي الجلدة واللحم الشفة، وكلام المصنف أي صاحب الهداية على أن يحاذيه ثم قال الطحاوي: والحلق أحسن وهذا (1) رواه البخاري في كتاب الاستئذان باب .٥١ ومسلم في كتاب الطهارة حديث ٤٩. وأبو داود في كتاب الترجل باب ٤٩. والترمذي في كتاب الأدب باب ١٤ والنسائي في كتاب الطهارة باب ٦،٨. وأحمد في مسنده (٢٢٩/٢). قوله : (وليس كما ظن لأن محمداً لم يقصد هنا بيان السنة وإنما قصد بيان حكم هذه الجناية بإزالة الشعر بأي طريق كان ولهذا ذكر الحلق في الإبط واختار في الهداية سنية النتف لا الحلق ولأن الأخذ أعم من الحلق لأن الحلق أخذ وليس القص متبادراً من الأخذ والوارد في الصحيحين «أحفوا الشوارب واعفوا اللحى»(۱) وهو المبالغة في القطع، فبأي شيء حصل حصل المقصود غير أنه بالحلق بالموسى أيسر منه بالقصة فلذا قال الطحاوي: الحلق أحسن من القص وقد يكون مثله بسبب بعض الآلات الخاصة بقص الشارب، وأما ذكر القص في بعض الأحاديث فالمراد منه المبالغة في الاستئصال وبما قررناه اندفع ما في البدائع من أن الصحيح أن السنة فيه القص وإعفاء اللحية تركها حتى تكث وتكثر والسنة قدر القبضة فما زاد قطعه .
This is from the Book of Hajj, Chapter of Offenses. And in al-Hidayah, shaving the armpits is mentioned here, but in the original, plucking is the sunnah. And in al-Nihayah: As for the pubic area, the sunnah is to shave it because it is mentioned in the hadith: 'Ten are from the sunnah, including shaving the pubic area' (istihdad), and its explanation is shaving the pubic area with iron. His statement: 'And in taking his mustache, a just assessment (hukumat 'adl) is (given)' contradicts what he first stated with his saying 'otherwise he gives charity'—for the mustache is part of the beard. And if it is less than a quarter, there is charity in it, and it is based on a weak (view), which is the saying of Muhammad regarding perfuming part of a limb, where he said: an amount of blood is due commensurate with it. But the madhhab is the obligation of charity. The conclusion as in al-Muhit is that there are three opinions regarding shaving the mustache: The madhhab: charity is obligatory, as mentioned in al-Kafi by al-Hakim al-Shahid, which is a compilation of Muhammad's statements and validated in Ghayat al-Bayan and al-Mabsut, because it is subject to the beard and it is small, a small organ—and whether he shaves all of it or some of it. The second opinion: what is mentioned in the book following al-Hidayah: one looks at how much the mustache is of a quarter of the beard, and charity is due proportionally—so if it is like a quarter of a quarter, he owes a quarter of the value of a sheep or an eighth of that. In Fath al-Qadir: the obligation is to look at the proportion of what is taken from the quarter of the beard, considering the mustache along with it, as indicated in al-Mabsut that the mustache is an extension of the beard and with it one single organ, not that it is measured against the quarter of the beard without considering the mustache. According to this, a quarter of the value of a sheep is only due if what is taken from the mustache reaches a quarter of the total of the beard together with the mustache, not less. The third opinion: blood is due from shaving it because it is intended by shaving—Sufis and others do it. And the author of al-Hidayah thought from Muhammad's expression in al-Jami' al-Saghir here with 'taking' that the sunnah is cutting the mustache, not shaving it, as a refutation of al-Tahawi who said the sunnah is shaving. So he is obligated... from cupping... it did not occur as a means, so it was not intended, so only charity is due. And the wording of Sharh al-Kanz is clear in that, where it said in its proof: 'Because it is little, so it does not require blood, as when he shaves it without cupping.' And in its proof: that shaving it for one who is cupping is intended, and it is what matters, unlike shaving for other reasons.' End quote. His statement: 'In al-Nihayah: As for the pubic area...' There is a difference of opinion about the pubic area that is sunnah to shave. The well-known (view) with the majority is that it is the hair around the male's penis and the female's vulva. And it is said that it is sunnah to shave all the hair on the front and back and around them. The basic sunnah is achieved by any means—shaving, cutting, plucking, or using depilatory lotion—since the aim is cleanliness, except that the best for this sunnah is shaving with a razor because it is cleaner. This is from the marginalia of Nuh Afandi. His statement: 'Refuting al-Tahawi...' where he said: 'Cutting is good' and its explanation is that one cuts until it goes below the rim (itar)—with a kasra on the hamza—which is the meeting point of the skin and flesh of the lip. And the speech of the author (i.e., the author of al-Hidayah) is that it should align with it. Then al-Tahawi said: 'Shaving is better.' And this is narrated by al-Bukhari in the Book of Permission, chapter 51; Muslim in the Book of Purity, hadith 49; Abu Dawud in the Book of Combing, chapter 49; al-Tirmidhi in the Book of Manners, chapter 14; al-Nasa'i in the Book of Purity, chapter 6,8; and Ahmad in his Musnad (2/229). His statement: 'It is not as he thought, because Muhammad did not intend here to explain the sunnah; rather, he intended to explain the ruling of this offense of removing hair by any method. That is why he mentioned shaving in the armpits, and al-Hidayah chose the sunnah of plucking, not shaving. And because 'taking' is more general than shaving, for shaving is a taking, but cutting is not readily understood from 'taking'. And what is reported in the two Sahihs: 'Trim the mustaches and let the beards grow' is hyperbole in cutting. So whatever achieves this, the purpose is achieved, except that shaving with a razor is easier than with scissors. Therefore al-Tahawi said: 'Shaving is better than cutting,' and sometimes it is similar due to some special instruments for cutting the mustache. As for mentioning cutting in some hadiths, the intent is hyperbole in removal. And with what we have established, what is in al-Bada'i' is refuted—that the correct (view) is that the sunnah is cutting. And letting the beard grow means leaving it until it becomes thick and abundant, and the sunnah is a handful, so any excess is cut.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is a commentary on the ruling for a Muhrim (one in Ihram) who shaves his mustache. It is an intra-Hanafi dispute because there are three opinions within the school. The author begins by noting that in al-Hidayah, the armpits are mentioned as being shaved, but the original ruling is that plucking is sunnah. Then he discusses the pubic area, where shaving is sunnah based on the hadith listing ten sunnan. Then the main issue: the ruling for a Muhrim shaving his mustache. The text states that the mustache is part of the beard, and the penalty depends on the amount removed. Three opinions are presented: (1) The madhhab: charity is obligatory regardless of amount, as it is a small part. (2) The view in al-Hidayah: one calculates the proportion of the mustache relative to a quarter of the beard, and gives charity accordingly. (3) Blood is due according to some, because shaving the mustache is a deliberate act resembling shaving for cupping. The author then clarifies that the view from al-Hidayah that cutting is sunnah is a refutation of al-Tahawi who holds shaving as sunnah. He explains that 'taking' is more general, and the hadith 'Trim the mustaches' (ahfu al-shawarib) means hyperbole in cutting, which can be achieved by shaving or cutting. The sunnah is to remove excess hair, and shaving is just easier. The passage ends by refuting al-Bada'i' that the sunnah is only cutting, asserting that any method achieving the goal is acceptable. The obligation for a Muhrim is charity for removing less than a quarter of the beard (including mustache), and blood for more, unless the removal is for a specific need like cupping.

Key Terms
حكومة عدل (hukumat 'adl): A just assessment of the value of what is removed, used to determine the penalty for cutting hair in Ihram.
صدقة (sadaqah): A specified charity (food) given by a Muhrim for violating the prohibition of removing hair.
دم (dam): A blood sacrifice (e.g., a sheep) due for major violations of Ihram, such as removing a significant amount of hair.
إطار (itar): The rim or meeting point of the skin and flesh of the lip; used to describe the proper trim length of the mustache.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi position (madhhab), what is the penalty for a Muhrim who shaves his entire mustache?
A) Blood (dam) is required.
B) Charity (sadaqah) is required.
C) No penalty because it is a small amount.
D) Proportional charity based on a quarter of the beard.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi for a Muhrim who shaves his mustache is the obligation of charity, as the mustache is a small part of the beard.

Penalty for Muhrim Trimming Mustache or Nails: Food Obligation
Explaining that a Muhrim who trims mustache or nails must give food (charity)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a Muhrim who trims his mustache or nails, identify the proof (dalil), and explain why charity (food) is due instead of blood.

Core Idea
A Muhrim who trims mustache or nails must give food, not blood — it's a minor benefit requiring minor compensation.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq, the author clarifies the penalty for a Muhrim who performs two minor grooming acts: trimming the mustache or cutting the nails. While many assume that any prohibited act in Ihram requires blood (dam), the Hanafi school distinguishes major and minor violations. Here, because the benefit is limited, only charity (food) is wajib. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof from the hadith, and the sunnah of trimming the mustache.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on a Muhrim who shaves (or cuts) his mustache or trims his nails. The ruling is wajib food (charity), not blood.
The text uses 'shaves' but the later discussion clarifies that the sunnah is cutting, not shaving.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith 'Ahfu al-shawarib…' (Trim the mustaches…) is the primary evidence. The penalty analogy is based on the minor nature of the act.
The hadith is from Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'ahfu' indicates an obligation to trim, but not necessarily shave. The penalty for a Muhrim is derived by qiyas to other minor prohibitions, such as clipping nails.
The text mentions that the act is a 'minor benefit' (irtifaq qasir).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is no cross-madhhab dispute on the penalty being charity. However, within Hanafi, there is a difference on whether the sibalan (ends of the mustache) should be cut or left. The stronger view is to cut them to avoid resemblance to Magians.
The passage cites Ibn Hibban's narration.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is charity, supported by the majority of early Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) and texts like al-Hidayah.
Some later scholars emphasized cutting (qass) as sunnah, but the penalty remains charity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي شارب حلال أو قلم أظفاره طعام وقص أظفار يديه ورجليه بمجلس أو يداً أو 19 قوله : ( وفي شارب حلال أو قلم أظفاره طعام) أي يجب طعام على محرم حلال أو قلم أظفاره لأن إزالته عن غيره ارتفاق لكنه قاصر فوجبت الصدقة أو لأنه أزال الأمن عن الشعر المستحق له ثم المصنف تبع صاحب الهداية في جمعه بين الشارب وتقليم الأظفار في وجوب الطعام ولم يذكر الصدقة، وقد تعبقه في غاية البيان بأنه إن أراد بالطعام قول أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف ومحمد والمذهب عند المتأخرين من مشايخنا أن السنة القص ا هـ. كذا في الفتح قوله : ( لأن الحلق أخذ قال في الفتح والذي ليس أخذاً هو النتف قوله: (وهو المبالغة في القطع) قال نوح أفندي : والمراد بالإحفاء هنا قطع ما طال على الشفتين حتى تبدو الشفة العليا لا القص من أصله، فالمعنى بالغوا في قص ما طال من الشوارب حتى يبين طرف الشفة العليا بياناً ظاهراً. ويستحب الابتداء بقص الجهة اليمنى من الشارب، واختلفوا هل يقص طرفاه أيضاً وهما المسميان بالسبالين أم يتركهما كما يفعله كثير من الناس؟ قيل لا بأس بترك سباليه فعل ذلك عمر وغيره، وقيل كره بقاء السبال لما فيه من التشبه بالأعاجم بل بالمجوس وأهل الكتاب وهذا أولى بالصواب لما رواه ابن حبان في صحيحه من حديث ابن عمر قال : ذكر لرسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم المجوس فقال : إنهم يوفرون سبالهم ويحلقون لحاهم فخالفوهم، فكان ابن عمر يجز كما تجز الشاة أو البعير . في شرح البخاري : وأما الشاري فهو الشعر النابت على الشفة العليا، واختلف في جانبيه وهما السبالان فقيل هما من الشارب فيشرع قصهما معه، وقيل هما من جملة شعر ا هـ. فعلى هذا يحمل ما روي عن عمر إن ثبت أنه كان يذهب إلى الثاني والله تعالى أعلم ا هـ قوله : قال الحافظ بن حجر (وإعفاء اللحية تركها الخ ) قال في غاية البيان: اختلف الناس في إعفاء اللحى ما هو فقال بعضهم تركها حتى تطول فذاك إعفاؤها من غير قص ولا قصر وقال :أصحانبا : الإعفاء تركها حتى تكث
And regarding a Muhrim who shaves his mustache or trims his nails, (he must give) food. And (he) cut the nails of his hands and feet in one sitting, or a hand or... His statement: 'And regarding a Muhrim who shaves his mustache or trims his nails, (he must give) food' means that food is obligatory for a Muhrim who shaves or trims his nails, because removing it from another is a benefit but it is minor, so charity is obligatory, or because he removed the protection of the hair he was entitled to. Then the author followed the author of al-Hidayah in combining the mustache and nail trimming in the obligation of food, and he did not mention charity. And he (the commentator) followed up in Ghayat al-Bayan that if he meant by 'food' the saying of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad, and the madhhab among our later scholars is that the sunnah is cutting. End quote. This is in al-Fath. His statement: 'Because shaving is a taking. It is said in al-Fath: That which is not a taking is plucking.' His statement: 'And it is hyperbole in cutting.' Nuh Afandi said: The meaning of 'ihfa'' here is cutting what is long on the lips until the upper lip appears, not cutting it from the root. So the meaning is: exaggerate in cutting what is long of the mustaches until the edge of the upper lip is clearly visible. And it is recommended to start with the right side of the mustache. They differed: should he also cut the two ends, called the sibalan, or leave them as many people do? It is said there is no harm in leaving the sibalan; 'Umar and others did that. And it is said that it is disliked to keep the sibal because it resembles the non-Arabs, indeed the Magians and the People of the Book. And this is more correct, based on what Ibn Hibban narrated in his Sahih from Ibn 'Umar: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was mentioned the Magians, and he said: 'They grow their sibal and shave their beards, so oppose them.' So Ibn 'Umar used to cut as a sheep or a camel is cut. In Sharh al-Bukhari: As for the shar (mustache), it is the hair that grows on the upper lip. They differed about its two sides, which are the sibalan: some say they are part of the mustache, so cutting them is prescribed along with it. Others say they are part of the hair (of the beard). End quote. Upon this is based what is reported from 'Umar, if it is confirmed that he held the second view. And Allah knows best. His statement: Al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar said: 'And letting the beard grow means leaving it.' He said in Ghayat al-Bayan: People differed about what 'letting the beard grow' means. Some said: leaving it until it grows long, that is letting it grow without cutting or shortening. Our companions said: letting it grow means leaving it until it becomes thick.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses the ruling for a Muhrim who trims his mustache or cuts his nails. The author explains that the obligation is food (charity), not blood. The reasoning: removing hair or nails is a minor benefit, so only a small compensation (sadaqah) is required. The text then discusses the sunnah of trimming the mustache and nails in general. It clarifies the meaning of 'ihfa'' (trimming) from the hadith: one should cut the hair that covers the upper lip, not remove it entirely. It is recommended to start on the right side. There is a difference of opinion about the two ends (sibalan): some say they are part of the mustache and should be trimmed; others say they are part of the beard and should be left. The stronger view is to trim them because it avoids resemblance to Magians. Then the passage discusses 'letting the beard grow' (i'fa' al-lihyah). It explains that the sunnah is to let the beard become thick and long, but not beyond a handful according to some scholars. The hadith 'Trim the mustaches and let the beards grow' is cited as evidence.

Key Terms
إحفاء (ihfa'): Trimming the mustache so that the upper lip becomes visible; hyperbole in cutting.
سبال (sibalan (dual: sibalan)): The two ends of the mustache that hang down on the sides of the mouth.
إعفاء (i'fa'): Letting the beard grow without cutting or trimming; allowing it to become thick and long.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the Hanafi madhhab, what is the penalty for a Muhrim who trims his fingernails?
A) Blood (dam)
B) Food (charity)
C) No penalty if done unintentionally
D) It is not allowed at all

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prescribes charity (food) for a Muhrim's minor acts like trimming mustache or nails, distinguishing them from major violations requiring blood.

The Sunnah of Mustache and Beard: Clipping vs Shaving
Commentary on sunnah of mustache and beard

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the sunnah of mustache and beard, explain the evidence from the hadith 'Ahfu al-shawarib wa a'fu al-liha', and distinguish the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding clipping versus shaving.

Core Idea
The Hanafi sunnah is to clip the mustache and let the beard grow; shaving is permissible but not the preferred practice.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explores the sunnah of grooming, focusing on the mustache and beard. While the immediate context is a ruling for a muhrim, the commentator expands to clarify the proper Islamic practice. You will learn the evidence from the hadith and the Hanafi school's preferred interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage discusses the sunnah for mustache (clipping) and beard (letting grow). Determine the hukm level: it is sunnah muakkadah.
The ruling is derived from the hadith; it's a confirmed practice, not obligatory.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The key evidence is the hadith from al-Sahihayn: 'Ahfu al-shawarib wa a'fu al-liha'. Understand the meaning of 'ihfa'' and 'i'fa''.
The commentator argues 'ihfa'' means exaggeration in cutting, not shaving from the root.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The word 'ihfa'' is from 'hafw' meaning to trim closely. The commentator interprets it as clipping to make the upper lip visible, not shaving completely.
This interpretation supports the sunnah of clipping over shaving.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
There is a difference within the Hanafi school: al-Tahawi held shaving is better; the majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) say clipping is sunnah.
The later scholars (mufta bihi) adopt clipping as sunnah, but shaving is permissible.
5
Apply the ruling to beard
The hadith also commands letting the beard grow. The Hanafi position is to let it grow and trim only what exceeds a fistful.
This is based on practice of the Companions and later scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کتاب الحج باب الجنايات
وفي شارب حلال أو قلم أظفاره طعام وقص أظفار يديه ورجليه بمجلس أو يداً أو
۱۹
وليس كما ظن لأن محمداً لم يقصد هنا بيان السنة وإنما قصد بيان حكم هذه الجناية بإزالة الشعر بأي طريق كان ولهذا ذكر الحلق في الإبط واختار في الهداية سنية النتف لا الحلق ولأن الأخذ أعم من الحلق لأن الحلق أخذ وليس القص متبادراً من الأخذ والوارد في الصحيحين «أحفوا الشوارب واعفوا اللحى»(۱) وهو المبالغة في القطع، فبأي شيء حصل حصل المقصود غير أنه بالحلق بالموسى أيسر منه بالقصة فلذا قال الطحاوي: الحلق أحسن من القص وقد يكون مثله بسبب بعض الآلات الخاصة بقص الشارب، وأما ذكر القص في بعض الأحاديث فالمراد منه المبالغة في الاستئصال وبما قررناه اندفع ما في البدائع من أن الصحيح أن السنة فيه القص وإعفاء اللحية تركها حتى تكث وتكثر والسنة قدر القبضة فما زاد قطعه .
أخذ شارب
قوله : ( وفي شارب حلال أو قلم أظفاره طعام) أي يجب طعام على محرم حلال أو قلم أظفاره لأن إزالته عن غيره ارتفاق لكنه قاصر فوجبت الصدقة أو لأنه أزال الأمن عن الشعر المستحق له ثم المصنف تبع صاحب الهداية في جمعه بين الشارب وتقليم الأظفار في وجوب الطعام ولم يذكر الصدقة، وقد تعبقه في غاية البيان بأنه إن أراد بالطعام
قول أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف ومحمد والمذهب عند المتأخرين من مشايخنا أن السنة القص ا هـ. كذا في الفتح قوله : ( لأن الحلق أخذ قال في الفتح والذي ليس أخذاً هو النتف قوله: (وهو المبالغة في القطع) قال نوح أفندي : والمراد بالإحفاء هنا قطع ما طال على الشفتين حتى تبدو الشفة العليا لا القص من أصله، فالمعنى بالغوا في قص ما طال من الشوارب حتى يبين طرف الشفة العليا بياناً ظاهراً. ويستحب الابتداء بقص الجهة اليمنى من الشارب، واختلفوا هل يقص طرفاه أيضاً وهما المسميان بالسبالين أم يتركهما كما يفعله كثير من الناس؟ قيل لا بأس بترك سباليه فعل ذلك عمر وغيره، وقيل كره بقاء السبال لما فيه من التشبه بالأعاجم بل بالمجوس وأهل الكتاب وهذا أولى بالصواب لما رواه ابن حبان في صحيحه من حديث ابن عمر قال : ذكر لرسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم المجوس فقال : إنهم يوفرون سبالهم ويحلقون لحاهم فخالفوهم، فكان ابن عمر يجز كما تجز الشاة أو البعير . في شرح البخاري : وأما الشاري فهو الشعر النابت على الشفة العليا، واختلف في جانبيه وهما السبالان فقيل هما من الشارب فيشرع قصهما معه، وقيل هما من جملة شعر ا هـ. فعلى هذا يحمل ما روي عن عمر إن ثبت أنه كان يذهب إلى الثاني والله تعالى أعلم ا هـ قوله :

Book of Hajj, Chapter of Offenses
And regarding a mustache of a halal [person] or trimming his nails: food. And cutting nails of his hands and feet in one sitting, or a hand or a foot...
19
And it is not as he thought, because Muhammad did not intend here to explain the sunnah, but rather intended to explain the ruling of this offense of removing hair by any means. For this reason he mentioned shaving in the armpit, and in al-Hidayah he chose the sunnah of plucking, not shaving. And because 'taking' is more general than shaving, since shaving is a type of taking, and cutting is not immediately understood from 'taking'. And what is found in the two Sahihs: 'Trim the mustaches and let the beards grow' (1), which means exaggeration in cutting. So whatever means achieves the objective, except that shaving with a razor is easier than with scissors, hence al-Tahawi said: Shaving is better than cutting, and it may be equivalent due to some special instruments for cutting the mustache. As for mentioning 'cutting' in some hadiths, what is meant is exaggeration in removal. With what we have established, what is in al-Bada'i' is refuted, namely that the correct view is that the sunnah is cutting. And letting the beard grow means leaving it until it becomes thick and abundant, and the sunnah is [to cut] a fistful, so whatever exceeds that should be cut.
Taking a mustache
His statement: (And regarding a mustache of a halal [person] or trimming his nails: food) meaning that a muhrim must give food for [shaving] a halal [person's] mustache or trimming his nails, because removing it from someone else is a benefit but it is deficient, so charity is obligatory, or because he removed the security from the hair that is due to him. Then the author follows the author of al-Hidayah in combining mustache and nail trimming in the obligation of food, and did not mention charity. And he [the commentator] criticized this in Ghayat al-Bayan: if by 'food' he meant...
The statement of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad, and the school according to the later scholars of our shaykhs is that the sunnah is cutting. End quote in al-Fath.
His statement: (because shaving is taking). He said in al-Fath: That which is not taking is plucking.
His statement: (And it is exaggeration in cutting). Nuh Afandi said: What is meant by 'trimming' here is cutting what is long on the lips until the upper lip becomes visible, not cutting from the root. So the meaning is: exaggerate in cutting what is long of the mustaches until the edge of the upper lip becomes clearly visible. It is recommended to start with cutting the right side of the mustache. And they differed: should he also cut its two ends, which are called the 'sibalan', or leave them as many people do? It was said: there is no harm in leaving his sibalan; 'Umar and others did that. It was said: it is disliked to leave the sibal because it resembles the non-Arabs, nay the Magians and the People of the Book. This is more correct because of what Ibn Hibban narrated in his Sahih from Ibn 'Umar: The Messenger of Allah was mentioned the Magians and he said: 'They let their sibal grow and shave their beards, so oppose them.' So Ibn 'Umar used to trim as a sheep or a camel is trimmed.
In Sharh al-Bukhari: As for the mustache, it is the hair that grows on the upper lip. They differed concerning its two sides, which are the sibalan. It was said: they are part of the mustache, so it is legislated to cut them with it. It was said: they are part of the hair. End quote. Based on this, what is narrated from 'Umar, if it is confirmed, is that he held the second view. And Allah knows best. End quote.
His statement:
Al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar said: the beard... becomes thick.
(And letting the beard grow means leaving it etc.). He said in Ghayat al-Bayan: People differed concerning what is 'letting the beard grow'. Some said: leaving it until it becomes long, that is its letting grow without cutting or shortening. And our companions said: letting grow means leaving it until...
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, specifically the ruling for a muhrim (person in ihram) who shaves the mustache of a halal (non-muhrim) person or cuts his nails. The matn states that such an act requires 'food' (طعم) as expiation. The commentator, Zayn al-Din ibn Nujaym (author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq), explains that this is because removing hair from another is a benefit (irtifaq) but of a lower degree, so charity (sadaqah) is required; alternatively, because the muhrim removes the protection of the hair that is due to the other person. The author of al-Hidayah combined both mustache and nails in the obligation of food, but the commentator notes a critique from Ghayat al-Bayan that the term 'food' could be ambiguous; however, the correct view (mufta bihi) is that for cutting nails of a halal person, the obligation is 'something' (shay'), not a fixed measure. The passage then digresses into the sunnah of the mustache and beard. Citing the hadith 'Trim the mustaches and let the beards grow' from al-Sahihayn, the commentator discusses whether the sunnah is to shave (halq) or clip (qass) the mustache. He argues that the command 'ihfa'' (trimming) means exaggeration in cutting, not necessarily shaving. The preferred view (according to later Hanafi scholars) is that the sunnah is to clip (qass) the mustache, not shave, because shaving is more extreme and the hadith emphasizes removal by any means. For the beard, the sunnah is to let it grow and only trim what exceeds a fistful. The commentator also addresses the issue of the sibalan (the ends of the mustache) and concludes it is better to trim them to avoid resemblance to non-Muslims. This passage is important for understanding both the penalty for a muhrim and the general sunnah of grooming.

Key Terms
شارب (shārib): Mustache: the hair growing on the upper lip.
إحفاء (iḥfā'): Trimming closely: to cut the mustache so that the upper lip becomes visible.
إعفاء اللحية (i‘fā' al-liḥyah): Letting the beard grow: leaving it without cutting or shortening.
سبال (sibāl): The two ends of the mustache that hang down on the sides of the mouth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Shaving it completely with a razor
B) Clipping it so the upper lip is visible
C) Plucking it out
D) Leaving it to grow freely

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi sunnah is to clip the mustache and let the beard grow; shaving the mustache is permissible but not the preferred practice.

The Ruling on Cutting Nails in Ihram: Dam or Sadaqah
Clarifies the ruling on cutting nails in ihram and the condition of majlis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the expiation required for a muhrim who cuts nails, and apply the condition of unity of sitting.

Core Idea
Cutting all nails in one sitting requires a dam; less than a full hand or foot requires per-nail sadaqah.

In ihram, the muhrim is prohibited from cutting nails. The penalty varies based on the extent and manner of cutting. This lesson clarifies the rulings derived from the Hanafi school, focusing on when a blood sacrifice (dam) is required versus charity (sadaqah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its prohibition
Recognize that cutting nails is a prohibited act (mahzur) in ihram because it removes something that grows from the body, akin to shaving.
The prohibition applies to both the muhrim cutting his own nails or those of another muhrim.
2
Classify the amount cut
Determine if the cutting constitutes a complete benefit (all nails in one sitting, or a full hand/foot) or partial (less than a full hand/foot). Complete benefit requires a dam; partial requires sadaqah per nail.
The text states: 'If he trims them all, it is a complete benefit, and similarly if he trims a hand or a foot.'
3
Apply the condition of unity of sitting
If nails are cut in multiple sittings, each sitting that trims a limb triggers a separate dam for that limb, because the expiation does not overlap across different sittings.
This is analogous to the prostration verse in Quran 4:43, where unity of sitting is considered.
4
Distinguish the type of expiation
The expiation for cutting nails is legislated to compensate for deficiency, unlike expiation for breaking fast which is for deterrence. Hence, it does not multiply across sittings unless the sittings are separate.
This distinction affects whether multiple expiations are due.

Source Text

وإن أراد به الصدقة التي هي نصف صاع التي هي المراد عند إطلاقهم الصدقة في هذا الباب فلا أيضاً لأن المحرم إذا حلق شاربه وجبت عليه الصدقة، فإذا حلق شارب غيره أطعم ما شاء كسرة خبز أو كفاً من طعام لقصور الجناية، وقد وقع التعبير بإطعام شيء وجوباً للمسألتين في الجامع الصغير لكنه أتى بـ من التبعيضية في تقليم الأظفار فقال في المحرم يأخذ من شارب الحلال أو يقص من أظفاره يطعم ما شاء، فسلم من الاعتراض فيكون المراد بما شاء العموم ا هـ . وأشار في فتح القدير إلى جوابه بأن المنقول في الأصل وكافي الحاكم أن المحرم إذا حلق رأس حلال تصدق بشيء، وإذا حلق رأس محرم فعليه صدقة، وأن الجواب في الأظفار كالجواب في الحلق ا هـ . فقوله في غاية البيان أن المحرم إذا قص أظافير حلال وجبت عليه الصدقة المعينة نصاً معارض بالمنصوص عليه في ظاهر الرواية من التصدق بشيء وهو يعم القليل والكثير بدليل مقابلته بما إذا حلق رأس محرم ، فحينئذ المراد بالطعام في عبارة الهداية ما القليل والكثير وهو صحيح بالنسبة إلى الشارب والأظفار كلها. وبهذا علم التقييد بالحلال ليخرج ما إذا قص المحرم أظافير محرم آخر فإنه يجب عليه الصدقة المعينة، وظاهر ما في غاية البيان يقتضي أنه إذا حلق شارب غيره محرماً كان أو حلالاً فإنه يطعم ما شاء، فليس الحلال قيداً بالنسبة إلى الشارب كما لا يخفى وعلم أيضاً أن قوله فيما مضى «كالحالق فيه اشتباه بالنسبة إلى المحلوق رأسه فإنه إن كان محرماً فالتشبيه تام، وإن كان حلالاً لأن الواجب إطعام شيء لا الصدقة المعينة. فلا يتم يعم أن قوله : (أو قص أظفار يديه ورجليه بمجلس أو يداً أو رجلاً وإلا تصدق كخمسة متفرقة) معطوف على «طيب أول الباب فيلزمه دم بالقص لأنه من المحظورات لما فيه من قضاء التفث وإزالة ما ينمو من البدن، فإذا قلمها كلها فهو ارتفاق كامل، وكذا إذا قص يداً أو رجلاً إقامة للربع مقام الكل كما في الحلق، وإن لم يقص يداً كاملة ولا رجلاً كاملة فعليه صدقة لتقاصر الجناية. قيد بالمجلس لأنه لو قص الكل في مجالس في كل مجلس عضو لزمه أربعة دماء لأن الغالب في هذه الكفارة معنى العبادة فيتقيد التداخل باتحاد المجلس كما في آية السجدة، سواء كفر للأولى أو لا، وفي الأول خلاف محمد. [وفيد بكون المحل مختلفاً لأنه لو كان متحداً كما إذا حلق الرأس في أربع مرات فإنه لا تتعدد الكفارة اتفاقاً اتحد المجلس أو اختلف. وفيد بكونها كفارة في الإحرام لأن كفارة الفطر في رمضان كما إذا أفسد أياماً من رمضان تتعدد إن كفر للأول وإن لم يكفر فكفارة واحدة اتفاقاً لأنها شرعت للزجر، فالغالب فيها معنى العقوبة وهذه شرعت لجبر النقصان.] وفي قوله وإلا تصدق اشتباه لأنه يقتضي أن يلزمه صدقة واحدة فيما إذا لم يقص يداً كاملة أو رجلاً كاملة وليس كذلك، بل يلزمه لكل ظفر قصه نصف صاع من بر حتى لو قص ستة عشر ظفراً من كل عضو أربعة فعليه لكل ظفر طعام مسكين إلا أن يبلغ ذلك دماً فحينئذ ينقص ما شاء. كذا في المبسوط. وإنما صرح بالخمسة المتفرقة مع أنها فهمت مما ذكره لدفع قول محمد المنقول في المجمع أن الخمسة المتفرقة كطرف كامل فيجب فأفاد أن في كل ظفر من الخمسة صدقة كما قررناه
And if by 'sadaqah' is meant the half sa' that is intended when they use the word 'sadaqah' in this chapter, then also no, because if a muhrim shaves his own mustache, sadaqah is obligatory on him. If he shaves someone else's mustache, he feeds whatever he wishes, a piece of bread or a handful of food, due to the lesser nature of the offense. And the expression 'feeding something' has occurred as obligatory for both issues in al-Jami' al-Saghir, but he [the author] came with the partitive 'min' in the case of trimming nails, saying: 'The muhrim who takes from the mustache of a non-muhrim or trims from his nails feeds whatever he wishes.' So he is safe from the objection, and thus by 'whatever he wishes' is meant generality. End quote. And he [Ibn al-Humam?] indicated in Fath al-Qadir his answer: that what is transmitted in al-Asl and Kafi al-Hakim is that if a muhrim shaves the head of a non-muhrim, he gives charity of something; if he shaves the head of a muhrim, a fixed sadaqah is due on him; and that the answer regarding nails is the same as the answer regarding shaving. End quote. So his statement in Ghayat al-Bayan that if a muhrim trims the nails of a non-muhrim, a specific fixed sadaqah is due on him textually, is contradicted by what is transmitted in Zahir al-Riwayah of giving charity of something, which includes little and much, evidenced by its contrast with the case of shaving a muhrim's head. So then by 'food' in the expression of al-Hidayah is meant what includes little and much, and this is correct regarding the mustache and all nails. And by this is known the restriction to 'non-muhrim' to exclude the case where a muhrim trims the nails of another muhrim, for then the fixed specific sadaqah is due on him. And the apparent meaning of what is in Ghayat al-Bayan requires that if he shaves the mustache of another, whether muhrim or non-muhrim, he feeds whatever he wishes, so 'non-muhrim' is not a restriction regarding the mustache, as is not hidden. And it is also known that his statement earlier 'like the shaver' has ambiguity concerning the one whose head is shaved: if he is a muhrim, the analogy is complete; if he is a non-muhrim, because the obligation is feeding something, not the specific fixed sadaqah. So it is not complete. That his statement: (Or he trims the nails of his hands and feet in one sitting, or a hand or a foot, otherwise he gives sadaqah like five separate [nails]) is conjoined to 'perfume' at the beginning of the chapter, so a dam is incumbent on him by trimming because it is among the prohibited acts, since it involves removing excess and removing what grows from the body. So if he trims them all, it is a complete benefit, and similarly if he trims a hand or a foot, establishing a quarter in place of the whole, as in shaving. And if he does not trim a complete hand nor a complete foot, then sadaqah is due on him due to the lesser nature of the offense. He restricted it to 'one sitting' because if he trims all in multiple sittings, each sitting a limb, four dams are incumbent on him, because the predominant aspect in this expiation is worship, so overlap is restricted to unity of sitting, as in the verse of prostration, whether he has expiated for the first or not. And there is a difference of opinion of Muhammad in the first case. [And it is restricted to difference of location: if it is unified, as when he shaves the head in four times, then the expiation does not multiply by agreement, whether the sitting is unified or different. And it is restricted to expiation in ihram, because the expiation for breaking fast in Ramadan, as if he invalidates days of Ramadan, multiplies if he expiated for the first, and if not, one expiation by agreement, because it is legislated for deterrence, so the predominant aspect is punishment, while this is legislated to compensate for deficiency.] And in his statement 'otherwise he gives sadaqah' there is ambiguity, because it implies that a single sadaqah is due on him when he does not trim a complete hand nor a complete foot, but it is not so; rather, for every nail he trims, half a sa' of wheat is due on him, such that if he trims sixteen nails, four from each limb, then for each nail the food of a miskin is due, unless that reaches [the value of] a dam, in which case he reduces as he wishes. This is from al-Mabsut. And he only explicitly mentioned 'five separate' although it is understood from what he mentioned, to refute the statement of Muhammad transmitted in al-Majma' that five separate [nails] are like a complete limb, so a dam is obligatory. Thus he indicated that for each of the five nails, a sadaqah is due, as we have established.
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage is a complex commentary (sharh) discussing the rulings for a muhrim (pilgrim in ihram) who cuts his own or another's nails. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, Ibn Nujaym, is reconciling apparent contradictions in the text of al-Hidayah and other sources. The core issue is: when does cutting nails obligate a specified sadaqah (half sa' of grain) versus an unspecified 'something' (shay')? And when does it obligate a dam (blood sacrifice) versus a sadaqah? The passage clarifies that if a muhrim cuts all nails of hands and feet in one sitting, or a complete hand or foot, a dam is required because it constitutes a complete benefit (irtifaq kamil). If he cuts less than a complete hand or foot, then a sadaqah per nail (half sa') is due, not a single sadaqah for the whole. This is contrary to the apparent meaning of earlier statements. The passage also discusses the condition of 'one sitting' (majlis): if nails are cut in multiple sittings, each sitting a different limb, then multiple dams are required (one per limb) because the expiation for the acts of ihram is like worship and does not overlap across different sittings. There is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani) holds that cutting five separate nails (e.g., from different fingers) is like a complete limb (i.e., a hand), thus requiring a dam. The majority position (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is that each nail is separate, and only when a full hand or foot is cut does a dam become obligatory. The passage refutes Muhammad's view by explicitly mentioning 'five separate' to show that even five nails are not a complete limb. The commentary also distinguishes between cutting nails of another muhrim (fixed sadaqah) versus a non-muhrim (unspecified charity), and between acts in ihram versus acts like breaking fast in Ramadan, where the nature of expiation differs (punishment vs. compensation).

Key Terms
مجلس (majlis): A single sitting or session; acts performed in one continuum without interruption.
صدقة (sadaqah): A charitable payment; in this context, usually half a sa' of wheat per nail, but can be unspecified 'something' in some cases.
دم (dam): A blood sacrifice (usually a sheep or goat) required for certain violations of ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A muhrim trims all nails of his left hand (five nails) in one sitting. What is the expiation?
A) One dam, because it is a complete hand.
B) Five sadaqahs, one per nail.
C) One sadaqah for all five nails.
D) No expiation, because a hand is not a full limb.

Key Takeaway
The expiation for cutting nails in ihram depends on the extent: complete benefit (all nails in one sitting or a full hand/foot) requires a dam; partial requires per-nail sadaqah, with each nail counted separately.

The Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Do Five Separate Nails Equal a Full Hand?
Clarifies the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the threshold for dam when cutting nails.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the disagreement between Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad regarding five separate nails, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Five separate nails do not equal a complete hand; each requires a separate sadaqah, refuting Muhammad’s view of equivalence.

Within the Hanafi school, a subtle disagreement exists: does cutting five nails from different fingers constitute a complete hand, thereby requiring a dam? Imam Muhammad argued yes, but the majority disagreed. This lesson examines the proofs and the preferred position.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
When a muhrim cuts five separate nails (not forming a complete hand or foot), does it trigger a dam or multiple sadaqahs? The difference arises because five nails resemble the number of fingers on a hand.
The dispute is recorded in al-Majma' and quoted by al-Marghinani.
2
Present the majority view (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf)
Each nail is an independent offense; a sadaqah of half sa' is due per nail, regardless of number, unless a complete hand or foot (all five nails of that limb) is cut in one sitting. Five separate nails from different limbs do not constitute a complete hand.
The text explicitly states: 'otherwise he gives sadaqah like five separate', implying that even five nails are still separate.
3
Present Muhammad's view
Imam Muhammad considers five separate nails as equivalent to a complete limb (hand) by analogy (qiyas), because the number five resembles the fingers of a hand, and thus a dam is due.
This view is transmitted in al-Majma'.
4
Analyze the refutation
The Hanafi response is that the text's explicit mention of 'five separate' is intended to rebut Muhammad's analogy. The phrase shows that even five nails are not a complete limb unless they form a whole hand (i.e., all five nails of the same hand). The 'illa (effective cause) for dam is complete benefit, which is not achieved by scattered nails.
The commentator Ibn Nujaym explicitly says: 'He only explicitly mentioned five separate... to refute the statement of Muhammad.'
5
Determine the tarjih
The majority view (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is mufta bihi (relied upon for fatwa). Muhammad's view is considered weak (marjuh) because the Zahir al-Riwayah texts and the explicit wording of al-Hidayah support per-nail sadaqah.
The tarjih authority is Ibn Nujaym in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, following the majority of the madhhab.

وإن أراد به الصدقة التي هي نصف صاع التي هي المراد عند إطلاقهم الصدقة في هذا الباب فلا أيضاً لأن المحرم إذا حلق شاربه وجبت عليه الصدقة، فإذا حلق شارب غيره أطعم ما شاء كسرة خبز أو كفاً من طعام لقصور الجناية، وقد وقع التعبير بإطعام شيء وجوباً للمسألتين في الجامع الصغير لكنه أتى بـ من التبعيضية في تقليم الأظفار فقال في المحرم يأخذ من شارب الحلال أو يقص من أظفاره يطعم ما شاء، فسلم من الاعتراض فيكون المراد بما شاء العموم ا هـ . وأشار في فتح القدير إلى جوابه بأن المنقول في الأصل وكافي الحاكم أن المحرم إذا حلق رأس حلال تصدق بشيء، وإذا حلق رأس محرم فعليه صدقة، وأن الجواب في الأظفار كالجواب في الحلق ا هـ . فقوله في غاية البيان أن المحرم إذا قص أظافير حلال وجبت عليه الصدقة المعينة نصاً معارض بالمنصوص عليه في ظاهر الرواية من التصدق بشيء وهو يعم القليل والكثير بدليل مقابلته بما إذا حلق رأس محرم ، فحينئذ المراد بالطعام في عبارة الهداية ما القليل والكثير وهو صحيح بالنسبة إلى الشارب والأظفار كلها. وبهذا علم التقييد بالحلال ليخرج ما إذا قص المحرم أظافير محرم آخر فإنه يجب عليه الصدقة المعينة، وظاهر ما في غاية البيان يقتضي أنه إذا حلق شارب غيره محرماً كان أو حلالاً فإنه يطعم ما شاء، فليس الحلال قيداً بالنسبة إلى الشارب كما لا يخفى وعلم أيضاً أن قوله فيما مضى «كالحالق فيه اشتباه بالنسبة إلى المحلوق رأسه فإنه إن كان محرماً فالتشبيه تام، وإن كان حلالاً لأن الواجب إطعام شيء لا الصدقة المعينة. فلا يتم يعم أن قوله : (أو قص أظفار يديه ورجليه بمجلس أو يداً أو رجلاً وإلا تصدق كخمسة متفرقة) معطوف على «طيب أول الباب فيلزمه دم بالقص لأنه من المحظورات لما فيه من قضاء التفث وإزالة ما ينمو من البدن، فإذا قلمها كلها فهو ارتفاق كامل، وكذا إذا قص يداً أو رجلاً إقامة للربع مقام الكل كما في الحلق، وإن لم يقص يداً كاملة ولا رجلاً كاملة فعليه صدقة لتقاصر الجناية. قيد بالمجلس لأنه لو قص الكل في مجالس في كل مجلس عضو لزمه أربعة دماء لأن الغالب في هذه الكفارة معنى العبادة فيتقيد التداخل باتحاد المجلس كما في آية السجدة، سواء كفر للأولى أو لا، وفي الأول خلاف محمد. [وفيد بكون المحل مختلفاً لأنه لو كان متحداً كما إذا حلق الرأس في أربع مرات فإنه لا تتعدد الكفارة اتفاقاً اتحد المجلس أو اختلف. وفيد بكونها كفارة في الإحرام لأن كفارة الفطر في رمضان كما إذا أفسد أياماً من رمضان تتعدد إن كفر للأول وإن لم يكفر فكفارة واحدة اتفاقاً لأنها شرعت للزجر، فالغالب فيها معنى العقوبة وهذه شرعت لجبر النقصان.] وفي قوله وإلا تصدق اشتباه لأنه يقتضي أن يلزمه صدقة واحدة فيما إذا لم يقص يداً كاملة أو رجلاً كاملة وليس كذلك، بل يلزمه لكل ظفر قصه نصف صاع من بر حتى لو قص ستة عشر ظفراً من كل عضو أربعة فعليه لكل ظفر طعام مسكين إلا أن يبلغ ذلك دماً فحينئذ ينقص ما شاء. كذا في المبسوط. وإنما صرح بالخمسة المتفرقة مع أنها فهمت مما ذكره لدفع قول محمد المنقول في المجمع أن الخمسة المتفرقة كطرف كامل فيجب فأفاد أن في كل ظفر من الخمسة صدقة كما قررناه
And if by 'sadaqah' is meant the half sa' that is intended when they use the word 'sadaqah' in this chapter, then also no, because if a muhrim shaves his own mustache, sadaqah is obligatory on him. If he shaves someone else's mustache, he feeds whatever he wishes, a piece of bread or a handful of food, due to the lesser nature of the offense. And the expression 'feeding something' has occurred as obligatory for both issues in al-Jami' al-Saghir, but he [the author] came with the partitive 'min' in the case of trimming nails, saying: 'The muhrim who takes from the mustache of a non-muhrim or trims from his nails feeds whatever he wishes.' So he is safe from the objection, and thus by 'whatever he wishes' is meant generality. End quote. And he [Ibn al-Humam?] indicated in Fath al-Qadir his answer: that what is transmitted in al-Asl and Kafi al-Hakim is that if a muhrim shaves the head of a non-muhrim, he gives charity of something; if he shaves the head of a muhrim, a fixed sadaqah is due on him; and that the answer regarding nails is the same as the answer regarding shaving. End quote. So his statement in Ghayat al-Bayan that if a muhrim trims the nails of a non-muhrim, a specific fixed sadaqah is due on him textually, is contradicted by what is transmitted in Zahir al-Riwayah of giving charity of something, which includes little and much, evidenced by its contrast with the case of shaving a muhrim's head. So then by 'food' in the expression of al-Hidayah is meant what includes little and much, and this is correct regarding the mustache and all nails. And by this is known the restriction to 'non-muhrim' to exclude the case where a muhrim trims the nails of another muhrim, for then the fixed specific sadaqah is due on him. And the apparent meaning of what is in Ghayat al-Bayan requires that if he shaves the mustache of another, whether muhrim or non-muhrim, he feeds whatever he wishes, so 'non-muhrim' is not a restriction regarding the mustache, as is not hidden. And it is also known that his statement earlier 'like the shaver' has ambiguity concerning the one whose head is shaved: if he is a muhrim, the analogy is complete; if he is a non-muhrim, because the obligation is feeding something, not the specific fixed sadaqah. So it is not complete. That his statement: (Or he trims the nails of his hands and feet in one sitting, or a hand or a foot, otherwise he gives sadaqah like five separate [nails]) is conjoined to 'perfume' at the beginning of the chapter, so a dam is incumbent on him by trimming because it is among the prohibited acts, since it involves removing excess and removing what grows from the body. So if he trims them all, it is a complete benefit, and similarly if he trims a hand or a foot, establishing a quarter in place of the whole, as in shaving. And if he does not trim a complete hand nor a complete foot, then sadaqah is due on him due to the lesser nature of the offense. He restricted it to 'one sitting' because if he trims all in multiple sittings, each sitting a limb, four dams are incumbent on him, because the predominant aspect in this expiation is worship, so overlap is restricted to unity of sitting, as in the verse of prostration, whether he has expiated for the first or not. And there is a difference of opinion of Muhammad in the first case. [And it is restricted to difference of location: if it is unified, as when he shaves the head in four times, then the expiation does not multiply by agreement, whether the sitting is unified or different. And it is restricted to expiation in ihram, because the expiation for breaking fast in Ramadan, as if he invalidates days of Ramadan, multiplies if he expiated for the first, and if not, one expiation by agreement, because it is legislated for deterrence, so the predominant aspect is punishment, while this is legislated to compensate for deficiency.] And in his statement 'otherwise he gives sadaqah' there is ambiguity, because it implies that a single sadaqah is due on him when he does not trim a complete hand nor a complete foot, but it is not so; rather, for every nail he trims, half a sa' of wheat is due on him, such that if he trims sixteen nails, four from each limb, then for each nail the food of a miskin is due, unless that reaches [the value of] a dam, in which case he reduces as he wishes. This is from al-Mabsut. And he only explicitly mentioned 'five separate' although it is understood from what he mentioned, to refute the statement of Muhammad transmitted in al-Majma' that five separate [nails] are like a complete limb, so a dam is obligatory. Thus he indicated that for each of the five nails, a sadaqah is due, as we have established.
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage is a complex commentary (sharh) discussing the rulings for a muhrim (pilgrim in ihram) who cuts his own or another's nails. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, Ibn Nujaym, is reconciling apparent contradictions in the text of al-Hidayah and other sources. The core issue is: when does cutting nails obligate a specified sadaqah (half sa' of grain) versus an unspecified 'something' (shay')? And when does it obligate a dam (blood sacrifice) versus a sadaqah? The passage clarifies that if a muhrim cuts all nails of hands and feet in one sitting, or a complete hand or foot, a dam is required because it constitutes a complete benefit (irtifaq kamil). If he cuts less than a complete hand or foot, then a sadaqah per nail (half sa') is due, not a single sadaqah for the whole. This is contrary to the apparent meaning of earlier statements. The passage also discusses the condition of 'one sitting' (majlis): if nails are cut in multiple sittings, each sitting a different limb, then multiple dams are required (one per limb) because the expiation for the acts of ihram is like worship and does not overlap across different sittings. There is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani) holds that cutting five separate nails (e.g., from different fingers) is like a complete limb (i.e., a hand), thus requiring a dam. The majority position (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is that each nail is separate, and only when a full hand or foot is cut does a dam become obligatory. The passage refutes Muhammad's view by explicitly mentioning 'five separate' to show that even five nails are not a complete limb. The commentary also distinguishes between cutting nails of another muhrim (fixed sadaqah) versus a non-muhrim (unspecified charity), and between acts in ihram versus acts like breaking fast in Ramadan, where the nature of expiation differs (punishment vs. compensation).

Key Terms
خمسة متفرقة (khamsah mutafarriqah): Five separate nails cut from different fingers or toes, not forming a complete hand or foot.
صدقة (sadaqah): A charitable payment; in this context, half a sa' of wheat per nail.
دم (dam): A blood sacrifice (usually a sheep or goat) required for certain violations of ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi Hanafi position, if a muhrim cuts five nails from different fingers in one sitting, what is the expiation?
A) One dam, because five nails are like a complete hand.
B) Five sadaqahs, one per nail.
C) One sadaqah for all five nails.
D) No expiation, because the nails are not from a complete limb.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position holds that five separate nails do not equal a complete hand; each nail requires a separate sadaqah, and only a complete hand or foot requires a dam.

Penalty for Cutting Nails During Ihram: The Principle of Tadaakhul (Overlapping)
Ruling on cutting nails: full limb vs. partial in multiple sessions, with tadaakhul rules

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the penalty (dam or sadaqah) for cutting multiple nails during ihram by applying the rule of tadaakhul based on unity of majlis, and distinguish the compensatory nature of this kaffarah from the punitive kaffarah of Ramadan.

Core Idea
Cutting a full limb requires a blood penalty; each partial nail requires a separate sadaqah, but multiple cuts in one session overlap into a single penalty.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the penalty for a muḥrim who cuts his nails. The base ruling is straightforward: a complete hand or foot requires one blood penalty (dam), while each individual nail cut requires half a sa' of wheat (sadaqah). However, the commentary delves into the subtle rules of overlapping (tadaakhul) when multiple cuts occur, drawing an analogy with the prostration of recitation (sajdat al-tilawah). Understanding these rules is essential for correctly assessing the penalty in complex scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling for a full limb vs. partial
A muḥrim who cuts a complete hand or foot (all five nails of one limb) owes one dam. If he cuts fewer than five nails of a limb, each nail cut requires a separate sadaqah (half sa' of wheat).
The matn says: 'full hand/foot, otherwise he gives sadaqah like five separate' meaning each of five nails incurs sadaqah.
2
Distinguish the penalty category: compensatory vs. punitive
The nail-cutting penalty is compensatory (jābir al-nuqṣān) – it aims to make up for a deficiency in the act of worship. In contrast, the expiation for breaking Ramadan fast is punitive (zājir) – it deters by punishment. This difference affects the rule of overlapping.
Compensatory penalties follow the rule of sajdat al-tilawah (single prostration per sitting), while punitive penalties multiply even within one sitting unless atonement has been made.
3
Apply the principle of tadaakhul based on unity of majlis
If multiple cuts occur in a single sitting (majlis), they overlap into one penalty, analogous to multiple prostrations of recitation in one sitting requiring only one prostration. If cuts occur in different sittings, each requires its own penalty.
Unity of majlis is the key: same time and place without interruption.
4
Resolve the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding five separate nails
Imam Muhammad held that five nails from different limbs are equivalent to a complete limb, thus requiring one dam. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf maintain that each nail is independent. The relied-upon (muftā bihī) position is the latter.
The commentator explicitly refutes Muhammad's view by stating that each nail (even five separate) requires its own sadaqah.
5
Calculate the final penalty using the accumulation rule
Sum the sadaqahs from all nails. If the total value reaches the value of a dam (typically 5 sā' of wheat), the muḥrim may choose to give one dam instead of multiple sadaqahs. Otherwise, each nail's sadaqah must be given separately.
This is derived from the text: 'unless that amounts to a blood penalty, in which case he reduces as he wishes.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رجلاً وإلا تصدق كخمسة متفرقة قيد بالمجلس لأنه لو قص الكل في مجالس في كل مجلس عضو لزمه أربعة دماء لأن الغالب في هذه الكفارة معنى العبادة فيتقيد التداخل باتحاد المجلس كما في آية السجدة، سواء كفر للأولى أو لا، وفي الأول خلاف محمد. وقيد التداخل بكونه من جنس واحد لأنه لو قلم أظافير يده وحلق ربع رأسه وطيب عضواً فإنه يلزمه لكل جناية دم، سواء اتحد المجلس أو اختلف اتفاقاً . وقيد بكون المحل مختلفاً لأنه لو كان متحداً كما إذا حلق الرأس في أربع مرات فإنه لا تتعدد الكفارة اتفاقاً اتحد المجلس أو اختلف. وفيد بكونها كفارة في الإحرام لأن كفارة الفطر في رمضان كما إذا أفسد أياماً من رمضان تتعدد إن كفر للأول وإن لم يكفر فكفارة واحدة اتفاقاً لأنها شرعت للزجر، فالغالب فيها معنى العقوبة وهذه شرعت لجبر النقصان. وفي قوله وإلا تصدق اشتباه لأنه يقتضي أن يلزمه صدقة واحدة فيما إذا لم يقص يداً كاملة أو رجلاً كاملة وليس كذلك، بل يلزمه لكل ظفر قصه نصف صاع من بر حتى لو قص ستة عشر ظفراً من كل عضو أربعة فعليه لكل ظفر طعام مسكين إلا أن يبلغ ذلك دماً فحينئذ ينقص ما شاء. كذا في المبسوط. وإنما صرح بالخمسة المتفرقة مع أنها فهمت مما ذكره لدفع قول محمد المنقول في المجمع أن الخمسة المتفرقة كطرف كامل فيجب فأفاد أن في كل ظفر من الخمسة صدقة كما قررناه
A full hand/foot, otherwise he gives sadaqah like five separate [nails]. Constrained by the council: because if he cut all in councils, each council a limb, he owes four blood penalties because in this expiation the meaning of worship predominates, so overlapping is restricted to unity of council as in ayah al-sajdah, whether he makes atonement for the first or not. In the first there is a difference from Muhammad. Constrained: overlapping is by being of one type: if he cut his fingernails, shaved a quarter of his head, and perfumed a limb, he owes a blood penalty for each, whether the council is united or different, by agreement. Constrained by the place being different: if it is united, as when he shaved the head in four times, the expiation does not multiply, by agreement, whether the council is united or different. And constrained by it being an expiation in ihram: because the expiation of breaking fast in Ramadan, like when he corrupts days of Ramadan, multiplies if he atones for the first, and if not, then one expiation, by agreement, because it was legislated for deterrence, so the meaning of punishment predominates, while this expiation was legislated to compensate deficiency. In his saying 'otherwise he gives sadaqah' there is confusion: it implies that he owes one sadaqah when he did not cut a complete hand or foot, but it is not so; rather, he owes for each nail he cuts half a sa' of wheat, so if he cut sixteen nails, four from each limb, he owes for each nail the food of a poor person, unless that amounts to a blood penalty, in which case he reduces as he wishes. This is in al-Mabsut. And he explicitly mentioned five separate nails even though it is understood from what he mentioned, to refute the saying of Muhammad related in al-Majma' that five separate nails are like a complete limb, so it would be obligatory. He thus indicated that in each of the five nails there is sadaqah, as we have established.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling for cutting nails during ihram. The matn states that if a muḥrim cuts a full hand or foot (i.e., all five nails of one hand or foot), he must give a blood penalty (dam). If he cuts less than a full limb, he gives sadaqah for each nail, like five separate nails—meaning for each of the five nails he gives one sadaqah (half a sa' of wheat per nail). The commentary then discusses when multiple cuts in different sessions require multiple penalties. The key point is that the expiation for cutting nails is considered an act of worship aimed at compensating a deficiency, so it behaves like the prostration of recitation: if multiple acts are done in a single sitting (majlis), they overlap into one penalty; if done in different sitings, each requires its own penalty. This is contrasted with the expiation for breaking fast in Ramadan, which is punitive and thus multiplies regardless of sitings unless atonement has already been made for the first offense. The commentary also clarifies an ambiguity in the matn: the phrase 'otherwise give sadaqah like five separate' might be misunderstood as one sadaqah for all partial cuts, but the correct view is that each nail cut requires its own sadaqah. Only when the penalties accumulate to the value of a blood penalty, the muḥrim may choose to give a blood penalty instead. The commentary also notes an intra-Hanafi difference: Imam Muhammad considered five separate nails as equivalent to a full limb, so one blood penalty would be required for five nails from different limbs. The author rejects this, insisting that each nail is a separate offense when not from the same limb.

Key Terms
ظفر (zafar): Nail; specifically a fingernail or toenail cut during ihram.
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation; the penalty paid for violating a prohibition of ihram.
مجلس (majlis): A sitting or session; the unit of time/place in which acts are considered one occasion.
تداخل (tadaakhul): Overlapping; when multiple acts merge into a single penalty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a muḥrim cuts three nails from each hand in a single sitting, how many sadaqahs are due?
A) One sadaqah for all six nails
B) Six sadaqahs (half sa' per nail)
C) One blood penalty since total reaches a dam
D) No penalty since it's not a full limb

Key Takeaway
The penalty for cutting nails during ihram is per nail unless a complete limb is cut, but multiple cuts in a single session overlap into one penalty, following the principle for compensatory expiations.
